Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Ruling on Istinja' and Number of Stones
Ruling with proof on the number of stones in istinja'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istinja' (sunnah muakkadah) and explain why three stones are recommended but not obligatory, distinguishing the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Istinja' is sunnah muakkadah, not fard; the number three is recommended, not obligatory.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi school's position on istinja'—cleansing after relieving oneself. The text from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that istinja' is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation. It also addresses the common misconception that three stones are required, showing that they are merely recommended and that the purpose is thorough cleaning (inqa').

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling status of istinja'
Find the explicit statement that istinja' is sunnah muakkadah, not fard. Note the distinction with the Shafi'i school which considers it fard.
The Hanafi reliance on the principle that acts of purification are sunnah unless proven otherwise.
2
Analyze the evidence for the number of stones
Examine the hadith evidence cited: the Prophet's acceptance of two stones and discarding dung, and the sufficiency of a stone with three edges. Understand that the mention of three is customary or recommendatory.
The rebuttal to Ibn Hajar's criticism is addressed: the initial command for three stones does not make them obligatory when the purpose (inqa') is achieved with fewer.
3
Derive the Hanafi ruling
Conclude that the number of stones is not fixed; three is mustahabb, not fard. The condition for validity is achieving inqa', not the count.
The practical implication: one stone with three edges suffices, as does two stones.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school makes three stones obligatory based on the view that istinja' is fard. The Hanafi response is that the act itself is sunnah, so its components cannot be fard.
This is a classic example of a branch dispute stemming from a difference in the usul al-fiqh principle regarding the nature of ablution.

كتاب الطهارة - باب الانجاس

أن جهة تدل على وقوعه فإن دل دليل على التكرار عمل به وإلا فلا تقتضيه بوضعها، وقد قالت عائشة رضي الله عنها : كنت أطيب رسول الله ﷺ قبل أن يطوف، ومعلوم أنه لم يحج بعد صحبته عائشة إلا حجة واحدة وهي حجة الوداع فاستعملت كان في مرة واحدة، ولا يقال لعلها طيبته في إحرامه لأن المعتمر لا يحل له التطيب قبل الطواف بالإجماع فثبت أنها استعملت «كان» في مرة واحدة كما قال الأصوليون ذكره النووي في شرح مسلم من باب الوتر، واختاره المحقق في التحرير فإنه اختار أن إفادتها للتكرار من جهة الاستعمال لا من الوضع لكن الاستعمال مختلف كما رأيت. وقد علم مما ذكرنا أن التقييد بالإنقاء إنما هو لحصول السنة حتى لو لم ينق فإن السنة قد فاتت لا أنه قيد للجواز. وأطلق الخارج ولم يقيده بكونه معتاداً ليفيد أن غير المعتاد إذا أصاب المحل كالدم يطهر بالحجارة على الصحيح، سواء كان خارجاً منه أو لا، وليفيد أنه لا فرق بين أن يكون الغائط رطباً ولم يقم من موضعه أو قام من موضعه أو جف الغائط فإن الحجر كاف فيه وفي الثاني خلاف ذكره في السراج الوهاج . وأراد بنحو الحجر ما كان عيناً طاهرة مزيلة لا قيمة له كالمدر والتراب والعود والخرقة والقطن والجلد الممتهن، فخرج الزجاج والثلج والآجر والخزف والفحم.

قوله : (وما سن فيه عدد أي في الاستنجاء لما قدمنا من أن المقصود إنما هو الإنقاء، وشرط الشافعي الثلاث مبني على أن الاستنجاء فرض ولا نقول به وذكر الثلاث في بعض الأحاديث خرج مخرج العادة لأن الغالب حصول الإنقاء بها، أو يحمل على الاستحباب بدليل أنه لو استنجى بحجر له ثلاثة أحرف جاز عندهم، وبدليل أنه لما أتى له عليه الصلاة والسلام بحجرين وروثة ألقى الروثة واقتصر على الحجرين كذا ذكر أئمتنا وتعقبه شيخ الإسلام ابن حجر في فتح الباري بأن الأمر أولاً بإتيان ثلاثة أحجار يغني عن طلب ثالث بعد إلقاء الروثة، وبأنه ورد في بعض الروايات الصحيحة أنه طلب منه ثالثاً وأتى له به. وبما قررناه علم أن المراد نفي السنة المؤكدة وإلا فقد صرحوا بالاستحباب كما قدمناه. قوله: (وغسله بالماء أحب) أي غسل المحل بالماء أفضل لأنه قالع للنجاسة والحجر مخفف لها فكان الماء أولى. كذا ذكره الشارح الزيلعي وهو ظاهر في أن المحل لم يطهر بالحجر، ويتفرع عليه أنه السبيل باصابة الماء وفيه الخلاف المعروف في مسألة الأرض إذا جفت بعد التنجس ثم أصابها ماء وكذا في نظائرها وقد اختاروا في الجميع عدم عود النجاسة كما قدمناه عنهم فليكن كذلك هنا. ويدل على ذلك من السنة ما رواه الدارقطني وصححه عن أبي هريرة أنه نهى يتنجس
يستنجي بروث أو عظم وقال : إنهما لا يطهران. فعلم أن ما أطلق الاستنجاء به بطهر إذ لو لم يطهر لم يطلق الاستنجاء به بحكم هذه العلة. وفي فتح القدير: وأجمع المتأخرون أنه لا ينجس بالعرق حتى لو سال العرق منه وأصاب الثوب والبدن أكثر من قدر الدرهم لا يمنع، وظاهر ما في الكتاب يدل على أن الماء مندوب سواء كان قبله الحجر أو لا. فالحاصل أنه إذا اقتصر على الحجر كان مقيماً للسنة وإذا اقتصر على الماء كان مقيماً لها أيضاً وهو من الأول، وإذا جمع بينهما كان أفضل من الكل، وقيل الجمع سنة في زماننا، وقيل سنة على الإطلاق وهو الصحيح وعليه الفتوى كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي فتح القدير: هذا والنظر إلى ما تقدم أول الفصل من حديث أنس وعائشة يفيد أن الاستنجاء بالماء سنة مؤكدة في كل زمان لإفادته المواظبة وفيه ما قدمناه من البحث أطلق الغسل بالماء ولم يقيده بعدد ليفيد أن الصحيح تفويضه إلى رأيه فيغسل حتى يقع في قلبه أنه طهر. كذا في الخلاصة بعد نقل الخلاف، فمنهم من شرط الثلاث، ومنهم من شرط السبع، ومنهم من شرط العشرة . والمراد بالاشتراط الاشتراط في حصول السنة وإلا فترك الكل لا يضره عندهم كما قدمناه .. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان والاستنجاء بالماء أفضل إن أمكنه ذلك من غير كشف العورة، وإن احتاج إلى كشف العورة يستنجي بالحجر ولا يستنجي بالماء. قالوا : من كشف العورة للاستنجاء يصير فاسقاً. وفي فتح القدير : ولو كان على شط نهر ليس فيه سترة لو استنجى بالماء قالوا يفسق وكثيراً ما يفعله عوام المصريين في الميضأة فضلاً عن شاطئ النيل .اهـ. وقد قدمنا الكلام عليه أول الباب ..
The Book of Purification - Chapter of Impurities. That aspect indicates its occurrence; if evidence indicates repetition, it is acted upon, otherwise it does not require it by its coinage. Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) said: 'I used to perfume the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) before he would circumambulate.' It is known that he did not perform Hajj after his companionship with Aisha except one Hajj, the Farewell Hajj, so she used 'kana' for a single occasion. It cannot be said that perhaps she perfumed him during his ihram, because the performer of Umrah is not permitted to apply perfume before Tawaf by consensus. So it is established that she used 'kana' for a single occasion, as the usuliyyun said. Al-Nawawi mentioned it in Sharh Muslim, chapter of Witr. The muhaqqiq in al-Tahrir chose that its indication of repetition is from usage, not coinage, but usage varies as you have seen. It has been known from what we mentioned that the restriction to cleaning (inqa') is only for attainment of sunnah; so if he does not clean, the sunnah is lost, not that it is a condition for permissibility. And he left the exiting impurity unrestricted, not specifying it to be customary, to indicate that non-customary impurity (like blood) when it hits the place is purified by stones on the correct view, whether it exits from him or not; and to indicate that there is no difference between feces being wet and not having risen from his place, or having risen from his place, or the feces having dried, for the stone suffices. In the second there is a difference mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And by 'like stone' he means a pure removable substance that has no value, such as clods of earth, dust, wood, cloth, cotton, and worn-out leather. Thus glass, snow, brick, ceramic, and coal are excluded. His statement: 'and what is sunnah in it is number' meaning in istinja', because we have stated that the purpose is cleaning. Al-Shafi'i made three a condition based on his view that istinja' is obligatory, but we do not say that. The mention of three in some hadiths is taken as customary, because cleaning is usually achieved thereby, or interpreted as recommendatory, evidenced by the fact that if he cleans with a stone having three edges, it is permissible for them; and by the evidence that when two stones and dung were brought to the Prophet (peace be upon him), he threw away the dung and was content with the two stones, as our imams mentioned. Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani in Fath al-Bari criticized this, saying that the initial command to bring three stones dispenses with the need to seek a third after discarding the dung, and because it is reported in some authentic narrations that he asked for a third and it was brought. By what we have established, it is known that the intention is to negate the emphatic sunnah; otherwise they have explicitly stated recommendation as we have mentioned. His statement: 'and washing it with water is more beloved' meaning washing the place with water is better, because it removes the impurity, while the stone only mitigates it, so water is more appropriate. Al-Zayla'i mentioned it, and it is apparent that the place is not purified by the stone. This leads to the issue of the path being affected by water, regarding which there is the well-known dispute in the case of earth that becomes dry after being contaminated and then water hits it, and similar cases. They have chosen in all cases the non-return of impurity, as we have mentioned from them, so it should be the same here. Supporting that from the sunnah is what al-Daraqutni narrated and authenticated from Abu Huraira that he prohibited... he cleans himself with dung or bone, and said: 'They do not purify.' Thus it is known that what is called 'cleansing with it' purifies, because if it did not purify, it would not be called cleansing by virtue of this cause. In Fath al-Qadir: The later scholars have agreed that sweat does not become impure, such that if sweat flows from him and touches the garment and body more than the size of a dirham, it does not prevent. The apparent meaning of the book indicates that water is recommended (mandub), whether preceded by stone or not. So the conclusion is that if he confines himself to stone, he has fulfilled the sunnah; if he confines himself to water, he has also fulfilled it; and it is from the first. If he combines both, it is better than all. It is said that combining is sunnah in our time; it is said it is sunnah absolutely, which is correct and the fatwa is upon it, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. In Fath al-Qadir: This and the consideration of what preceded at the beginning of the chapter from the hadith of Anas and Aisha indicate that istinja' with water is an emphatic sunnah in every time, because it indicates constancy. And there is the research we mentioned. He left washing with water unrestricted, not specifying a number, to indicate that the correct view is to delegate it to his opinion; he washes until it occurs to his heart that it is pure, as in al-Khulasa after quoting the dispute. Some stipulated three, some seven, some ten. The intent of stipulation is stipulation for attainment of the sunnah; otherwise leaving it entirely does not harm him according to them, as we have mentioned. In Fatawa Qadikhan: Istinja' with water is better if he can do so without uncovering the private part; if he needs to uncover the private part, he cleans with stone and does not use water. They said: Whoever uncovers his private part for istinja' becomes a sinner. In Fath al-Qadir: If he is on a riverbank without a screen and he uses water, they said he becomes sinful. Many common Egyptians do that in the ablution place, let alone the Nile bank. End. We have discussed it at the beginning of the chapter.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of istinja' (cleansing after relieving oneself) using stones or similar solids. It addresses several key points:

1. **Repetition of 'kana'**: The author clarifies that the verb 'kana' (was/were) does not indicate repetition by itself; it can be used for a single event. Evidence is the hadith of Aisha who said she perfumed the Prophet before Tawaf during the Farewell Hajj, which was a single occurrence.

2. **Cleaning (inqa') and sunnah**: The condition of cleaning is for the attainment of the sunnah, not for the permissibility of the act. If one does not achieve cleaning, the sunnah is lost but the act (istinja') is still valid.

3. **Types of impurities and materials**: The stone (or similar solids) suffices for cleansing from any impurity, including non-customary ones like blood, whether it exits from the body or not. Materials like clods, dust, wood, cloth, cotton, and worn-out leather are valid; glass, snow, brick, ceramic, and coal are not.

4. **Number of stones**: The school of Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the number of stones is not obligatory; three stones mentioned in hadith are recommended (mustahabb) or customary. Evidence includes the Prophet accepting two stones and discarding dung, and a stone with three edges suffices. Al-Shafi'i made three obligatory because he considers istinja' a fard, but the Hanafi school does not.

5. **Preference of water**: Water is better ('ahabb/afdal) than stones because it removes impurity, while stones only mitigate. The Hanafi position is that water is sunnah, and combining both is the best. However, if one must uncover the private part to use water, it is better to use stones to avoid sin.

6. **Sweat**: According to later Hanafi consensus, sweat is not najis (impure), even if it exceeds a dirham in amount, and does not prevent prayer.

7. **Number of washes**: There is no fixed number for washing with water; one should wash until certain of purity. Stipulations of three, seven, or ten are only for attaining sunnah.

This commentary consistently follows the Hanafi school, distinguishing between obligatory (fard/wajib), sunnah, and mustahabb. The key takeaway is that istinja' with stones is sufficient for the sunnah, but water is superior, and the number of stones is not obligatory.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja'): Cleansing the private parts after relieving oneself using solid substances like stones or water.
الإنقاء (al-inqa'): Complete removal of impurity from the site of exit.
الأحجار (al-ahjar): Stones or similar solid, pure, removable substances used for istinja'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of using three stones for istinja'?
A) Obligatory (fard).
B) Recommended (mustahabb).
C) Forbidden (haram).
D) Invalid without three stones.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, istinja' is a confirmed sunnah, and the number of stones is not fixed; three is only recommended.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Preference of Water and Combining Stones and Water in Istinja'
Ruling with proof on the preference of water and the ruling on combining stones and water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that water is preferred over stones for istinja' in the Hanafi school, explain the superiority of combining both, and identify the exceptions when stones alone are better.

Core Idea
Water is better than stones, and combining both is the best practice, but if it leads to uncovering the awrah, stones alone are preferable.

This lesson continues the discussion on istinja' by focusing on the preference of water. The Hanafi school holds that water is superior because it removes impurity while stones only mitigate. Combining both achieves the highest level of sunnah. However, practical considerations such as avoiding uncovering the private part may make stones the better choice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling that water is 'ahabb' (more beloved)
Locate the statement in the text that washing with water is better (afdal) than stones. Understand the reason: water removes impurity, stone only mitigates.
This is a preference (tanzih) and not a requirement.
2
Understand the implication that the place is not purified by stone alone
Al-Zayla'i's commentary indicates that after using stone, the place is not fully pure; it requires water for complete purification. However, the Hanafi school holds that once water is used, impurity does not return, based on the analogy of dry earth.
This is a nuanced point: the stone serves to remove the bulk, but water achieves full purity.
3
Analyze the ruling on combining stones and water
The text states that using both is better than either alone. There is a difference of opinion whether combining is sunnah absolutely or only in later times. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that it is sunnah absolutely.
Evidence includes the hadith of Anas and Aisha indicating constancy in using water.
4
Examine the exception regarding uncovering the awrah
If using water requires uncovering the private part (e.g., at a riverbank without a screen), it is better to use stones to avoid sin. Fatawa Qadikhan and Fath al-Qadir stress that uncovering the awrah for istinja' is sinful.
This prioritizes the prohibition of exposing awrah over the preference for water.

كتاب الطهارة - باب الانجاس

أن جهة تدل على وقوعه فإن دل دليل على التكرار عمل به وإلا فلا تقتضيه بوضعها، وقد قالت عائشة رضي الله عنها : كنت أطيب رسول الله ﷺ قبل أن يطوف، ومعلوم أنه لم يحج بعد صحبته عائشة إلا حجة واحدة وهي حجة الوداع فاستعملت كان في مرة واحدة، ولا يقال لعلها طيبته في إحرامه لأن المعتمر لا يحل له التطيب قبل الطواف بالإجماع فثبت أنها استعملت «كان» في مرة واحدة كما قال الأصوليون ذكره النووي في شرح مسلم من باب الوتر، واختاره المحقق في التحرير فإنه اختار أن إفادتها للتكرار من جهة الاستعمال لا من الوضع لكن الاستعمال مختلف كما رأيت. وقد علم مما ذكرنا أن التقييد بالإنقاء إنما هو لحصول السنة حتى لو لم ينق فإن السنة قد فاتت لا أنه قيد للجواز. وأطلق الخارج ولم يقيده بكونه معتاداً ليفيد أن غير المعتاد إذا أصاب المحل كالدم يطهر بالحجارة على الصحيح، سواء كان خارجاً منه أو لا، وليفيد أنه لا فرق بين أن يكون الغائط رطباً ولم يقم من موضعه أو قام من موضعه أو جف الغائط فإن الحجر كاف فيه وفي الثاني خلاف ذكره في السراج الوهاج . وأراد بنحو الحجر ما كان عيناً طاهرة مزيلة لا قيمة له كالمدر والتراب والعود والخرقة والقطن والجلد الممتهن، فخرج الزجاج والثلج والآجر والخزف والفحم.

قوله : (وما سن فيه عدد أي في الاستنجاء لما قدمنا من أن المقصود إنما هو الإنقاء، وشرط الشافعي الثلاث مبني على أن الاستنجاء فرض ولا نقول به وذكر الثلاث في بعض الأحاديث خرج مخرج العادة لأن الغالب حصول الإنقاء بها، أو يحمل على الاستحباب بدليل أنه لو استنجى بحجر له ثلاثة أحرف جاز عندهم، وبدليل أنه لما أتى له عليه الصلاة والسلام بحجرين وروثة ألقى الروثة واقتصر على الحجرين كذا ذكر أئمتنا وتعقبه شيخ الإسلام ابن حجر في فتح الباري بأن الأمر أولاً بإتيان ثلاثة أحجار يغني عن طلب ثالث بعد إلقاء الروثة، وبأنه ورد في بعض الروايات الصحيحة أنه طلب منه ثالثاً وأتى له به. وبما قررناه علم أن المراد نفي السنة المؤكدة وإلا فقد صرحوا بالاستحباب كما قدمناه. قوله: (وغسله بالماء أحب) أي غسل المحل بالماء أفضل لأنه قالع للنجاسة والحجر مخفف لها فكان الماء أولى. كذا ذكره الشارح الزيلعي وهو ظاهر في أن المحل لم يطهر بالحجر، ويتفرع عليه أنه السبيل باصابة الماء وفيه الخلاف المعروف في مسألة الأرض إذا جفت بعد التنجس ثم أصابها ماء وكذا في نظائرها وقد اختاروا في الجميع عدم عود النجاسة كما قدمناه عنهم فليكن كذلك هنا. ويدل على ذلك من السنة ما رواه الدارقطني وصححه عن أبي هريرة أنه نهى يتنجس
يستنجي بروث أو عظم وقال : إنهما لا يطهران. فعلم أن ما أطلق الاستنجاء به بطهر إذ لو لم يطهر لم يطلق الاستنجاء به بحكم هذه العلة. وفي فتح القدير: وأجمع المتأخرون أنه لا ينجس بالعرق حتى لو سال العرق منه وأصاب الثوب والبدن أكثر من قدر الدرهم لا يمنع، وظاهر ما في الكتاب يدل على أن الماء مندوب سواء كان قبله الحجر أو لا. فالحاصل أنه إذا اقتصر على الحجر كان مقيماً للسنة وإذا اقتصر على الماء كان مقيماً لها أيضاً وهو من الأول، وإذا جمع بينهما كان أفضل من الكل، وقيل الجمع سنة في زماننا، وقيل سنة على الإطلاق وهو الصحيح وعليه الفتوى كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي فتح القدير: هذا والنظر إلى ما تقدم أول الفصل من حديث أنس وعائشة يفيد أن الاستنجاء بالماء سنة مؤكدة في كل زمان لإفادته المواظبة وفيه ما قدمناه من البحث أطلق الغسل بالماء ولم يقيده بعدد ليفيد أن الصحيح تفويضه إلى رأيه فيغسل حتى يقع في قلبه أنه طهر. كذا في الخلاصة بعد نقل الخلاف، فمنهم من شرط الثلاث، ومنهم من شرط السبع، ومنهم من شرط العشرة . والمراد بالاشتراط الاشتراط في حصول السنة وإلا فترك الكل لا يضره عندهم كما قدمناه .. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان والاستنجاء بالماء أفضل إن أمكنه ذلك من غير كشف العورة، وإن احتاج إلى كشف العورة يستنجي بالحجر ولا يستنجي بالماء. قالوا : من كشف العورة للاستنجاء يصير فاسقاً. وفي فتح القدير : ولو كان على شط نهر ليس فيه سترة لو استنجى بالماء قالوا يفسق وكثيراً ما يفعله عوام المصريين في الميضأة فضلاً عن شاطئ النيل .اهـ. وقد قدمنا الكلام عليه أول الباب ..
The Book of Purification - Chapter of Impurities. That aspect indicates its occurrence; if evidence indicates repetition, it is acted upon, otherwise it does not require it by its coinage. Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) said: 'I used to perfume the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) before he would circumambulate.' It is known that he did not perform Hajj after his companionship with Aisha except one Hajj, the Farewell Hajj, so she used 'kana' for a single occasion. It cannot be said that perhaps she perfumed him during his ihram, because the performer of Umrah is not permitted to apply perfume before Tawaf by consensus. So it is established that she used 'kana' for a single occasion, as the usuliyyun said. Al-Nawawi mentioned it in Sharh Muslim, chapter of Witr. The muhaqqiq in al-Tahrir chose that its indication of repetition is from usage, not coinage, but usage varies as you have seen. It has been known from what we mentioned that the restriction to cleaning (inqa') is only for attainment of sunnah; so if he does not clean, the sunnah is lost, not that it is a condition for permissibility. And he left the exiting impurity unrestricted, not specifying it to be customary, to indicate that non-customary impurity (like blood) when it hits the place is purified by stones on the correct view, whether it exits from him or not; and to indicate that there is no difference between feces being wet and not having risen from his place, or having risen from his place, or the feces having dried, for the stone suffices. In the second there is a difference mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And by 'like stone' he means a pure removable substance that has no value, such as clods of earth, dust, wood, cloth, cotton, and worn-out leather. Thus glass, snow, brick, ceramic, and coal are excluded. His statement: 'and what is sunnah in it is number' meaning in istinja', because we have stated that the purpose is cleaning. Al-Shafi'i made three a condition based on his view that istinja' is obligatory, but we do not say that. The mention of three in some hadiths is taken as customary, because cleaning is usually achieved thereby, or interpreted as recommendatory, evidenced by the fact that if he cleans with a stone having three edges, it is permissible for them; and by the evidence that when two stones and dung were brought to the Prophet (peace be upon him), he threw away the dung and was content with the two stones, as our imams mentioned. Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani in Fath al-Bari criticized this, saying that the initial command to bring three stones dispenses with the need to seek a third after discarding the dung, and because it is reported in some authentic narrations that he asked for a third and it was brought. By what we have established, it is known that the intention is to negate the emphatic sunnah; otherwise they have explicitly stated recommendation as we have mentioned. His statement: 'and washing it with water is more beloved' meaning washing the place with water is better, because it removes the impurity, while the stone only mitigates it, so water is more appropriate. Al-Zayla'i mentioned it, and it is apparent that the place is not purified by the stone. This leads to the issue of the path being affected by water, regarding which there is the well-known dispute in the case of earth that becomes dry after being contaminated and then water hits it, and similar cases. They have chosen in all cases the non-return of impurity, as we have mentioned from them, so it should be the same here. Supporting that from the sunnah is what al-Daraqutni narrated and authenticated from Abu Huraira that he prohibited... he cleans himself with dung or bone, and said: 'They do not purify.' Thus it is known that what is called 'cleansing with it' purifies, because if it did not purify, it would not be called cleansing by virtue of this cause. In Fath al-Qadir: The later scholars have agreed that sweat does not become impure, such that if sweat flows from him and touches the garment and body more than the size of a dirham, it does not prevent. The apparent meaning of the book indicates that water is recommended (mandub), whether preceded by stone or not. So the conclusion is that if he confines himself to stone, he has fulfilled the sunnah; if he confines himself to water, he has also fulfilled it; and it is from the first. If he combines both, it is better than all. It is said that combining is sunnah in our time; it is said it is sunnah absolutely, which is correct and the fatwa is upon it, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. In Fath al-Qadir: This and the consideration of what preceded at the beginning of the chapter from the hadith of Anas and Aisha indicate that istinja' with water is an emphatic sunnah in every time, because it indicates constancy. And there is the research we mentioned. He left washing with water unrestricted, not specifying a number, to indicate that the correct view is to delegate it to his opinion; he washes until it occurs to his heart that it is pure, as in al-Khulasa after quoting the dispute. Some stipulated three, some seven, some ten. The intent of stipulation is stipulation for attainment of the sunnah; otherwise leaving it entirely does not harm him according to them, as we have mentioned. In Fatawa Qadikhan: Istinja' with water is better if he can do so without uncovering the private part; if he needs to uncover the private part, he cleans with stone and does not use water. They said: Whoever uncovers his private part for istinja' becomes a sinner. In Fath al-Qadir: If he is on a riverbank without a screen and he uses water, they said he becomes sinful. Many common Egyptians do that in the ablution place, let alone the Nile bank. End. We have discussed it at the beginning of the chapter.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of istinja' (cleansing after relieving oneself) using stones or similar solids. It addresses several key points:

1. **Repetition of 'kana'**: The author clarifies that the verb 'kana' (was/were) does not indicate repetition by itself; it can be used for a single event. Evidence is the hadith of Aisha who said she perfumed the Prophet before Tawaf during the Farewell Hajj, which was a single occurrence.

2. **Cleaning (inqa') and sunnah**: The condition of cleaning is for the attainment of the sunnah, not for the permissibility of the act. If one does not achieve cleaning, the sunnah is lost but the act (istinja') is still valid.

3. **Types of impurities and materials**: The stone (or similar solids) suffices for cleansing from any impurity, including non-customary ones like blood, whether it exits from the body or not. Materials like clods, dust, wood, cloth, cotton, and worn-out leather are valid; glass, snow, brick, ceramic, and coal are not.

4. **Number of stones**: The school of Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the number of stones is not obligatory; three stones mentioned in hadith are recommended (mustahabb) or customary. Evidence includes the Prophet accepting two stones and discarding dung, and a stone with three edges suffices. Al-Shafi'i made three obligatory because he considers istinja' a fard, but the Hanafi school does not.

5. **Preference of water**: Water is better ('ahabb/afdal) than stones because it removes impurity, while stones only mitigate. The Hanafi position is that water is sunnah, and combining both is the best. However, if one must uncover the private part to use water, it is better to use stones to avoid sin.

6. **Sweat**: According to later Hanafi consensus, sweat is not najis (impure), even if it exceeds a dirham in amount, and does not prevent prayer.

7. **Number of washes**: There is no fixed number for washing with water; one should wash until certain of purity. Stipulations of three, seven, or ten are only for attaining sunnah.

This commentary consistently follows the Hanafi school, distinguishing between obligatory (fard/wajib), sunnah, and mustahabb. The key takeaway is that istinja' with stones is sufficient for the sunnah, but water is superior, and the number of stones is not obligatory.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja'): Cleansing the private parts after relieving oneself using solid substances like stones or water.
الماء (al-ma'): Pure water used for istinja'.
الغسل بالماء (al-ghusl bi al-ma'): Washing with water during istinja'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if someone uses only water for istinja' and does not use stones?
A) It is makruh tanzihi.
B) It fulfills the sunnah, but combining is better.
C) It is invalid because stones are required.
D) It is fard.

Key Takeaway
Water is the preferred medium for istinja'; combining stones and water is the most complete practice, but avoiding sin takes precedence.

When Water Becomes Obligatory: Impurity Exceeding the Exit
Ruling on water obligation when impurity spreads beyond the exit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that makes washing with water obligatory (fard) after relieving oneself, and distinguish between the ruling for the exit itself and the surrounding area.

Core Idea
Water becomes fard when impurity spreads beyond the exit; stones suffice only for the exit itself.

The Hanafi school makes a careful distinction between cleaning the private part itself (istinja') and cleaning the area around it. While using stones is a sunnah for the exit, once impurity spreads beyond that point, water becomes an absolute obligation. This lesson clarifies when water is required and what conditions trigger that obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Locate the matn statement 'And it is obligatory if the impurity exceeds the exit' and note that the commentary expands it to mean washing with water is fard.
The obligation is for ghusl (washing), not istinja'.
2
Understand the Condition
The condition for water to be obligatory is that the impurity (najasah) must have spread beyond the exit (makhraj) itself.
The exit is the specific area where istinja' with stones is sufficient.
3
Define 'Exceeding'
The commentary specifies that 'exceeding' means the impurity covers an area larger than a dirham (approx. 2.5 cm diameter).
This is the preventive amount (al-qadr al-mani') that invalidates prayer if left.
4
Recognize the Distinction
Understand that for the exit alone, istinja' with stones is sunnah. Once impurity exceeds, the ruling changes from sunnah to fard.
This is based on the text allowing stones for the exit, but analogy requiring water for spread.
5
Apply the Preventive Amount
The 'preventive amount' behind the istinja' site is considered; if impurity exceeds that, water is obligatory for the validity of prayer.
This is a practical measure for purity before salah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويجب إن جاوز النجس المخرج) أي ويجب غسل المحل بالماء إن تعدت النجاسة المخرج لأن للبدن حرارة جاذبة أجزاء النجاسة فلا يزيلها المسح بالحجر وهو القياس في محل الاستنجاء إلا أنه ترك فيه للنص على خلاف القياس فلا يتعداه وفسرنا فاعل يجب بالغسل دون الاستنجاء كما فعل الشارح الزيلعي لما أن غسل ما عدا المخرج لا استنجاء، ء، ولما أن الاستنجاء لا يكون إلا سنة وأراد بالماء هنا كل مائع طاهر مزيل بقرينة تصريحه من حمله على رواية محمد المعينة للماء كما أشار إليه في الكافي لأنها من ضعيفة في المذهب كما علمت سابقاً. وأراد بالمجاوز أن يكون أكثر من قدر الدرهم بقرينة ما بعده وحينئذ فالمراد بالوجوب الفرض قوله : ( ويعتبر القدر المانع وراء موضع الاستنجاء) أي
قدمنا أول الباب وهو يزول الغائط أولى . عن موضعه ويتجاوز مخرجه وبجفاقه لا يزيله الحجر فوجب الماء فيه اهـ. قوله : (يدل على أن الماء (مندوب فيه نظر بل فيه إيماء إلى أنه مسنون وأنى يكون المستحب أفضل من المسنون اهـ . أي لو كان الماء مندوباً كيف يكون أفضل من الحجر المسنون قوله : وكثيراً ما يفعله عوام المصلين)
His statement: 'And it is obligatory if the impurity exceeds the exit' meaning it is obligatory to wash the place with water if the impurity exceeds the exit, because the body has a heat that attracts parts of the impurity, so wiping with a stone does not remove it. This is the analogy for the place of istinja', except that it was left for the text contrary to analogy, so it is not extended beyond. And we explained the subject of 'obligatory' as washing (ghusl) not istinja', as al-Zayla'i did, because washing beyond the exit is not istinja', and istinja' is only sunnah. He intended by 'water' here every pure liquid that removes, based on his explicit statement of carrying it on Muhammad's narration specifying water, as indicated in al-Kafi, because it is weak in the school as you know earlier. And by 'exceeding' he means more than the size of a dirham, by evidence of what follows. Then the intended obligation is fard. His statement: 'And the preventive amount behind the place of istinja' is considered' – we presented at the beginning of the chapter that it is the removal of feces as a priority. From its place and exceeds its exit and its sides, the stone does not remove it, so water is obligatory. End. His statement: 'it indicates that water is recommended (mandub)' – there is consideration, rather it indicates it is sunnah. How can the recommended be better than the sunnah? Meaning if water were mandub, how could it be better than the sunnah (stone)? His statement: 'And many of the common worshippers do it'.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement: 'And it is obligatory if the impurity exceeds the exit.' It clarifies the obligation of using water when the impurity spreads beyond the exit area. Key points:

1. **Obligation (wujub)**: Washing with water becomes fard (obligatory) when the impurity exceeds the exit (i.e., spreads to the surrounding area more than a dirham in size). This is because the body's heat attracts impurity particles, and wiping with a stone does not remove them fully. The ruling is based on analogy (qiyas) for the area beyond the exit, but for the exit itself, analogy was abandoned due to the text allowing stones.

2. **Water vs. stones**: The author clarifies that the obligation is for 'washing' (ghusl) with water, not for 'istinja'' per se, because cleaning beyond the exit is not istinja'. Istinja' is only for the exit itself and is sunnah.

3. **What is considered water?**: Water here means any pure liquid that removes impurity, but the commentary notes a weak narration from Muhammad specifying water, which is not relied upon.

4. **Preventive amount**: The 'preventive amount' (the size that prevents prayer) is considered beyond the istinja' site. If the impurity exceeds that, water is obligatory.

5. **Critique of 'mandub'**: The commentator corrects a previous idea that water is merely mandub (recommended), arguing it is actually sunnah, as it cannot be that the mandub is better than the sunnah.

6. **Common practice**: The text notes that common people often expose their awrah when using water, which is sinful.

This section reinforces the Hanafi position that water is not only recommended but becomes obligatory in certain conditions, and that using substances like bone or dung is prohibited.

Key Terms
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation, here used to mean fard (obligatory in the strongest sense) when impurity exceeds the exit.
القدر المانع (al-qadr al-mani'): The amount of impurity (size of a dirham or more) that prevents the validity of prayer if it remains on the body or clothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does washing with water become obligatory (fard) after relieving oneself?
A) Always, for every time one relieves oneself.
B) Only when the impurity exceeds the exit area by more than a dirham.
C) Only if one intends to offer prayer.
D) Never, because stones always suffice.

Key Takeaway
Water is obligatory only when impurity spreads beyond the istinja' site by more than a dirham; otherwise, stones suffice for the exit itself.

Istinja with Stones or Water: The Hanafi Ruling and Its Conditions
Commentary explaining istinja rulings, the dirham measurement, and the sufficiency of stones.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istinja with stones and water, identify when water becomes obligatory, and apply the dirham measurement to determine prayer validity.

Core Idea
Stones suffice for istinja even when impurity exceeds a dirham, but combining with water is the sunna mufta bihi.

Purification from impurities (najasa) is essential for prayer validity. The Hanafi school balances ease and thoroughness: stones are permitted for cleansing, but water is preferred and becomes mandatory in certain cases. This lesson unpacks the precise conditions—especially the dirham measurement—and clarifies an important intra-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
Istinja is the cleansing of the private parts. The Hanafi school holds that using stones is sunna, water is sunna (and better), and combining both is most virtuous. However, water becomes obligatory (fard) when impurity exceeds the exit and is more than one dirham in area.
The combined use of water and stones is the mufta bihi sunna.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The allowance for stones comes from general hadith (e.g., Bukhari's narration prohibiting bone/dung but implying the permissibility of clean stones). This text-based permission overrides qiyas (analogy) that would have required water for any impurity beyond the exit.
Dalil type: sunnah ahad; thubut: qati, dalala: zanni.
3
Understand the dirham condition for prayer validity
Impurity on the body or clothing prevents prayer only if it is more than a dirham and is located beyond the normal place of istinja (mawdi' al-istinja). The area of the exit itself is legally dropped, even if the impurity there accumulates.
This is the 'amr mu'afun 'anhu' (excused amount).
4
Analyze the internal Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that stones suffice for both feces and urine, even when the impurity exceeds a dirham outside the exit. Muhammad al-Shaybani argues that stones are insufficient for such excess—water must be used. The dispute turns on whether what lies on the exit is considered 'interior' (exempt) or 'exterior' (not exempt).
The mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's view, adopted by later authorities.
5
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
The chosen view (which is the basis for fatwa) is that stones are absolutely sufficient, even for urine exceeding a dirham. The combination of water and stones remains a confirmed sunna. This eases practice, especially where water is scarce or requires exposing the private parts.
The tarjih is from Abu al-Layth and confirmed in al-Dhakhira and al-Walwaljiyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

يستنجي بروث أو عظم وقال : إنهما لا يطهران. فعلم أن ما أطلق الاستنجاء به بطهر إذ لو لم يطهر لم يطلق الاستنجاء به بحكم هذه العلة. وفي فتح القدير: وأجمع المتأخرون أنه لا ينجس بالعرق حتى لو سال العرق منه وأصاب الثوب والبدن أكثر من قدر الدرهم لا يمنع، وظاهر ما في الكتاب يدل على أن الماء مندوب سواء كان قبله الحجر أو لا. فالحاصل أنه إذا اقتصر على الحجر كان مقيماً للسنة وإذا اقتصر على الماء كان مقيماً لها أيضاً وهو من الأول، وإذا جمع بينهما كان أفضل من الكل، وقيل الجمع سنة في زماننا، وقيل سنة على الإطلاق وهو الصحيح وعليه الفتوى كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي فتح القدير: هذا والنظر إلى ما تقدم أول الفصل من حديث أنس وعائشة يفيد أن الاستنجاء بالماء سنة مؤكدة في كل زمان لإفادته ،المواظبة وفيه ما قدمناه من البحث أطلق الغسل بالماء ولم يقيده بعدد ليفيد أن الصحيح تفويضه إلى رأيه فيغسل حتى يقع في قلبه أنه طهر. كذا في الخلاصة بعد نقل الخلاف، فمنهم من شرط الثلاث، ومنهم من شرط السبع، ومنهم من شرط العشرة . والمراد بالاشتراط الاشتراط في حصول السنة وإلا فترك الكل لا يضره عندهم كما قدمناه .. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان والاستنجاء بالماء أفضل إن أمكنه ذلك من غير كشف العورة، وإن احتاج إلى كشف العورة يستنجي بالحجر ولا يستنجي بالماء. قالوا : من كشف العورة للاستنجاء يصير فاسقاً. وفي فتح القدير : ولو كان على شط نهر ليس فيه سترة لو استنجى بالماء قالوا يفسق وكثيراً ما يفعله عوام المصريين في الميضأة فضلاً عن شاطئ النيل .اهـ. وقد قدمنا الكلام عليه

عن موضعه ويتجاوز مخرجه وبجفاقه لا يزيله الحجر فوجب الماء فيه اهـ. قوله : (يدل على أن الماء (مندوب فيه نظر بل فيه إيماء إلى أنه مسنون وأنى يكون المستحب أفضل من المسنون اهـ . أي لو كان الماء مندوباً كيف يكون أفضل من الحجر المسنون قوله : وكثيراً ما يفعله عوام المصلين)
عنده .
ويعتبر في منع صحة الصلاة أن تكون النجاسة أكثر من قدر الدرهم مع سقوط موضع الاستنجاء حتى إذا كان المجاوز للمخرج مع ما على المخرج أكثر من قدر الدرهم فإنه لا يمنع لأن ما على المخرج ساقط شرعاً، ولهذا لا تكره الصلاة معه فبقي المجاوز غير مانع. وهذا عندهما خلافاً لمحمد بناء على أن ما على المخرج في حكم الباطن عندهما، وفي حكم الظاهر وهذا بعمومه يتناول ما إذا كانت مقعدته كبيرة وكان فيها نجاسة أكثر من قدر الدرهم ولم يتجاوز المخرج فإنه ينبغي أن يعفى عنه اتفاقاً لاتفاقهم على أن ما على المقعدة ساقط، وإنما خلاف محمد فيما إذا جاوزت النجاسة المخرج وكان قليلاً وكان لو جمع مع ما على المخرج كان كثيراً، فعلى هذا فالاختلاف المنقول في الشرح وغيره بين الفقيه أبي بكر القائل بأنه لا يجزئه الاستنجاء بالأحجار، وبين ابن شجاع القائل بالجواز مشكل إلا أن يخص هذا العموم بالمقعدة المعتادة التي قدر بها الدرهم الكبير المثقالي وأما الكبيرة التي جاوز ما عليها الدرهم فليست ساقطة فله وجه مع بعده. وفي السراج الوهاج : هذا حكم الغائط إذا تجاوز، وأما البول إذا تجاوز عن رأس الإحليل أكثر من قدر الدرهم فالظاهر أنه يجزئ فيه الحجر عند أبي حنيفة، وعند محمد لا يجزئ فيه الحجر إلا إذا كان أقل من قدر الدرهم اهـ. وفي الخلاصة: ولو أصاب طرف الإحليل من البول أكثر من قدر الدرهم لا تجوز صلاته الصحيح اهـ. وتعبير المصنف بموضع الاستنجاء أولى من تعبير صاحب النقاية وغيرها بالمخرج لأنه لا يجب الغسل بالماء إلا إذا تجاوز ما على نفس المخرج وما حوله من موضع الشرج، وكان المجاوز أكثر من قدر الدرهم كما في المجتبى. وذكر في العناية معزياً إلى القنية أنه إذا أصاب موضع الاستنجاء نجاسة من الخارج أكثر من قدر الدرهم يطهر بالحجر، وقيل الصحيح أنه لا طهر إلا بالغسل وقد قدمنا أنه يطهر بالحجر، وقد نقلوا هذا التصحيح هنا بصيغة التمريض فالظاهر خلافه والله أعلم . قوله : (لا) بعظم وروث وطعام ويمين) أي لا يستنجي بهذه الأشياء، والمراد أنه يكره بها كما صرح به الشارح. والظاهر أنها كراهة تحريم للنهي الوارد في ذلك لما روى البخاري من حديث أبي هريرة في بدء الخلق أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال
هو
كذا في بعض النسخ وفي بعضها المصريين قوله : (وهذا بعمومه الخ) الإشارة إلى قوله «لأن ما على المخرج ساقط شرعاً فإنه يتناول ما إذا كان أكثر من الدرهم، وظاهره أنه متفق عليه لأنه ذكر دليلاً لعدم منع المتجاوز الذي فيه خلاف محمد وشأن الدليل أن يكون مسلماً عند الخصم لكن صرح في الخلاصة بأنه عند محمد لا يكفيه الحجر إذا كانت النجاسة على موضع الاستنجاء أكثر من الدرهم، ونقل عن أبي يوسف روايتين. وعن أبي حنيفة أنه يكفي وفي البدائع : إنه لم يذكر في ظاهر الرواية. واختلف المشايخ فيه قيل لا يكفي فيه الحجر، وقيل يكفي وبه أخذ أبو الليث وهو الصحيح لأن الشرع ورد بالاستنجاء بالأحجار مطلقاً من غير فصل وفي الذخيرة والولوالجية أنه المختار .
Book of Purification - Chapter of Impurities. It is recommended and obligatory if the impurity exceeds the exit and the amount that prevents prayer is considered beyond the place of istinja, not with bone, dung, food, and the right [hand]. That he prefers to perform istinja with dung or bone and said: They do not purify. So it is known that what is allowed for istinja with it purifies, because if it did not purify, istinja would not be permitted with it by virtue of this cause. And in Fath al-Qadir: The later scholars have agreed that it does not become impure with sweat, so if sweat flows from him and hits clothing and body more than the size of a dirham, it does not prevent. The apparent meaning of what is in the book indicates that water is recommended whether stones preceded it or not. So the summary is that if he restricts to stones, he is fulfilling the sunna; if he restricts to water, he is also fulfilling it, and it is from the first; if he combines both, it is better than all. It was said that the combination is a sunna in our time, and it was said it is a sunna absolutely, and that is correct and the fatwa is upon it, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And in Fath al-Qadir: This, and consideration of what preceded at the beginning of the chapter from the hadith of Anas and Aisha, indicates that istinja with water is a confirmed sunna in every time because it conveys continuity. And in it is what we presented before: the washing with water was absolute and not restricted by a number to indicate that the correct view is to delegate to his opinion so he washes until he feels that he has become pure. So also in al-Khulasa after reporting the disagreement: among them who required three, among them who required seven, among them who required ten. And by requiring is meant requiring for attainment of sunna, otherwise leaving all does not harm him according to them, as we presented earlier. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: Istinja with water is better if he can do it without exposing the private parts, but if he needs to expose the private parts, he performs istinja with stones and does not perform istinja with water. They said: Whoever exposes his private parts for istinja becomes a sinner. And in Fath al-Qadir: If he is on the bank of a river with no screen, if he performs istinja with water, they said he sins. And many of the common Egyptians do this in the ablution area, let alone on the bank of the Nile. End. And we have already discussed it at the beginning of the chapter. It is called. His statement: (And it becomes obligatory if the impurity exceeds the exit) i.e., it becomes obligatory to wash the place with water if the impurity exceeds the exit, because the body has a heat that attracts the parts of the impurity, so wiping with stone does not remove it, and that is the analogy for the place of istinja, but it was left there due to the text contrary to analogy, so it does not extend beyond it. And we interpreted the subject of 'must' as washing, not istinja, as the commentator al-Zayla'i did, because washing other than the exit is not istinja, and because istinja is only sunna. And he meant by water here every pure liquid that removes, by indication of his explicit statement of carrying it on the narration of Muhammad specifying water, as he pointed out in al-Kafi, because it is from the weak ones in the madhhab as you know earlier. And he meant by exceeding to be more than the size of a dirham by indication of what follows. And then the intended meaning of obligation is fard. His statement: (And the preventing amount is considered beyond the place of istinja) i.e., we presented at the beginning of the chapter that it is more appropriate. It removes feces from its place and exceeds its exit, and with its side, the stone does not remove it, so water is obligatory. End. His statement: (It indicates that water is recommended) there is scrutiny in it, rather it suggests that it is sunna, and how can the recommended be better than the sunna? End. i.e., if water is recommended, how is it better than the sunna of stones? His statement: And many of the common worshippers do it. With him. And it is considered for preventing the validity of prayer that the impurity is more than a dirham amount, with the dropping of the place of istinja, so that if the part exceeding the exit together with what is on the exit is more than a dirham, it does not prevent, because what is on the exit is legally dropped, and therefore prayer is not disliked with it, so the exceeding remains non-preventing. And this is according to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) contrary to Muhammad (al-Shaybani) based on the fact that what is on the exit is in the ruling of the interior according to them, and in the ruling of the exterior according to Muhammad. And this by its generality includes the case where his buttock is large and there is more than a dirham of impurity on it and it does not exceed the exit, then it should be excused unanimously because they agree that what is on the buttock is dropped. The disagreement of Muhammad is only when the impurity exceeds the exit and is little, and if combined with what is on the exit it would be much. So based on this, the disagreement reported in the commentary and elsewhere between al-Faqih Abu Bakr who said that istinja with stones is not sufficient, and Ibn Shuja' who said it is permissible, is problematic unless this generality is specified to the usual buttock whose dirham is the large mithqali dirham. As for the large one whose amount exceeds a dirham, it is not dropped, so his view has some justification but it is weak. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: This is the ruling for feces if it exceeds, and as for urine if it exceeds the tip of the urethra by more than a dirham, the apparent view is that stones are sufficient according to Abu Hanifa, and according to Muhammad, stones are not sufficient unless it is less than a dirham. End. And in al-Khulasa: If the tip of the urethra is affected by more than a dirham of urine, his prayer is not valid according to the correct view. End. And the author's expression 'place of istinja' is better than the expression of the author of al-Nuqaya and others of 'exit' because water is not obligatory except when what is on the very exit and what is around it from the area of the anus exceeds, and the exceeding is more than a dirham as in al-Mujtaba. And it is mentioned in al-Inaya attributed to al-Quniya that if the place of istinja is hit by impurity from outside more than a dirham, it is purified with stones, and it was said the correct view is that there is no purification except with washing, and we have already said it is purified with stones, and they have transmitted this correction here with a hedging formulation, so the apparent is otherwise, and Allah knows best. His statement: (Not) with bone, dung, food, and the right [hand] i.e., one should not perform istinja with these things, and what is meant is that it is disliked, as the commentator stated. And the apparent is that it is a prohibitive dislike (makruh tahrimi) due to the prohibition transmitted in that regard, as narrated by Bukhari from Abu Huraira in the Beginning of Creation that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said... It is so in some copies, and in some copies 'the Egyptians'. His statement: (And this by its generality etc.) refers to his statement 'because what is on the exit is legally dropped' as it includes the case when it is more than a dirham. Its apparent meaning is that it is agreed upon because he mentioned a proof for the non-prevention of the exceeding, which involves the disagreement of Muhammad, and the nature of a proof is that it is accepted by the opponent. However, it was explicitly stated in al-Khulasa that according to Muhammad, stones are not sufficient for him if the impurity on the place of istinja is more than a dirham. And two narrations are reported from Abu Yusuf. And from Abu Hanifa that it is sufficient. And in al-Bada'i': It is not mentioned in the apparent narrations. And the shaykhs differed: some said stones are not sufficient, and some said they are sufficient, and Abu al-Layth adopted this, and it is correct because the sharia came with performing istinja with stones absolutely without distinction. And in al-Dhakhira and al-Walwaljiyya, it is the chosen view.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq, explaining the rulings of istinja and the impact of impurity on the validity of prayer. The author, Ibn Nujaym, expands on each phrase of the matn. The matn states that using water is recommended (and obligatory in certain cases), that the amount of impurity that prevents prayer is considered beyond the place of istinja, and that one should not use bone, dung, food, or the right hand. The commentary begins by discussing the virtue of water over stones: combining both is best, but using only water or only stones both fulfill the sunna. Citing Fath al-Qadir, it reports that later scholars agree that sweat does not become impure, even if it exceeds a dirham. The preferred view is that water is sunna, not merely recommended, and the fatwa is on the combination of water and stones as sunna. The commentary then explains the condition when water becomes obligatory: when impurity exceeds the exit and is more than a dirham in area. This is an exception to the general qiyas that stones would suffice, but the text overrides qiyas. The author clarifies that the 'obligation' here means fard. Next, the commentary addresses the amount of impurity that prevents prayer: only when the impurity exceeds the exit and is more than a dirham does it prevent prayer. The area of the exit itself is excluded (dropped legally). There is a dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on one side and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the other: according to the first two, what is on the exit is considered interior (and thus exempt), while Muhammad considers it exterior. The practical consequence is whether stones suffice for impurity that exceeds a dirham combined with what is on the exit. There is also a discussion about urine: according to Abu Hanifa, stones suffice for urine exceeding a dirham, but not according to Muhammad. The commentary then discusses the prohibition of using bone, dung, food, and the right hand for istinja, noting that it is makruh tahrimi based on a hadith from Bukhari. Finally, the passage addresses the case where the buttock is large and impurity remains on it without exceeding the exit: it is unanimously excused. The author presents the differences of opinion and concludes that the correct view is that stones suffice absolutely, as per Abu al-Layth, and it is the chosen view in later works.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): The act of cleaning the private parts after relieving oneself, typically with water or stones.
قدر الدرهم (qadr al-dirham): The size of a dirham coin, used as a legal measure for the amount of impurity that affects prayer validity; approximately 4.25 grams or area of a typical silver dirham.
موضع الاستنجاء (mawdi' al-istinja): The area around the private parts that is typically involved in cleaning; includes the exit and its surroundings up to the buttocks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what is the ruling regarding istinja with stones when urine exceeds a dirham?
A) Stones are not sufficient; water is required.
B) Stones are sufficient, as per Abu Hanifa and the chosen view.
C) Stones are only sufficient for feces, not urine.
D) Stones are sufficient only if the urine is less than a dirham.

Key Takeaway
Stones are sufficient for istinja even when impurity exceeds a dirham; the Hanafi school allows ease while maintaining the sunna of water.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
6 min
Impurity at the Place of Istinja: Excused or Not?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on impurity threshold exemption for istinja site.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on impurity at the place of istinja and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the threshold for prayer validity.

Core Idea
Impurity on the exit is legally excused; only the excess beyond counts toward the dirham threshold.

In the Hanafi school, the validity of prayer depends on the amount of impurity on the body. However, not all impurity is treated equally. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a key exception: the impurity naturally present at the site of istinja is legally disregarded. We will explore the intra-madhhab dispute on this point and understand the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon (prayer validity) and the general ruling: impurity exceeding a dirham invalidates prayer.
The dirham is a measure of impurity extent; less than a dirham is pardoned.
2
Locate the Exception for the Makhraj
Note that impurity on the makhraj (exit) is legally excused (sāqit), so it is not counted toward the dirham threshold.
This is based on the principle that what is on the makhraj is considered internal (hukm al-bātin).
3
Understand the Ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold the makhraj impurity is excused; Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it is not excused and must be counted.
Muhammad considers the makhraj as external (zāhir), so total impurity including that on the exit matters.
4
Apply the Thamarah al-Khilaf
If total impurity on and around the makhraj is more than a dirham but the part beyond the makhraj alone is less than a dirham, prayer is valid according to Abu Hanifa, invalid according to Muhammad.
The practical consequence: one must know which view to follow for fatwa.
5
Identify the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa, as stated in al-Dhakhira and al-Walwaljiya.
Later mashāyikh adopted this view, making it the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعتبر في منع صحة الصلاة أن تكون النجاسة أكثر من قدر الدرهم مع سقوط موضع الاستنجاء حتى إذا كان المجاوز للمخرج مع ما على المخرج أكثر من قدر الدرهم فإنه لا يمنع لأن ما على المخرج ساقط شرعاً، ولهذا لا تكره الصلاة معه فبقي المجاوز غير مانع. وهذا عندهما خلافاً لمحمد بناء على أن ما على المخرج في حكم الباطن عندهما، وفي حكم الظاهر وهذا بعمومه يتناول ما إذا كانت مقعدته كبيرة وكان فيها نجاسة أكثر من قدر الدرهم ولم يتجاوز المخرج فإنه ينبغي أن يعفى عنه اتفاقاً لاتفاقهم على أن ما على المقعدة ساقط، وإنما خلاف محمد فيما إذا جاوزت النجاسة المخرج وكان قليلاً وكان لو جمع مع ما على المخرج كان كثيراً، فعلى هذا فالاختلاف المنقول في الشرح وغيره بين الفقيه أبي بكر القائل بأنه لا يجزئه الاستنجاء بالأحجار، وبين ابن شجاع القائل بالجواز مشكل إلا أن يخص هذا العموم بالمقعدة المعتادة التي قدر بها الدرهم الكبير المثقالي وأما الكبيرة التي جاوز ما عليها الدرهم فليست ساقطة فله وجه مع بعده. وفي السراج الوهاج : هذا حكم الغائط إذا تجاوز، وأما البول إذا تجاوز عن رأس الإحليل أكثر من قدر الدرهم فالظاهر أنه يجزئ فيه الحجر عند أبي حنيفة، وعند محمد لا يجزئ فيه الحجر إلا إذا كان أقل من قدر الدرهم اهـ. وفي الخلاصة: ولو أصاب طرف الإحليل من البول أكثر من قدر الدرهم لا تجوز صلاته الصحيح اهـ. وتعبير المصنف بموضع الاستنجاء أولى من تعبير صاحب النقاية وغيرها بالمخرج لأنه لا يجب الغسل بالماء إلا إذا تجاوز ما على نفس المخرج وما حوله من موضع الشرج، وكان المجاوز أكثر من قدر الدرهم كما في المجتبى. وذكر في العناية معزياً إلى القنية أنه إذا أصاب موضع الاستنجاء نجاسة من الخارج أكثر من قدر الدرهم يطهر بالحجر، وقيل الصحيح أنه لا طهر إلا بالغسل وقد قدمنا أنه يطهر بالحجر، وقد نقلوا هذا التصحيح هنا بصيغة التمريض فالظاهر خلافه والله أعلم .
It is considered in preventing the validity of prayer that the impurity be more than the amount of a dirham, with the exemption of the place of istinja. So if the excess beyond the exit along with what is on the exit is more than a dirham, it does not prevent, because what is on the exit is legally dropped. Hence prayer with it is not disliked, so the excess remains non-preventing. This is according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) contrary to Muhammad, based on the fact that what is on the exit is in the ruling of internal according to them, and in the ruling of external according to Muhammad. This generality includes the case where his seat is large and there is impurity more than a dirham without exceeding the exit; then it should be excused unanimously, because they agree that what is on the seat is dropped. The only dispute with Muhammad is when the impurity exceeds the exit and is little, and if combined with what is on the exit it would be much. According to this, the reported disagreement in the commentary and others between Faqih Abu Bakr, who says istinja with stones is not sufficient, and Ibn Shuja, who says it is permissible, is problematic, unless this generality is restricted to the normal seat, which is measured by the large mithqali dirham. As for the large seat where what is on it exceeds a dirham, it is not dropped, so it has a point though far-fetched. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: This is the ruling for feces if it exceeds. As for urine, if it exceeds the tip of the urethra by more than a dirham, apparently it is sufficient with a stone according to Abu Hanifa. According to Muhammad, stone is not sufficient unless it is less than a dirham. End quote. In al-Khulasa: If the tip of the urethra is affected by urine more than a dirham, his prayer is not valid—the correct view. End quote. The author's expression 'place of istinja' is better than the expression of the author of al-Niqayah and others using 'exit', because washing with water is not obligatory unless the impurity exceeds what is on the exit itself and around it from the area of the anus, and the excess is more than a dirham, as in al-Mujtaba. It is mentioned in al-Inayah, citing al-Qunyah, that if a place of istinja is affected by external impurity more than a dirham, it is purified with a stone. It is said the correct view is that there is no purification except with water, and we have previously stated that it is purified with a stone. They have transmitted this correction here in a weakening form (tamrid), so apparently the opposite is true, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of impurity on the validity of prayer when the impurity is on the place of istinja (the exit area). The ruling: For impurity to prevent prayer, it must exceed a dirham in amount, BUT with the provision that the impurity residing on the makhraj (the exit itself) is legally disregarded (sāqit). Therefore, if the total impurity (including that on the makhraj) is more than a dirham, but the part beyond the makhraj alone is less than a dirham, prayer is valid. The basis is that what is on the makhraj is considered internal (hukm al-bātin) legally, as it is the natural site of impurity. The author explains that this is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) contrary to Muhammad's own known view? Actually, the text states 'عندهما خلافاً لمحمد' which is ambiguous: 'عندهما' likely refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad as a pair, but then 'خلافاً لمحمد' would be contradictory. The correct understanding as per Hanafi sources is that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the makhraj area is excused, while Muhammad holds it is not excused (it counts as external). So the text may have an error. The commentary then discusses if the seat (maq'ada) is large and impurity is only on the seat without exceeding the exit, it is unanimously excused. The dispute is when impurity exceeds the exit and is little, but combined with the excused part becomes much. The author then links this to a reported disagreement between Faqih Abu Bakr and Ibn Shuja on the sufficiency of stones, noting it is problematic. Then quotes al-Siraj al-Wahhaj distinguishing between feces and urine: for urine exceeding the urethra tip, Abu Hanifa allows stones, Muhammad does not unless less than a dirham. Al-Khulasa says if urine at the tip exceeds a dirham, prayer is invalid. The author prefers the term 'place of istinja' over 'exit' because washing is only required if impurity goes beyond the anus area. Finally, he mentions a citation from al-Inayah/al-Qunyah that external impurity on the istinja site can be cleaned with a stone, though some say only water suffices; the author leans towards stone being sufficient despite the 'tamrid' weakening.

Key Terms
موضع الاستنجاء (mawḍiʿ al-istinjāʾ): The area of the anus and its immediate surroundings that is cleansed during istinja.
ساقط شرعاً (sāqiṭ sharʿan): Legally disregarded: the impurity on the makhraj is not counted toward the threshold that invalidates prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if the total impurity on and around the makhraj is 1.5 dirhams but the part beyond the makhraj is only 0.75 dirhams, is the prayer valid?
A) Yes, because the impurity on the makhraj is excused.
B) No, because the total exceeds a dirham.
C) It depends on whether it is urine or feces.
D) Only if washed with water.

Key Takeaway
Impurity on the exit site is legally excused; only the spread beyond matters for the dirham threshold.

Prohibited and Disliked Materials for Istinja
Ruling with proof on prohibited istinja materials

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istinja with bone, dung, food, and the right hand, and identify the hadith evidence that establishes the prohibition-level dislike.

Core Idea
Using bone, dung, food, or the right hand for istinja is makruh tahrimi due to explicit prophetic prohibitions.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the Hanafi position on which materials are disliked for istinja and why. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states 'Not with bone, dung, food, and right hand.' The commentator clarifies that this means it is disliked, and the primary evidence is prophetic hadith. We will examine the hadith, the rationale for each prohibition, and the expanded list of thirteen disliked items.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and specific prohibition
The act is istinja (cleaning after relieving oneself). The prohibition applies to using bone, dung, food, and the right hand. Determine the ruling level from the text: it is makruh tahrimi.
The text says 'لا يستنجي' which indicates prohibition; the commentator says 'كراهة تحريم'.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
Two hadith are cited: (1) Bukhari: Prophet tells Abu Hurairah to bring stones, not bone or dung. (2) Abu Qatadah: prohibition of using right hand for wiping or touching private parts. Assess thubut (transmission) and dalala (meaning).
The hadith are ahad but authentic; Hanafi principle: nahy (prohibition) indicates tahrim.
3
Understand the Hanafi classification of the prohibition
The ruling is makruh tahrimi (dislike approaching prohibition) rather than haram, because the evidence is zanni al-thubut. Distinguish from makruh tanzihi (dislike without prohibition).
This is a key Hanafi usul concept: ahad hadith yield karahah tahrimi, not absolute haram.
4
List the additional disliked items and reasons
The text lists 13 items from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: bone, dung, retted dung (rajī‘), coal, food, glass, paper, pottery, reed, hair, cotton, cloth, and animal feed. For each, note why it is disliked: impurity (dung), harm (glass/pottery/coal), waste (food), or causing poverty (others).
The right hand is prohibited due to explicit hadith; excuses are allowed.
5
Note the nuance: istinja is sunnah
The commentator emphasizes that istinja is a sunnah, not wajib. Therefore, using a prohibited item may mean the sunnah is not fulfilled, and the term 'ijza' (sufficiency) is loosely used. Understand that the ruling of makruh tahrimi does not invalidate the purification, but it is contrary to the sunnah.
This nuance is important: the act is valid (taharah achieved) but disliked, and the reward of following the sunnah is lost.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا) بعظم وروث وطعام ويمين) أي لا يستنجي بهذه الأشياء، والمراد أنه يكره بها كما صرح به الشارح. والظاهر أنها كراهة تحريم للنهي الوارد في ذلك لما روى البخاري من حديث أبي هريرة في بدء الخلق أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال له : اتبعني أحجاراً استنقض بها ولا تأتني بعظم ولا بروثة. قالت: ما بال العظام والروثة؟ قال : هما من طعام الجن. وروى أصحاب الكتب الستة عن أبي قتادة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم «إذا بال أحدكم فلا يمس ذكره بيمينه وإذا أتى الخلاء فلا يتمسح بيمينه، وإذا شرب فلا يشرب نفساً السنة : واحداً وفي القنية في شرح جمع الحديث النهي عن الاستنجاء باليمين ومس الذكر باليمين ولا يمكنه إلا بالارتكاب أحدهما، فالصواب أن يأخذ الذكر بشماله فيمره على جدار أو ناء موضع من الأرض وإن تعذر يقعد ويمسك الحجر بين عقبيه فيمر العضو عليه بشماله، فإن تعذر يأخذ الحجر بيمينه ولا يحركه ويمر العضو عليه بشماله. قال مولانا نجم الدين : وفيما أشار إليه من إمساك الحجر بعقبيه حرج وتعسير وتكلف، بل يستنجي بجدار إن أمكن وإلا يأخذ الحجر بيمينه ويستنجي بيساره .ا.هـ. وليس مراده القصر على هذه الأشياء فإن ما يكره الاستنجاء به ثلاثة عشر كما في السراج الوهاج : العظم والروث والرجيع والفحم والطعام والزجاج والورق والخزف والقصب والشعر والقطن والخرقة وعلف الدواب مثل الحشيش وغيره. فإن استنجى بها أجزأه مع الكراهة لحصول المقصود، والروث وإن كان نجساً عندنا بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام فيها ركس أو رجس لكن لما كان يابساً لا ينفصل منه شيء صح الاستنجاء به لأنه يجفف ما على البدن من النجاسة الرطبة والرجيع العذرة اليابسة، وقيل الحجر الذي قد استنجى به وفي فتح القدير: ولا يجزئه الاستنجاء بحجر استنجى به مرة إلا أن يكون له حرف آخر لم يستنج به .اهـ. والورق قيل إنه ورق الكتابة، وقيل إنه ورق الشجر، وأي ذلك كان فإنه مكروه. وأما الطعام فلأنه إسراف ،وإهانة وإنما كرهوا وضع المملحة على الخبز للإهانة فهذا أولى، وسواء كان مائعاً أو لا كاللحم وأما الخزف والزجاج والفحم فإنه يضر بالمقعدة، وأما باليمين فللنهي المتقدم، فإن كان باليسرى عذر يمنع الاستنجاء بها جاز أن يستنجي بيمينه من غير كراهة. وأما باقي هذه الأشياء فقيل إن الاستنجاء بها يورث الفقر، وقد قدمنا أن التحقيق أن الاستنجاء لا يكون إلا سنة فينبغي أنه إذا استنجى بالمنهي عنه أن لا يكون مقيماً لسنة الاستنجاء أصلاً، فقولهم بالإجزاء مع الكراهة تسامح لأن مثل هذه العبارة تستعمل في الواجب وليس به والله الموفق للصواب.
His statement: 'Not with bone, dung, food, and right hand' — meaning one should not perform istinja with these things. The intent is that it is disliked (makruh), as the commentator clarified. Apparently it is a prohibition-level dislike (karahah tahrim) due to the prohibition reported. Bukhari narrated from Abu Hurairah in the beginning of creation that the Prophet ﷺ said to him: 'Follow me with stones to clean yourself, and do not bring me bone or dung.' She said: 'What about bones and dung?' He said: 'They are from the food of the jinn.' The six books narrated from Abu Qatadah that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'When one of you urinates, let him not touch his penis with his right hand, and when he goes to the toilet, let him not wipe with his right hand, and when he drinks, let him not drink in one breath.' In al-Qunyah, in the commentary on the hadith collection, there is a prohibition of istinja with the right hand and touching the penis with the right hand. One cannot avoid both except by committing one. The correct is to take the penis with the left hand and rub it on a wall or some place on the ground. If difficult, he sits and holds the stone between his heels and rubs the organ with his left hand. If difficult, he takes the stone with his right hand without moving it and rubs the organ with his left. Our master Najm al-Din said: In what he indicated about holding the stone between the heels is hardship and difficulty; rather, he should perform istinja with a wall if possible, otherwise take the stone with his right hand and perform istinja with his left. End quote. He did not intend to limit to these things, for what is disliked for istinja is thirteen, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: bone, dung, retted dung, coal, food, glass, paper, pottery, reed, hair, cotton, cloth, and animal feed like hay etc. If one performs istinja with them, it suffices with dislike, because the purpose is achieved. Dung, although impure according to us due to his statement ﷺ that it is 'rijs' or 'rujs', but since it is dry, nothing separates from it, so istinja with it is valid because it dries the moist impurity on the body. 'Rajī‘' is dry human stool. It is also said: the stone that has been used for istinja. In Fath al-Qadir: Istinja with a stone used once is not sufficient unless it has another edge that has not been used. End quote. Paper: it is said it is writing paper, and it is said it is leaf paper; whichever it is, it is disliked. As for food, because it is wasteful and degrading; they disliked placing a salt cellar on bread due to degradation, so this is more appropriate. It is the same whether it is liquid or not, like meat. As for pottery, glass, and coal, they harm the anus. As for the right hand, due to the preceding prohibition. If there is an excuse in the left hand preventing istinja with it, it is permissible to perform istinja with the right hand without dislike. As for the remaining items, it is said that istinja with them causes poverty. We have previously stated that the reality is that istinja is only a sunnah. Therefore, if one performs istinja with what is prohibited, he is not upholding the sunnah of istinja at all. Their statement of sufficiency with dislike is a laxity, because such expressions are used for obligatory acts, and it is not obligatory. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on what is prohibited/disliked for istinja, based on explicit hadith. The commentator (Zayla'i) explains the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq which says 'Not with bone, dung, food, and right hand'. The ruling is that these are disliked, and the apparent level is karahah tahrimi (prohibition-level dislike) due to the prophetic prohibition. The hadith from Bukhari shows the Prophet forbidding bringing bone and dung because they are food for jinn. Another hadith from Abu Qatadah prohibits using the right hand for touching the private part or wiping after toilet. The commentator then discusses the method if both hands are needed, with a preference for using the left hand for the organ. Najm al-Din critiques the suggestion of holding a stone between the heels as impractical. The text then expands the list to 13 disliked items from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, including coal, glass, paper, pottery, reed, hair, cotton, cloth, and animal feed. Although some such items may be impure (like dung), they can be used if dry because they don't transfer impurity. A stone used once is not reusable unless a clean edge remains. Food is disliked because it is wasteful and degrading. Glass, pottery, and coal harm the anus. The right hand is prohibited unless there is an excuse in the left. The commentator notes a nuance: since istinja is a sunnah, using a prohibited item may mean the sunnah is not attained. The claim of sufficiency (ijza) with dislike is a laxity in terminology, as 'ijza' is normally used for obligatory acts.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريم (karāha taḥrīm): A level of dislike that approaches prohibition; the act is forbidden but not at the level of haram (which requires definitive evidence).
الاستنجاء (al-istinjāʾ): Cleaning the private parts after relieving oneself, typically with stones or water.
الرجيع (al-rajīʿ): Dry human stool (dried feces).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, using which of the following for istinja is considered makruh tahrimi?
A) Dry dung
B) Clean paper
C) Water
D) Smooth stone

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that istinja with bone, dung, food, and the right hand is makruh tahrimi due to explicit hadith; using these items is valid but contrary to the sunnah.
