Adab of Entering the Toilet and Makruhat
Ruling statement on toilet adab (sunan and makruhat)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (sunna) and disliked (makruh) actions when entering and using the toilet, and apply these rulings to common scenarios.

Core Idea
The toilet has its own sacred etiquette: enter with du'a and leave with thanks; avoid speech, qibla, and harmful places.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq compiles the prophetic etiquettes (adab) for using the toilet. It distinguishes between recommended acts (sunan) that follow the sunna and disliked acts (makruhat) that are best avoided. Understanding these rulings helps a Muslim maintain taqwa even in private moments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Recognize that the passage covers the act of entering and using the toilet. The rulings are either sunnah (recommended) or makruh tanzihi (disliked without sin).
The overall act is mubah, but the etiquettes carry reward or dislike.
2
List the Recommended Acts (Sunan)
Scan the passage for statements indicating recommendation: entering with a separate garment, covering the head, reciting the du'a, entering with left foot, sitting properly, and saying the post-exit du'a.
These are not obligatory but following them earns reward.
3
List the Disliked Acts (Makruhat)
Identify all actions the passage labels as 'yukrah' (it is disliked): entering with a ring bearing Allah's name, speaking, looking at private parts, facing/turning back to qibla, urinating in water, under a fruit tree, on a path, etc.
Some disliked acts are makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked), others may be makruh tahrimi (close to haram) – the passage does not specify the degree.
4
Note the Exceptions
The passage provides exceptions: if one forgetfully faces qibla, he should turn away if possible; urinating standing is allowed with an excuse; covering head is recommended but not required if one has no separate garment.
Exceptions show that rulings are not absolute.
5
Summarize the Du'as
The passage gives two du'as: one upon entering ('Bismillah, Allahumma inni a'udhu bika...') and one upon exiting ('Alhamdulillah alladhi adhhaba anni al-adha wa afani').
Memorize these for daily practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فروع : إذا أراد الإنسان دخول الخلاء وهو بيت التغوط يستحب له أن يدخل بثوب غير ثوبه الذي يصلي فيه إن كان له ذلك وإلا فيجتهد في حفظ ثوبه عن إصابة النجاسة والماء المستعمل، ويدخل مستور الرأس ويقول عند دخوله : باسم الله اللهم إني أعوذ بك من الخبث والخبائث، وأعوذ بك الرجس الخبيث المخبث الشيطان الرجيم والخبث بسكون الباء بمعنى الشر، وبضمها جمع الخبيث وهو الذكر من الشيطان والخبائث جمع الخبيثة وهي الأنثى من الشياطين. ويكره أن يدخل الخلاء ومعه خاتم مكتوب عليه اسم الله تعالى أو شيء من القرآن . ويبدأ برجله اليسرى ويقعد ولا يكشف عورته وهو قائم ويوسع بين رجليه ويميل على اليسرى، ولا يتكلم على الخلاء فإن الله تعالى يمقت على ذلك. والمقت هو البغض. ولا يذكر الله ولا يحمد إذا عطس، ولا يشمت عاطساً، ولا يرد السلام ولا يجيب المؤذن، ولا ينظر لعورته إلا لحاجة، ولا ينظر إلى ما يخرج منه ولا يبزق ولا يمخط، ولا يتنحنح، ولا يكثر الالتفات، ولا يعبث ببدنه، ولا يرفع بصره إلى السماء ولا يطيل القعود على البول والغائط لأنه يورث الباسور أو وجع الكبد كما روي عن لقمان عليه السلام، فإذا فرغ قام ويقول : الحمد لله الذي أذهب عني الأذى وعافاني أي بإبقاء شيء من الطعام لأنه لو خرج كله .هلك . ويكره البول والغائط في الماء ولو كان جارياً، ويكره على طرف نهر أو بئر أو حوض أو عين أو . تحت شجرة مثمرة أو في زرع أو في ظل ينتفع بالجلوس فيه، ويكره بجنب المساجد ومصلى العيد وفي المقابر وبين الدواب وفي طرق المسلمين ومستقبل القلبة ومستدبرها ولو في البنيان، فإن جلس مستقبل القبلة ناسياً ثم ذكر بعده أن أمكنه الانحراف انحرف وإلا فلا بأس. وكذا يكره للمرأة أن تمسك ولدها للبول والغائط نحو القبلة، واختلفوا في الاستقبال للتطهر فاختار التمرتاشي أنه لا يكره. وكذا يكره استقبال الشمس والقمر لأنهما من آيات الله الباهرة، ويكره أن يقعد في أسفل الأرض ويبول في أعلاها وأن يبول في مهب الريح وأن يبول في حجر فأرة أو حية أو نملة أو ثقب ويكره أن يبول قائماً أو مضطجعاً أو متجرداً عن ثوبه من غير عذر، فإن كان لعذر فلا بأس لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام بال قائماً لوجع في صلبه، ويكره أن يبول في موضع ويتوضأ أو يغتسل فيه للنهي، كذا في السراج الوهاج.
Branches: When a person wants to enter the toilet, which is the house of defecation, it is recommended that he enter wearing a garment other than the one in which he prays, if he has one; otherwise, he should strive to protect his garment from hitting impurity and used water. He should enter with his head covered and say upon entering: 'In the name of Allah, O Allah, I seek refuge in You from male and female devils, and I seek refuge in You from the filthy, wicked, accursed devil.' Al-khubth (with sukoon on the ba) means evil; with dammah, it is the plural of khabeeth (the male devil), and khaba'ith is the plural of khabeetha (the female devil). It is disliked to enter the toilet while wearing a ring on which is written the name of Allah or something from the Quran. He should begin with his left foot, sit down, and not uncover his private parts while standing. He should spread his legs apart and lean on his left side. He should not speak in the toilet, for Allah detests that. Al-maqt is hatred. He should not remember Allah nor praise Him if he sneezes, nor respond to a sneezer, nor return the greeting of peace, nor answer the mu'adhdhin. He should not look at his private parts except for need, nor look at what comes out of him, nor spit, nor blow his nose, nor clear his throat, nor turn around excessively, nor fidget with his body, nor raise his gaze to the sky, nor prolong sitting over urine and stool because it causes hemorrhoids or liver pain as narrated from Luqman (peace be upon him). When he finishes, he should stand and say: 'Praise be to Allah who has removed from me harm and granted me well-being' meaning by preserving some food, because if all came out he would perish. It is disliked to urinate or defecate into water even if flowing; at the edge of a river, well, basin, spring; under a fruit-bearing tree; in a cultivated field; in a shadow used for sitting; near mosques and the Eid prayer place; in graveyards; among animals; on Muslim pathways; and facing or turning one's back to the qibla even inside a building. If one sits facing qibla forgetfully and then remembers, if he can turn away he should, otherwise no problem. Similarly, it is disliked for a woman to hold her child for urination or defecation toward the qibla. There is disagreement about facing the qibla during purification; al-Tamartashi chose that it is not disliked. It is also disliked to face the sun and moon because they are magnificent signs of Allah. It is disliked to sit at a lower place and urinate higher up; to urinate into the wind; to urinate into the hole of a mouse, snake, ant, or any hole; to urinate standing or lying down or naked without excuse; if there is an excuse, there is no harm because the Prophet (peace be upon him) urinated standing due to pain in his back. It is disliked to urinate in a place where one performs wudu or ghusl, due to the prohibition. So in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the adab (etiquette) and makruhat (disliked actions) related to entering and using the toilet. It is a compilation of sunan and makruhat from Hanafi fiqh. The text begins with recommended actions: entering with a separate garment (to protect the prayer garment), covering the head, reciting the prescribed du'a (seeking refuge from male and female devils). It is disliked to enter with anything bearing Allah's name or Quranic verses. One should enter with the left foot, sit, and not uncover while standing; spread legs and lean left. Prohibitions during toilet: no speaking, no dhikr, no returning greetings, no answering adhan, no looking at private parts or excrement, no spitting, nose blowing, throat clearing, excessive turning, fidgeting, looking up, prolonged sitting (as it causes health issues). After finishing, say the du'a of thanks. Numerous disliked locations for urination/defecation: in water, at water sources, under fruit trees, in fields, in shaded sitting areas, near mosques/eid prayer places, graveyards, among animals, on paths, facing or back to qibla (even indoors). If done forgetfully, turn away if possible. For women, holding a child toward qibla is disliked. Facing sun/moon is disliked. Urinating from low to high, into wind, into animal holes, standing without excuse, in a place used for wudu/ghusl are all disliked. The proof for some rulings is cited (e.g., Prophet urinated standing due to back pain). The overall ruling is that these acts are makruh tanzihan.

Key Terms
الخبث (al-khubth): Evil; with dammah, plural of khabeeth (male devil).
المقت (al-maqt): Intense hatred or detestation.
القبلة (al-qibla): Direction of the Kaaba in Mecca.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on speaking while in the toilet according to this passage?
A) It is permissible (mubah) if necessary.
B) It is disliked (makruh) because Allah detests it.
C) It is recommended (sunnah) to speak to avoid anger.
D) It is forbidden (haram) due to impurity.

Key Takeaway
The prophetic etiquettes for the toilet are a blend of sunan (rewarded) and makruhat (disliked but not sinful); following them is a sign of complete iman.

Method of Istinja and Etiquette of Entering the Toilet
Ruling and commentary on istinja method and entry etiquette

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended method of istinja with water and identify the exception when the left hand has an excuse, and describe the ruling on entering a long passage or connected mosques.

Core Idea
Pour water with right, wash with left; left hand excuse permits using right without dislike.

This lesson covers the proper etiquette of istinja (cleansing after relieving oneself) with water as taught in the Hanafi school. We learn the preferred hand usage and an important exception. The passage also expands on the rulings for entering a long passage or multiple connected mosques, highlighting the school's attention to detail in daily acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
State the main instruction: use the right hand to pour water and the left hand to wash the private parts.
This is the default sunnah method.
2
Note the exception
If the left hand has an excuse (e.g., injury), using the right hand for washing is permissible without dislike.
The ruling changes due to necessity.
3
Understand the reasoning
The left hand is designated for cleaning impurities; the right hand for pouring clean water, to avoid transferring filth.
This ensures cleanliness and respect.
4
Examine the commentary on entry etiquette
When entering a long passage leading to the toilet, one should initially put forward the left foot, but after that, any foot is permissible.
All parts of the passage are considered equally filthy.
5
Compare with mosque entry
For two connected mosques, enter the first with the right foot, then no special rule when moving between them as they are one entity.
Mosques are pure places; right foot preferred initially.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the proper method of istinja with water, followed by a commentary from al-Ramli on the etiquette of entering the toilet. The main ruling: one should pour water with the right hand and wash the private parts with the left hand, unless the left hand has an excuse (e.g., injury), in which case using the right hand is permissible without dislike. This is the standard Hanafi practice. Then the author quotes al-Ramli who clarifies a nuance: when entering a long passage leading to the toilet, one should initially enter with the left foot, but after that, any foot may be used because all parts are equally filthy. For two connected mosques, one should enter the first with the right foot, but then no special rule applies when moving between them since they are considered one entity. This commentary is based on Shafi'i sources but adopted by Hanafis. The text ends abruptly, possibly cut off in the source.

Key Terms
يفيض (yufīḍu): He pours water in a flowing manner.
الممر (al-mamar): A passage or hallway leading to the toilet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Entering the Lavatory: Supplication and Foot Placement
Toilet etiquette: entry supplication and foot placement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended supplication and foot placement when entering a lavatory, identify the disliked act of entering with a ring bearing Allah's name, and explain the commentary on foot placement for passageways.

Core Idea
Enter the lavatory with your head covered, left foot first, and recite the du'a seeking refuge from devils.

The fiqh of entering the lavatory is governed by sunnan (recommended acts) and makruhat (disliked acts). This lesson walks through the opening portion of our passage, which details the proper etiquette upon entry: covering the head, reciting a specific supplication, and using the left foot. It also addresses the disliked practice of entering with a ring bearing the name of Allah, and the commentary clarifies foot placement in passageways and mosques.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts upon entry
Read the opening lines: the student enters with head covered and recites a supplication. Note that this is sunnah, not wajib. Understand the meaning of 'al-khubth' and 'al-khaba'ith' as male and female devils.
The supplication is a well-known hadith.
2
Identify the disliked act of wearing a ring with Allah's name
The text states it is makruh to enter with such a ring. Understand that the dislike here is tanzihi (lightly disliked) because it is disrespectful to bring sacred names into a place of filth.
If the ring is covered or hidden, some say it is not makruh.
3
Analyze the foot placement rule
The base text says enter with the left foot. Then the commentary (al-Ramli) expands: for a long passageway, the left foot is only at the first entry; after that, no specific foot is required. For two connected mosques, enter with the right foot at the first mosque only, as they are considered one entity.
This is a classic example of sharh (commentary) refining a ruling.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider: a madrasa has a long hallway leading to the restroom. According to al-Ramli, when does one use the left foot? Only at the outermost door of the hallway. Inside the hallway, no specific foot placement is needed.
The same principle applies to sharing a passageway.

غير ثوبه الذي يصلي فيه إن كان له ذلك وإلا فيجتهد في حفظ ثوبه عن إصابة النجاسة والماء المستعمل، ويدخل مستور الرأس ويقول عند دخوله : باسم الله اللهم إني أعوذ بك من الخبث والخبائث، وأعوذ بك من الرجس الخبيث المخبث الشيطان الرجيم. والخبث بسكون الباء بمعنى الشر، وبضمها جمع الخبيث وهو الذكر من الشيطان والخبائث جمع الخبيثة وهي الأنثى من الشياطين. ويكره أن يدخل الخلاء ومعه خاتم مكتوب عليه اسم الله تعالى أو شيء من القرآن . ويبدأ برجله اليسرى ويقعد ولا يكشف عورته وهو قائم ويوسع بين رجليه ويميل على اليسرى، ولا يتكلم على الخلاء فإن الله تعالى يمقت على ذلك. والمقت هو البغض. ولا يذكر الله ولا يحمد إذا عطس، ولا يشمت عاطساً، ولا يرد السلام ولا يجيب المؤذن، ولا ينظر لعورته إلا لحاجة، ولا ينظر إلى ما يخرج منه ولا يبزق ولا يمخط، ولا يتنحنح، ولا يكثر الالتفات، ولا يعبث ببدنه، ولا يرفع بصره إلى السماء ولا يطيل القعود على البول والغائط لأنه يورث الباسور أو وجع الكبد كما روي عن لقمان عليه السلام، فإذا فرغ قام ويقول : الحمد لله الذي أذهب عني الأذى وعافاني أي بإبقاء شيء من الطعام لأنه لو خرج كله هلك . ويكره البول والغائط في الماء ولو كان جارياً، ويكره على طرف نهر أو بئر أو حوض أو عين أو تحت شجرة مثمرة أو في زرع أو في ظل ينتفع بالجلوس فيه، ويكره بجنب المساجد ومصلى العيد وفي المقابر وبين الدواب وفي طرق المسلمين ومستقبل القبلة ومستدبرها ولو في البنيان، فإن جلس مستقبل القبلة ناسياً ثم ذكر بعده أن أمكنه الانحراف انحرف وإلا فلا بأس. وكذا يكره للمرأة أن تمسك ولدها للبول والغائط نحو القبلة، واختلفوا في الاستقبال للتطهر فاختار التمرتاشي أنه لا يكره. وكذا يكره استقبال الشمس والقمر لأنهما من آيات الله الباهرة، ويكره أن يقعد في أسفل الأرض ويبول في أعلاها وأن يبول في مهب الريح وأن يبول في حجر فأرة أو حية أو نملة أو ثقب ويكره أن يبول قائماً أو مضطجعاً أو متجرداً عن ثوبه من غير عذر، فإن كان لعذر فلا بأس لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام بال قائماً لوجع في صلبه، ويكره أن يبول في موضع ويتوضأ أو يغتسل فيه للنهي، كذا في السراج الوهاج.
ويفيض الماء بيده اليمنى على فرجه ويعلي الإناء ويغسل فرجه بيده اليسرى إذا لم يكن عذر، فإن كان بيده اليسرى عذر يمنع من الاستنجاء بها جاز الاستنجاء باليمنى من غير كراهة .اهـ. فهو بحمد الله تعالى كما بحثته قوله: (ويكره أن يدخل الخلاء الخ) قال الرملي : وإذا دخل الخلاء وله ممر طويل يقدم اليسار عند أول دخول الممر ثم يتخير فيما بعد ذلك حتى في الجلوس على محل قضاء الحاجة لأن الكل أجزاء المستقذر، فلا يطلب تقديم خصوص اليسار في شيء منها. وفي مسجدين متصلين متنافذين يقدم اليمنى عند دخول أولهما ثم لا يراعي شيئاً بعد ذلك حتى في الدخول من أحدهما للآخر لأنهما شيء واحد. كذا رأيت في حاشية الشيخ عميرة والشيخ ابن قاسم على شرح المنهج الشافعي، ولا شيء
Book of Purity - Chapter of Impurities. Other than his garment in which he prays if he can afford it, otherwise he strives to protect his garment from being hit by impurity and used water. He enters with his head covered and says upon entering: 'Bismillah, Allahumma inni a'udhu bika min al-khubthi wa al-khaba'ith, and I seek refuge in You from the filthy, foul, defiling, accursed Satan.' Al-khubth (with sukun on ba) means evil, and with damm it is the plural of khabith which is the male of the devils, and al-khaba'ith is the plural of khabithah which is the female of the devils. It is disliked that he enter the lavatory with a ring on which is written the name of Allah or something from the Quran. He begins with his left foot, sits down, does not uncover his private part while standing, widens between his legs, leans on the left, does not speak in the lavatory for Allah hates that. Hating (al-maqt) is hatred. He does not remember Allah nor praise Him if he sneezes, does not respond to a sneezer, does not return the greeting, does not answer the mu'adhdhin, does not look at his private part except for need, does not look at what comes out of him, does not spit, does not blow his nose, does not clear his throat, does not look around much, does not play with his body, does not raise his gaze to the sky, and does not prolong sitting over urine and stool because that causes hemorrhoids or liver pain as narrated from Luqman, peace be upon him. When he finishes, he stands up and says: 'Alhamdulillah alladhi adhhaba 'anni al-adha wa 'afani' meaning by preserving some food because if all of it had come out he would have perished. Urination and defecation in water, even if flowing, is disliked; at the edge of a river, well, basin, spring, under a fruit-bearing tree, in a crop, in a shade used for sitting, near mosques and Eid prayer grounds, in graveyards, among animals, in Muslim roads, facing or turning one's back to the qibla, even if in a building, is disliked. If he sits facing the qibla forgetfully, then remembers, if he can turn he turns, otherwise no problem. Similarly, it is disliked for a woman to hold her child for urination or defecation towards the qibla. There is disagreement about facing the qibla for purification; al-Tamartashi chose that it is not disliked. Similarly, facing the sun and moon is disliked because they are among the clear signs of Allah. It is disliked to sit at the bottom of the ground and urinate at the top, to urinate in the direction of the wind, to urinate into a hole of a mouse, snake, ant, or any hole. It is disliked to urinate standing, lying down, or naked without an excuse; if there is an excuse, there is no harm because the Prophet (peace be upon him) urinated standing due to pain in his back. It is disliked to urinate in a place and then perform wudu or ghusl there, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. He pours water with his right hand over his private part, raises the vessel, and washes his private part with his left hand if there is no excuse. If there is an excuse in his left hand preventing istinja with it, istinja with the right hand is permissible without dislike. End. So it is, by Allah's praise, as I researched. His statement: (It is disliked to enter the lavatory). al-Ramli said: When entering a lavatory with a long passageway, he places his left foot first at the beginning of the passage, then he may choose after that, even when sitting to relieve himself, because all parts are areas of filth; so placing the left specifically is not required in any of them. In the case of two connected and interpenetrating mosques, he places his right foot when entering the first one, then does not need to consider anything after that, even when entering from one to the other, because they are one thing. Thus I saw in the footnote of Shaykh 'Umayrah and Shaykh Ibn Qasim on the commentary of al-Minhaj al-Shafi'i. Nothing more.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq lists the rulings and etiquettes related to entering the lavatory and relieving oneself. It begins with the recommended act of having a separate garment for prayer if possible, otherwise protecting the garment from impurities. The sunnah of covering the head upon entering the lavatory is mentioned, along with the specific supplication: 'Bismillah...' The meaning of al-khubth and al-khaba'ith is explained as the male and female devils. The passage then enumerates many disliked (makruh) actions: entering with a ring bearing Allah's name, entering with the left foot (though later the commentary clarifies that the left is placed first when entering the restroom itself, but not when entering a long passage), sitting without covering the private part, speaking, and many others. Health reasons are given for not prolonging the sitting. The phrase 'maqt' is explained as hatred. It also covers disliked places: in water, near fruit trees, in graveyards, facing the qibla, etc. An exception is made for one who forgetfully faces the qibla. For women, holding a child towards the qibla is disliked. The different view of al-Tamartashi on facing qibla for istinja is noted. The ruling on urinating standing is that it is disliked without an excuse, but permissible if there is an excuse, citing the Prophet's action. The method of istinja is described: pouring water with the right hand and washing with the left, but if the left hand has an excuse, the right may be used. Finally, al-Ramli's comment clarifies that the specific foot placement (left for entering restroom, right for entering mosque) applies only at the moment of first entry; after that, no special sequence is needed. The example of two connected mosques is given as a single entity.

Key Terms
الخلاء (al-khala'): The place for relieving oneself (lavatory).
الخبث (al-khubth): Evil; also plural of khabith (male devil) when pronounced with damm.
الخبائث (al-khaba'ith): Plural of khabithah, the female devils.
الممر (al-mamarr): Passageway or corridor leading to the lavatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Haram
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Wajib to remove

Key Takeaway
Entering the lavatory with proper etiquette (covering head, du'a, left foot first) is sunnah, while bringing objects bearing Allah's name is makruh.

Disliked Actions and Places While Relieving Oneself
List of disliked actions and places for relieving oneself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least five disliked actions and five disliked locations for relieving oneself, and identify the exception for forgetfulness regarding qibla.

Core Idea
Do not speak, face the qibla, or relieve yourself in water or under fruit trees; it is all makruh.

The passage now turns to a comprehensive list of actions and places that are disliked (makruh) during urination and defecation. These range from speaking and looking at one's private parts to relieving oneself in water, near mosques, or under fruit trees. The lesson will help you categorize these, understand the underlying reasons (like health and respect), and note the exception for forgetfulness regarding the qibla.

Guided Path
1
List the disliked actions
Read from 'لا يتكلم' to 'ولا يطيل القعود' and identify each disliked action. Group them: verbal (speaking, answering adhan), looking (at private parts, at what comes out), body movements (spitting, blowing nose, looking around), and postures (standing, lying down).
The reason for not speaking is that Allah hates it (maqt).
2
List the disliked places
Read from 'يكره البول والغائط في الماء' to 'وفي طرق المسلمين'. Categorize into: water sources (river, well, basin), cultivated areas (under fruit trees, in crops), public areas (mosques, Eid grounds, graveyards, roads), and facing/non-facing qibla.
Facing qibla is disliked even if in a building; there is no distinction.
3
Understand the exception for forgetfulness
If one sits facing qibla forgetfully, then remembers, he must turn away if possible. If not, it is excused.
This follows the general principle of excusing forgetfulness.
4
Identify the underlying reasons
Some have health reasons (prolonged sitting causes hemorrhoids), others are for respect (not facing qibla, not in mosques).
The wisdom behind the rulings preserves both physical and spiritual well-being.

كتاب الطهارة - باب الانجاس

غير ثوبه الذي يصلي فيه إن كان له ذلك وإلا فيجتهد في حفظ ثوبه عن إصابة النجاسة والماء المستعمل، ويدخل مستور الرأس ويقول عند دخوله : باسم الله اللهم إني أعوذ بك من الخبث والخبائث، وأعوذ بك من الرجس الخبيث المخبث الشيطان الرجيم. والخبث بسكون الباء بمعنى الشر، وبضمها جمع الخبيث وهو الذكر من الشيطان والخبائث جمع الخبيثة وهي الأنثى من الشياطين. ويكره أن يدخل الخلاء ومعه خاتم مكتوب عليه اسم الله تعالى أو شيء من القرآن . ويبدأ برجله اليسرى ويقعد ولا يكشف عورته وهو قائم ويوسع بين رجليه ويميل على اليسرى، ولا يتكلم على الخلاء فإن الله تعالى يمقت على ذلك. والمقت هو البغض. ولا يذكر الله ولا يحمد إذا عطس، ولا يشمت عاطساً، ولا يرد السلام ولا يجيب المؤذن، ولا ينظر لعورته إلا لحاجة، ولا ينظر إلى ما يخرج منه ولا يبزق ولا يمخط، ولا يتنحنح، ولا يكثر الالتفات، ولا يعبث ببدنه، ولا يرفع بصره إلى السماء ولا يطيل القعود على البول والغائط لأنه يورث الباسور أو وجع الكبد كما روي عن لقمان عليه السلام، فإذا فرغ قام ويقول : الحمد لله الذي أذهب عني الأذى وعافاني أي بإبقاء شيء من الطعام لأنه لو خرج كله هلك . ويكره البول والغائط في الماء ولو كان جارياً، ويكره على طرف نهر أو بئر أو حوض أو عين أو تحت شجرة مثمرة أو في زرع أو في ظل ينتفع بالجلوس فيه، ويكره بجنب المساجد ومصلى العيد وفي المقابر وبين الدواب وفي طرق المسلمين ومستقبل القبلة ومستدبرها ولو في البنيان، فإن جلس مستقبل القبلة ناسياً ثم ذكر بعده أن أمكنه الانحراف انحرف وإلا فلا بأس. وكذا يكره للمرأة أن تمسك ولدها للبول والغائط نحو القبلة، واختلفوا في الاستقبال للتطهر فاختار التمرتاشي أنه لا يكره. وكذا يكره استقبال الشمس والقمر لأنهما من آيات الله الباهرة، ويكره أن يقعد في أسفل الأرض ويبول في أعلاها وأن يبول في مهب الريح وأن يبول في حجر فأرة أو حية أو نملة أو ثقب ويكره أن يبول قائماً أو مضطجعاً أو متجرداً عن ثوبه من غير عذر، فإن كان لعذر فلا بأس لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام بال قائماً لوجع في صلبه، ويكره أن يبول في موضع ويتوضأ أو يغتسل فيه للنهي، كذا في السراج الوهاج.
ويفيض الماء بيده اليمنى على فرجه ويعلي الإناء ويغسل فرجه بيده اليسرى إذا لم يكن عذر، فإن كان بيده اليسرى عذر يمنع من الاستنجاء بها جاز الاستنجاء باليمنى من غير كراهة .اهـ. فهو بحمد الله تعالى كما بحثته قوله: (ويكره أن يدخل الخلاء الخ) قال الرملي : وإذا دخل الخلاء وله ممر طويل يقدم اليسار عند أول دخول الممر ثم يتخير فيما بعد ذلك حتى في الجلوس على محل قضاء الحاجة لأن الكل أجزاء المستقذر، فلا يطلب تقديم خصوص اليسار في شيء منها. وفي مسجدين متصلين متنافذين يقدم اليمنى عند دخول أولهما ثم لا يراعي شيئاً بعد ذلك حتى في الدخول من أحدهما للآخر لأنهما شيء واحد. كذا رأيت في حاشية الشيخ عميرة والشيخ ابن قاسم على شرح المنهج الشافعي، ولا شيء
Book of Purity - Chapter of Impurities. Other than his garment in which he prays if he can afford it, otherwise he strives to protect his garment from being hit by impurity and used water. He enters with his head covered and says upon entering: 'Bismillah, Allahumma inni a'udhu bika min al-khubthi wa al-khaba'ith, and I seek refuge in You from the filthy, foul, defiling, accursed Satan.' Al-khubth (with sukun on ba) means evil, and with damm it is the plural of khabith which is the male of the devils, and al-khaba'ith is the plural of khabithah which is the female of the devils. It is disliked that he enter the lavatory with a ring on which is written the name of Allah or something from the Quran. He begins with his left foot, sits down, does not uncover his private part while standing, widens between his legs, leans on the left, does not speak in the lavatory for Allah hates that. Hating (al-maqt) is hatred. He does not remember Allah nor praise Him if he sneezes, does not respond to a sneezer, does not return the greeting, does not answer the mu'adhdhin, does not look at his private part except for need, does not look at what comes out of him, does not spit, does not blow his nose, does not clear his throat, does not look around much, does not play with his body, does not raise his gaze to the sky, and does not prolong sitting over urine and stool because that causes hemorrhoids or liver pain as narrated from Luqman, peace be upon him. When he finishes, he stands up and says: 'Alhamdulillah alladhi adhhaba 'anni al-adha wa 'afani' meaning by preserving some food because if all of it had come out he would have perished. Urination and defecation in water, even if flowing, is disliked; at the edge of a river, well, basin, spring, under a fruit-bearing tree, in a crop, in a shade used for sitting, near mosques and Eid prayer grounds, in graveyards, among animals, in Muslim roads, facing or turning one's back to the qibla, even if in a building, is disliked. If he sits facing the qibla forgetfully, then remembers, if he can turn he turns, otherwise no problem. Similarly, it is disliked for a woman to hold her child for urination or defecation towards the qibla. There is disagreement about facing the qibla for purification; al-Tamartashi chose that it is not disliked. Similarly, facing the sun and moon is disliked because they are among the clear signs of Allah. It is disliked to sit at the bottom of the ground and urinate at the top, to urinate in the direction of the wind, to urinate into a hole of a mouse, snake, ant, or any hole. It is disliked to urinate standing, lying down, or naked without an excuse; if there is an excuse, there is no harm because the Prophet (peace be upon him) urinated standing due to pain in his back. It is disliked to urinate in a place and then perform wudu or ghusl there, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. He pours water with his right hand over his private part, raises the vessel, and washes his private part with his left hand if there is no excuse. If there is an excuse in his left hand preventing istinja with it, istinja with the right hand is permissible without dislike. End. So it is, by Allah's praise, as I researched. His statement: (It is disliked to enter the lavatory). al-Ramli said: When entering a lavatory with a long passageway, he places his left foot first at the beginning of the passage, then he may choose after that, even when sitting to relieve himself, because all parts are areas of filth; so placing the left specifically is not required in any of them. In the case of two connected and interpenetrating mosques, he places his right foot when entering the first one, then does not need to consider anything after that, even when entering from one to the other, because they are one thing. Thus I saw in the footnote of Shaykh 'Umayrah and Shaykh Ibn Qasim on the commentary of al-Minhaj al-Shafi'i. Nothing more.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq lists the rulings and etiquettes related to entering the lavatory and relieving oneself. It begins with the recommended act of having a separate garment for prayer if possible, otherwise protecting the garment from impurities. The sunnah of covering the head upon entering the lavatory is mentioned, along with the specific supplication: 'Bismillah...' The meaning of al-khubth and al-khaba'ith is explained as the male and female devils. The passage then enumerates many disliked (makruh) actions: entering with a ring bearing Allah's name, entering with the left foot (though later the commentary clarifies that the left is placed first when entering the restroom itself, but not when entering a long passage), sitting without covering the private part, speaking, and many others. Health reasons are given for not prolonging the sitting. The phrase 'maqt' is explained as hatred. It also covers disliked places: in water, near fruit trees, in graveyards, facing the qibla, etc. An exception is made for one who forgetfully faces the qibla. For women, holding a child towards the qibla is disliked. The different view of al-Tamartashi on facing qibla for istinja is noted. The ruling on urinating standing is that it is disliked without an excuse, but permissible if there is an excuse, citing the Prophet's action. The method of istinja is described: pouring water with the right hand and washing with the left, but if the left hand has an excuse, the right may be used. Finally, al-Ramli's comment clarifies that the specific foot placement (left for entering restroom, right for entering mosque) applies only at the moment of first entry; after that, no special sequence is needed. The example of two connected mosques is given as a single entity.

Key Terms
المقت (al-maqt): Hatred; extreme detestation.
الباسور (al-basur): Hemorrhoids.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a person do if he sits facing the qibla forgetfully and then remembers?
A) He should stop immediately and move away
B) He should turn if possible, otherwise continue
C) He must restart the act
D) He should not turn because it is too late

Key Takeaway
Avoid speaking, facing qibla, and using public or sacred spaces when relieving yourself; forgetfulness is excused.

Method of Istinja and Excusable Postures
Method of istinja and rulings on urination postures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the correct method of istinja, identify the disliked postures for urination (standing, lying down, naked), and state the exceptions when these are permissible.

Core Idea
Pour water with your right hand, wash with your left; urinate standing or naked only if excused.

The final part of our passage addresses the actual practice of cleaning (istinja) and the postures one should avoid while urinating. It details how to pour water and use the hands, and when it is permissible to urinate standing or without clothes. This lesson will help you distinguish between the recommended method and the disliked practices, and understand the role of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Learn the method of istinja
Read: 'ويُفيض الماء بيده اليمنى على فرجه ويُعلي الإناء ويغسل فرجه بيده اليسرى'. Note that the right hand holds the vessel, the left hand does the washing. This is the sunnah.
If the left hand has an excuse (e.g., broken), the right hand may be used without dislike.
2
Understand the disliked postures
The passage lists: urinating standing, lying down, or naked without an excuse. These are makruh. The evidence for the standing exception is the Prophet (PBUH) doing so due to back pain.
The dislike is tanzihi, but if there is an excuse, it is permissible.
3
Apply the rule: excuse vs. no excuse
Consider a scenario: a person has back pain and cannot squat. He may urinate standing. If no excuse, he should squat.
The example from the Prophet is a precedent (qiyas).
4
Note the additional disliked actions
The passage also mentions: urinating in a place where one later does wudu/ghusl, and urinating into holes (mouse, snake, etc.). These are separate rulings.
The hole prohibition is to avoid harming animals or disturbing them.

غير ثوبه الذي يصلي فيه إن كان له ذلك وإلا فيجتهد في حفظ ثوبه عن إصابة النجاسة والماء المستعمل، ويدخل مستور الرأس ويقول عند دخوله : باسم الله اللهم إني أعوذ بك من الخبث والخبائث، وأعوذ بك من الرجس الخبيث المخبث الشيطان الرجيم. والخبث بسكون الباء بمعنى الشر، وبضمها جمع الخبيث وهو الذكر من الشيطان والخبائث جمع الخبيثة وهي الأنثى من الشياطين. ويكره أن يدخل الخلاء ومعه خاتم مكتوب عليه اسم الله تعالى أو شيء من القرآن . ويبدأ برجله اليسرى ويقعد ولا يكشف عورته وهو قائم ويوسع بين رجليه ويميل على اليسرى، ولا يتكلم على الخلاء فإن الله تعالى يمقت على ذلك. والمقت هو البغض. ولا يذكر الله ولا يحمد إذا عطس، ولا يشمت عاطساً، ولا يرد السلام ولا يجيب المؤذن، ولا ينظر لعورته إلا لحاجة، ولا ينظر إلى ما يخرج منه ولا يبزق ولا يمخط، ولا يتنحنح، ولا يكثر الالتفات، ولا يعبث ببدنه، ولا يرفع بصره إلى السماء ولا يطيل القعود على البول والغائط لأنه يورث الباسور أو وجع الكبد كما روي عن لقمان عليه السلام، فإذا فرغ قام ويقول : الحمد لله الذي أذهب عني الأذى وعافاني أي بإبقاء شيء من الطعام لأنه لو خرج كله هلك . ويكره البول والغائط في الماء ولو كان جارياً، ويكره على طرف نهر أو بئر أو حوض أو عين أو تحت شجرة مثمرة أو في زرع أو في ظل ينتفع بالجلوس فيه، ويكره بجنب المساجد ومصلى العيد وفي المقابر وبين الدواب وفي طرق المسلمين ومستقبل القبلة ومستدبرها ولو في البنيان، فإن جلس مستقبل القبلة ناسياً ثم ذكر بعده أن أمكنه الانحراف انحرف وإلا فلا بأس. وكذا يكره للمرأة أن تمسك ولدها للبول والغائط نحو القبلة، واختلفوا في الاستقبال للتطهر فاختار التمرتاشي أنه لا يكره. وكذا يكره استقبال الشمس والقمر لأنهما من آيات الله الباهرة، ويكره أن يقعد في أسفل الأرض ويبول في أعلاها وأن يبول في مهب الريح وأن يبول في حجر فأرة أو حية أو نملة أو ثقب ويكره أن يبول قائماً أو مضطجعاً أو متجرداً عن ثوبه من غير عذر، فإن كان لعذر فلا بأس لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام بال قائماً لوجع في صلبه، ويكره أن يبول في موضع ويتوضأ أو يغتسل فيه للنهي، كذا في السراج الوهاج.
ويفيض الماء بيده اليمنى على فرجه ويعلي الإناء ويغسل فرجه بيده اليسرى إذا لم يكن عذر، فإن كان بيده اليسرى عذر يمنع من الاستنجاء بها جاز الاستنجاء باليمنى من غير كراهة .اهـ. فهو بحمد الله تعالى كما بحثته قوله: (ويكره أن يدخل الخلاء الخ) قال الرملي : وإذا دخل الخلاء وله ممر طويل يقدم اليسار عند أول دخول الممر ثم يتخير فيما بعد ذلك حتى في الجلوس على محل قضاء الحاجة لأن الكل أجزاء المستقذر، فلا يطلب تقديم خصوص اليسار في شيء منها. وفي مسجدين متصلين متنافذين يقدم اليمنى عند دخول أولهما ثم لا يراعي شيئاً بعد ذلك حتى في الدخول من أحدهما للآخر لأنهما شيء واحد. كذا رأيت في حاشية الشيخ عميرة والشيخ ابن قاسم على شرح المنهج الشافعي، ولا شيء

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq lists the rulings and etiquettes related to entering the lavatory and relieving oneself. It begins with the recommended act of having a separate garment for prayer if possible, otherwise protecting the garment from impurities. The sunnah of covering the head upon entering the lavatory is mentioned, along with the specific supplication: 'Bismillah...' The meaning of al-khubth and al-khaba'ith is explained as the male and female devils. Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja'): Washing the private parts after relieving oneself.
محل الوضوء (mahall al-wudu): Place where one performs wudu or ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on urinating standing if there is an excuse (e.g., back pain)?
A) Still makruh
B) Permissible without dislike
C) Recommended (sunnah)
D) Prohibited

Key Takeaway
Perform istinja with the right hand pouring and left hand washing; urinate standing or naked only if excused.

Definition of Fay' and Determination of Zawal
Defines fay' linguistically and explains how to determine noon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-fay' and al-zill, and describe the Hanafi method for determining zawal using a gnomon and bodily measurement.

Core Idea
The shadow after zawal is called fay' because it returns; its onset is known by the shadow lengthening after it stops shortening.

Knowing the precise moment of zawal (the sun’s meridian) is essential for the timing of Zuhr and Asr prayers. This passage from Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the technical language used for shadows and provides a reliable empirical method to determine noon. It also addresses a key exception for Makkah and Madinah.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish fay' from zill linguistically
Identify that fay' is the shadow after zawal (afternoon), while zill is the shadow before zawal (morning). The term fay' literally means 'return' because the shadow returns from west to east.
This distinction prevents confusion in prayer timing.
2
Understand the gnomon method
A straight stick is planted in level ground. Mark the tip of its shadow. Observe: if the shadow shortens, the sun has not reached zenith; if it lengthens, it has passed. When the shadow remains still, that is the moment of zawal.
This is the most authentic narration according to the text.
3
Note the bodily substitute and measurement dispute
If no stick is available, use one's own height. There is a disagreement: al-Tahawi and most scholars say 7 feet, while others say 6.5 feet. The author reconciles by measuring from different parts of the foot.
This shows the Hanafi approach to resolving minor differences.
4
Identify the exception for Makkah and Madinah
At the longest day of the year, the sun in Makkah and Madinah takes all four walls, meaning no distinct shadow appears at zawal. This is a special case.
Thus the gnomon method may not apply there on that specific day.
5
Appreciate the precision of prayer timing
These detailed observations reflect the Hanafi commitment to accurate prayer times, ensuring that acts of worship are performed within their prescribed windows.
This is part of the broader fiqh of taharah and salat.

ليكون مؤدياً للصلاتين في وقتهما بالإجماع. كذا في السراج وفي المغرب: الفيء بوزن الشيء ما نسخ الشمس وذلك بالعشي والجمع أفياء ،وفيوء والظل ما نسخته الشمس وذلك بالغداة. وفي السراج الوهاج والفيء في اللغة اسم للظل بعد الزوال سمي فيأ لأنه فاء من جهة المغرب إلى جهة المشرق أي رجع وبه اندفع ما قيل إن الفيء هو الظل الذي يكون للأشياء وقت الزوال. وفي معرفة الزوال روايات أصحها أن يغرز خشبة مستوية في أرض مستوية ويجعل عند منتهى ظلها ،علامة فإن كان الظل ينقص عن العلامة فالشمس لم تزل، وإن كان الظل يطول ويجاوز الخط علم أنها زالت وإن امتنع الظل من القصر والطول فهو وقت الزوال. كذا في الظهيرية. وفي المجتبى : فإن لم يجد ما يغرزه لمعرفة الفيء والأمثال فليعتبره بقامته، وقامة كل انسان ستة أقدام ونصف بقدمه. وقال الطحاوي وعامة المشايخ : سبعة أقدام ويمكن الجمع بينهما بأن يعتبر سبعة أقدام من طرف سمت الساق، وستة ونصف من طرف الإبهام واعلم أن لكل شيء ظلاً وقت الزوال إلا بمكة والمدينة في أطول أيام السنة لأن الشمس فيها تأخذ الحيطان الأربعة. كذا في المبسوط.
So that he becomes one who performs both prayers in their times by consensus. Thus in al-Siraj. And in al-Mughrib: al-fay', with the weight of shay', is what the sun copies over, and that is in the afternoon; its plural is afiya' and fuyu'. And al-zill is what the sun copies over, and that is in the morning. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: al-fay' in language is a name for the shadow after zawal; it is called fay' because it returns from the west side to the east side, i.e., it came back. And by this is repelled what was said that al-fay' is the shadow that belongs to things at the time of zawal. And concerning knowing zawal, there are narrations; the most authentic is that one plants a straight stick in level ground and makes a mark at the end of its shadow. If the shadow decreases from the mark, then the sun has not passed its zenith; if the shadow lengthens and passes the line, one knows that it has passed; and if the shadow refrains from shortening and lengthening, that is the time of zawal. Thus in al-Zahiriyya. And in al-Mujtaba: if one does not find something to plant to know al-fay' and the like, then he should estimate it by his stature. The stature of every human is six and a half feet by his foot. And al-Tahawi and the majority of mashayikh said: seven feet. And reconciliation between them is possible by considering seven feet from the tip of the shin and six and a half from the tip of the big toe. And know that everything has a shadow at the time of zawal except Makkah and Madinah at the longest day of the year, because the sun there takes all four walls. Thus in al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of al-Kanz dealing with the definition of fay' and the method of determining zawal (midday). The author begins by explaining the linguistic distinction between fay' and zill: fay' is the shadow after zawal, while zill is the shadow before zawal. He cites the return (fay' meaning 'to return') as the reason for its name, refuting the notion that fay' refers to the shadow at the exact moment of zawal. The method for determining zawal involves planting a straight stick in level ground and marking the end of its shadow; if the shadow then shortens, the sun has not yet reached its zenith; if it lengthens beyond the mark, it has passed. When the shadow does not change, that is the moment of zawal. If a stick is unavailable, one may use his own height. There is a difference regarding the number of feet: al-Tahawi and most scholars say seven feet, while others say six and a half; the author reconciles by attributing six and a half to the tip of the big toe and seven to the shin. An exception is noted for Makkah and Madinah during the longest day, where shadow may not appear due to the sun's angle. This passage provides a practical method for prayer timing.

Key Terms
الفيء (al-fay'): The shadow after zawal (noon) that returns from west to east.
الظل (al-zill): The shadow before zawal, cast by the sun in the morning.
الزوال (al-zawal): The moment when the sun passes its zenith, indicated by the shadow starting to lengthen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the most authentic method for determining zawal?
A) Using a digital watch
B) Planting a straight stick and observing the shadow
C) Looking directly at the sun
D) Asking the local imam

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines fay' precisely as the post‑zawal shadow and provides an empirical gnomon method to determine the moment of zawal for accurate prayer timing.

Taharah — Purification

The Prohibition of Voluntary Prayer After Dawn and Before Maghrib
Commentary on the matn's ruling on prohibited times for nafl prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing nafl prayers after the break of dawn and before Maghrib, cite the primary hadith evidence, and explain the legal reasoning for makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
No voluntary prayer after dawn except the two rak'ahs of Fajr—the prohibition is strong, making it makruh tahrimi.

The source passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a key fiqh question: when is it forbidden to perform voluntary (nafl) prayers? The matn lists several prohibited times, and the commentary focuses on two: after dawn (more than the sunnah) and before Maghrib. The ruling is based on explicit hadith and is consistently held in the Hanafi school, though its application to before Maghrib is disputed by other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Prohibited Times
Extract from the text the two specific times: after the break of dawn (excluding the two sunnah rak'ahs) and before the Maghrib prayer. Note that the prohibition also applies after Asr (implied elsewhere).
The matn explicitly states 'after dawn more than the sunnah of Fajr' and 'before Maghrib'.
2
Quote the Hadith Evidence
The commentary cites two hadiths: 'No prayer after dawn except two rak'ahs' and 'When dawn appears, do not pray except two rak'ahs.' These are narrated by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and al-Tabarani.
These are ahad hadith, so their thubut is zanni, but they are accepted as evidence for prohibition.
3
Apply the Hanafi Principle
In Hanafi usul, a general prohibition (nahy) indicates karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibitively disliked) when the evidence does not reach the level of haram. The hadith's wording 'لا صلاة' is interpreted as a strong prohibition, not absolute nullity.
The prohibition applies to all voluntary prayers, including greeting the mosque and vowed prayers, but excludes missed obligatory prayers (qada).
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Dispute
The prohibition before Maghrib is contested. The Shafi'i school considers it recommended (mustahabb) to pray two rak'ahs before Maghrib based on weak hadith. The Hanafi position relies on the practice of Ibn Umar, who did not see anyone pray at that time in the Prophet's era.
The text mentions that the dislike is not established for before Maghrib unless another evidence indicates it, but the madhhab follows the apparent meaning of the hadith.

كتاب الصلاة
وصلاة جنازة وبعد طلوع الفجر بأكثر من سنة الفجر وقبل المغرب ووقت الخطبة وعن الجمع بين الصلاتين في وقت بعذر .
سبب بقية الواجبات من الصلاة داخل في النفل فيكره فيهما كالمنذور خلافاً لأبي يوسف، وما شرع فيه من النفل ثم أفسده وركعتي الطواف لأن ما التزمه بالنذر نفل لأن النذر سبب موضوع لالتزامه بخلاف سجود التلاوة لأنها ليست بنفل لأن التنفل بالسجدة غير مشروع فيكون واجباً بإيجاب الله تعالى، ولأنه تعلق وجوب النذر بسبب من جهته وسجدة التلاوة بإيجابه تعالى وإن كانت التلاوة فعله كجمع المال فعله ووجوب الزكاة بإيجاب الشرع. وفي فتح القدير : وقد يقال : وجوب السجدة في التحقيق متعلق بالسماع لا بالاستماع ولا التلاوة، وذلك ليس فعلاً من المكلف بل وصف خلق فيه بخلاف النذر والطواف والشروع فعله ولولاه لكانت الصلاة نفلاً اهـ. وهو قاصر على السامع للتلاوة لأن السبب في حقه السماع على خلاف فيه، وأما التالي فاتفقوا على أن السبب في حقه إنما هو التلاوة لا السماع وأطلق في التنفل فشمل ماله وما ليس له، فتكره تحية المسجد فيهما للعموم وهو مقدم على عموم قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «من دخل المسجد فليركع ركعتين» لأنه مبيح وذلك حاظر . وأشار إلى أنه لو شرع في النفل في وقت مستحب ثم قضاه فيهما فإنه لا يسقط عن ذمته كما في المحيط، وإلى أنه لو أفسد سنة الفجر ثم قضاها بعد صلاة الفجر فإنه لا يجوز على الأصح . وقيل يجوز والأحسن أن يشرع في السنة ثم يكبر بالفريضة فلا يكون مفسداً للعمل ويكون منتقلاً من عمل إلى عمل. كذا في الظهيرية وفيه نظر، لأنه إذا كبر للفريضة فقد أفسد السنة كما صرحوا به في باب ما يفسد الصلاة. وفي شرح المجمع لابن الملك : ما قاله بعض الفقهاء من أنه إذا أقيم للفجر وخاف رجل فوت الفرض يشرع في السنة فيقطعها فيقضيها قبل الطلوع مردود لكراهة قضاء التنفل الذي أفسده فيه على أن الأمر بالشروع للقطع قبيح شرعاً، وإلى أنه لا يكره التنفل قبل صلاة العصر في وقته، وإلى أن لصلاة العصر مدخلاً في كراهة النوافل فينشأ عنه كراهة التطوع بعد العصر المجموعة إلى الظهر في وقت الظهر بعرفات فيما يظهر، ولم أقف على التصريح به لأحد من أهل المذهب. كذا في شرح منية المصلي. واعلم أن قضاء الفائتة وما معها لا تكره بعد صلاة العصر إلى غاية التغير لا إلى الغروب كما هو ظاهر كلامه .

قال :
وفي التبيين حيث قال: والمراد بما بعد العصر قبل تغير الشمس، وأما بعده فلا يجوز فيه القضاء أيضاً وإن كان قبل أن يصلي العصر اهـ. على أنه يخالف كلام المصنف أولاً حيث قال : ومنع عن الصلاة وصلاة الجنازة وسجدة التلاوة عند الطلوع والاستواء والغروب وقد قدم أن المراد بالغروب التغير . وفي الشرنبلالية عند قول الدرر : إلا في وقت الاحمرار فإن القضاء فيه مكروه. أقول: ظاهره الصحة مع الكراهة فيناقض ما قدمه من قوله لا تصح صلاة الخ ويخالفه ما قاله الزيلعي الخ. ثم قلت ولا يقال إنه لا مخالفة لحمل نفي الجواز على الحل لأن المراد به عدم الصحة كما تقرر في مسألة الكافر إذا أسلم والصبي إذا بلغ في الوقت المكروه فلم يؤد حتى خرج الوقت فإنه لا قضاء ما يصح فات في وقت مكروه مثله لأن ما ثبت كامل لعدم نقص في الوقت نفسه فلا يخرج عن عهدته إلا بكامل كما في فتح القدير. فمن خوطب بالصلاة من أول وقتها فلم يؤدها حتى خرج الوقت حكمه كذلك بالأولى. وما وقع في الهداية من قوله ويكره أن يتنفل بعد الفجر حتى تطلع الشمس وبعد العصر حتى تغرب ولا بأس بأن يصلي في هذين الوقتين الفوائت ليس على ظاهره لما قال في شرح
Book of Prayer. And the funeral prayer and after dawn more than the sunnah of dawn and before maghrib and the time of the khutbah and about combining two prayers in one time due to an excuse. The reason: the remaining obligations from prayer are included in voluntary prayer, so it is disliked in both, like the vowed prayer, contrary to Abu Yusuf. And what one begins as voluntary then spoils it, and the two rak'ahs of tawaf, because what one undertakes by vow is voluntary, because the vow is a cause placed for undertaking it, unlike the prostration of recitation because it is not voluntary, because performing voluntary prostration is not legislated, so it becomes obligatory by the command of Allah the Exalted. And because the obligation of the vow is attached to a cause from his side, while the prostration of recitation is by His command, even if recitation is his action, like collecting wealth is his action and the obligation of zakat is by the command of the Law. And in Fath al-Qadir: It may be said that the obligation of prostration in reality is attached to hearing, not to listening or recitation, and that is not an action of the responsible person but rather a description created in him, unlike the vow, tawaf, and beginning an action, otherwise the prayer would be voluntary. It is restricted to the hearer of the recitation because the cause in his case is hearing, with a difference of opinion. As for the reciter, they agree that the cause in his case is only recitation, not hearing. And it (the text) spoke generally about voluntary prayer, so it includes what is for him and what is not for him. So greeting the mosque is disliked in both due to generality, and it takes precedence over the general meaning of his statement, peace be upon him, 'Whoever enters the mosque, let him pray two rak'ahs' because it (the first) permits and that (the second) prohibits. And he indicated that if one begins a voluntary prayer in a recommended time and then makes it up at these times, it does not fall from his responsibility, as in al-Muhit. And that if one spoils the sunnah of fajr and then makes it up after the fajr prayer, it is not permissible according to the most sound opinion. And it is said it is permissible, and the best is to start the sunnah and then say takbir for the obligatory prayer, so it is not spoiling the action and he moves from one action to another. This is in al-Zahiriya, but there is a problem with it, because when he says takbir for the obligatory prayer, he has spoiled the sunnah, as they explicitly stated in the chapter on what invalidates prayer. And in Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn al-Malik: What some jurists said that if the iqama for fajr is given and a man fears missing the obligatory prayer, he should start the sunnah and then cut it off and make it up before sunrise is rejected because of the dislike of making up a voluntary prayer that he spoiled, and because the command to start for the sake of cutting is repugnant in law. And that voluntary prayer before asr in its time is not disliked. And that the asr prayer has an entry in the dislike of voluntary prayers, which leads to the dislike of supererogatory prayer after asr combined with zuhr in the time of zuhr at Arafat, as it appears, but I have not come across an explicit statement of it from anyone of the madhhab. This is in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And know that making up a missed prayer and what is with it is not disliked after asr until the change (of the sun), not until sunset, as is apparent from his words. Then: His statement: (And after dawn more than the sunnah of fajr) meaning He prohibited voluntary prayer after dawn because restricting it to voluntary suffices, and this is very subtle so reflect on it, because through it one can dispense with removing voluntary from its legal meaning, since they have defined it as an action that is not obligatory, not mandatory, and not sunnah. His statement: (And he indicated) the indication is not apparent, consider. His statement: (And I have not come across an explicit statement by anyone) Al-Nahr said: This is strange, for in Fath al-Qadir is written: Some mentioned that one should not perform voluntary prayer after the combined prayer at Arafa and Muzdalifa, and it was attributed in al-Mi'raj to al-Mujtaba, and in al-Quniya to Majd al-A'imma al-Turjumani and Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani. His statement: (And know that making up missed prayer) contradicts what is before fajr more than its sunnah intentionally, because of what Ahmad and Abu Dawud narrated: 'No prayer after dawn except two rak'ahs' and in the narration of al-Tabarani: 'When dawn appears, do not pray except two rak'ahs.' We restricted it with intentional based on what is in al-Zahiriya. And if one began supererogatory prayer before dawn and when he prayed one rak'ah dawn appeared, it is said he should cut the prayer, and it is said he should complete it, and the most sound is that he completes it, and it does not substitute for the sunnah of fajr according to the most sound. And if the author had sufficed with saying 'And about voluntary prayer after dawn more than its sunnah and after asr', it would have sufficed him from elaboration, as is clear. And he came with fajr a second time apparently and did not say with its sunnah implicitly because 'sunnah of fajr' is not in the sense of time; rather it is the sunnah of the fajr prayer, so it is on the omission of a genitive, i.e., more than the sunnah of the fajr prayer. And in al-Mujtaba: Recitation in the two rak'ahs of fajr should be made light. He restricted it to voluntary because making up a missed prayer after dawn is not disliked, because the prohibition of voluntary at that time is for the right of the two rak'ahs of fajr so that he becomes like one occupied with them, because the time is specifically assigned to them, so that even if he intends supererogatory, it becomes fajr without his specification, so it does not appear regarding the obligatory because it is above it. And the prior research of Ibn al-Humam applies here due to the prohibition we mentioned in the previous issue. And in al-'Inaya: The conclusion is that where the prohibition is due to a meaning in the time, it affects both obligations and voluntary prayers, and where it is due to a meaning other than the time, it affects voluntary prayers without obligations, and what is in its meaning. His statement: (And before maghrib) meaning He prohibited voluntary prayer after sunset before the maghrib prayer because of what Abu Dawud narrated: Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, was asked about the two rak'ahs before maghrib and said: 'I have not seen anyone in the time of the Messenger of Allah praying them.' This implies the negation of recommendation. As for the establishment of dislike, no, unless another evidence indicates it. And what was mentioned about the implication of delaying maghrib, we have already mentioned from al-Quniya the exception of a little, and the two rak'ahs do not exceed a little if one is lenient in them. He said: And in al-Tabyin: The meaning of after asr is before the change of the sun, and after that, making up is also not permissible even if before praying asr. This contradicts the author's statement initially where he said: He prohibited prayer, funeral prayer, and prostration of recitation at sunrise, zenith, and sunset, and it was previously mentioned that by sunset is meant the change. And in al-Sharnabalaliya, regarding the statement of al-Durar: Except at the time of redness, making up then is disliked. I say: Its apparent meaning is validity with dislike, which contradicts what he previously said that prayer is not valid, and contradicts what al-Zayla'i said. Then I said: It cannot be said there is no contradiction by interpreting the negation of permissibility as permissibility, because what is meant is lack of validity, as established in the issue of the disbeliever who becomes Muslim and the boy who reaches puberty in a disliked time and does not perform until the time passes, then there is no making up because what became invalid in a disliked time is like it, because what was established was complete due to no deficiency in the time itself, so he cannot be discharged except by the complete, as in Fath al-Qadir. So the one who is addressed with prayer from the beginning of its time and does not perform it until the time leaves, his ruling is likewise by priority. And what occurred in al-Hidaya: 'It is disliked to perform voluntary prayer after fajr until the sun rises and after asr until it sets, and there is no problem with performing missed prayers in these two times' is not according to its apparent meaning, because of what was said in the commentary.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the ruling on performing voluntary prayers (nafl) in certain prohibited times: after dawn (fajr) more than the sunnah of fajr, before maghrib, and after asr (implied). The author begins by noting that the matn lists several prohibited times: funeral prayer (already covered), after fajr, before maghrib, during khutbah, and combining prayers due to excuse. The commentary then explains the reasoning: the remaining obligations of prayer (like vowed prayers) are included in the category of nafl, so they are disliked (makruh) at these times, contrary to Abu Yusuf's view that vowed prayers are separate. The discussion extends to other issues: the nature of prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah) as obligatory not nafl, the ruling on making up a spoiled nafl, and the dislike of greeting the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid) during these times due to the general prohibition overriding the general command. The author then delves into the specific prohibition after fajr, quoting hadith from Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and al-Tabarani: 'No prayer after dawn except two rak'ahs' and 'When dawn appears, do not pray except two rak'ahs.' The prohibition applies to intentional voluntary prayer, not to make-up (qada) of missed obligatory prayers, which is not disliked because the prohibition targets the sunnah of fajr itself. Similarly, voluntary prayer before maghrib is prohibited because of the practice of Ibn Umar not seeing anyone pray at that time, though the mention of dislike requires further evidence. The commentary also addresses the ruling on qada after asr, noting that it is not disliked until the change of the sun (yellowing), not until sunset, and clarifies potential contradictions in earlier texts. Overall, the passage reinforces the Hanafi principle that voluntary prayers are prohibited at these specific times, with exceptions for missed obligations and certain compensations.

Key Terms
التنفل (al-tanafful): Voluntary, supererogatory prayer beyond the obligatory and sunnah prayers.
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of sunnah prayer before the obligatory Fajr prayer.
المكروه (al-makruh): Disliked; an action that is not haram but carries a promise of reward for leaving and no sin for doing, or sin if near prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing the greeting of the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid) after the Fajr prayer?
A) Permissible and recommended because it is a specific sunnah.
B) Prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) because it is a nafl prayer at a prohibited time.
C) Haram and the prayer is invalid.
D) Permissible only if it is performed before the sun rises.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayer after dawn (except the sunnah of Fajr) and before Maghrib is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi), based on explicit hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Sunnahs of the Adhan: Turning, Fingers, and Tathwib
Explains sunnahs of adhan including turning, fingers, tathwib, and the proof for stationary feet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts of the adhan according to the Hanafi school and explain the proof for remaining stationary while turning.

Core Idea
The mu'adhdhin turns his upper body without moving his feet, as commanded by the Prophet.

The adhan is a sunnah mu'akkadah, and there are specific recommended actions that the mu'adhdhin should observe. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq enumerates several sunnahs, including turning in the minaret, placing fingers in the ears, tathwib, and sitting between adhan and iqamah in Maghrib. It also clarifies the correct method of turning based on a hadith from Bilal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah acts
List the sunnah acts mentioned: turning in the minaret, placing fingers in ears, tathwib, and sitting between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib. Note the correct phrasing for 'as-salat' and 'al-falah' on right and left.
2
Understand the ruling on turning
The mu'adhdhin should turn his upper body (iltifat) but not move his feet. This is sunnah. The text restricts turning because feet must stay stationary.
3
Analyze the dalil
The hadith from al-Daraqutni via Bilal: 'The Messenger of Allah ordered us, when we call the adhan or iqamah, not to move our feet from their places.' This proves that only upper body turning is allowed.
The hadith is ahad (zanni thubut) but its meaning (dalala) is clear (qati) in prohibiting foot movement.
4
Examine the ikhtilaf on iqamah
There are three views: (1) turn in iqamah as well (al-Ghunya), (2) do not turn because iqamah is for present attendees (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj), (3) turn if the mosque is spacious. The hadith applies to both adhan and iqamah, so the first view is stronger.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that turning the upper body without moving feet is sunnah for both adhan and iqamah, based on the literal command of the hadith.
Some later Hanafi scholars prefer not turning in iqamah, but the hadith is explicit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستدير في صومعته ويجعل أصبعه في أذنيه ويثوب ويجلس بينهما في المغرب ويؤذن الصحيح خلافاً لمن قال إن الصلاة باليمين والشمال والفلاح كذلك وفي فتح القدير: إنه الأوجه ولم يبين وجهه . وقيد بالالتفات لأنه لا يحول قدميه لما رواه الدارقطني عن بلال قال : أمرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا أذنا أو أقمنا أن لا نزيل أقدامنا عن مواضعها. وأطلق في الالتفات ولم يقيده بالأذان وقدمنا عن الغنية أنه يحول في الإقامة أيضاً. وفي السراج الوهاج : لا يحول فيها لأنها لإعلام الحاضرين بخلاف الأذان فإنه إعلام للغائبين، وقيل يحوّل إذا كان الموضع متسعاً. قوله (ويستدير في صومعته يعنى إن لم يتم الإعلام بتحويل وجهه مع ثبات قدميه فإنه يستدير في المئذنة ليحصل التمام والصومعة المنارة وهي في الأصل متعبد الراهب. ذكره العيني. ولم يكن في زمنه ل مئذنة لكن روى أبو داود من حديث عروة بن الزبير عن امرأة من بني النجار قالت: كان بيتي من أطول بيت بحول المسجد فكان بلال يأتي بسحر فيجلس عليه ينظر إلى الفجر، فإذا رآه أذن . وفي القنية : يؤذن المؤذن فتعوي الكلاب فله ضربها إن ظن أنها تمتنع بضربه وإلا فلا.
He turns around in his minaret and puts his fingers in his ears and performs tathwib and sits between them in Maghrib and gives the adhan - the correct view, contrary to whoever said 'as-salat' to the right and left and 'al-falah' likewise. In Fath al-Qadir: it is the most appropriate and he did not explain his reasoning. He restricted it to turning because he does not move his feet, due to what al-Daraqutni narrated from Bilal who said: The Messenger of Allah ordered us, when we call the adhan or iqamah, not to move our feet from their places. He made it absolute in turning and did not restrict it to the adhan, and we previously transmitted from al-Ghunya that he turns in iqamah as well. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: he does not turn in it because it is for informing those present, unlike the adhan which is for informing those absent. And it was said he turns if the place is spacious. His statement: (He turns around in his minaret) means if notifying is not completed by turning his face while keeping his feet stationary, then he turns around in the minaret to achieve completion. 'Sawma'a' is the minaret, originally the hermit's place of worship. Mentioned by al-'Ayni. There was no minaret in his time, but Abu Dawud narrated from the hadith of 'Urwa ibn al-Zubayr from a woman of Bani al-Najjar who said: My house was the tallest house around the mosque, so Bilal would come at dawn and sit on it looking for dawn, and when he saw it he would call the adhan. In al-Qunyah: The mu'adhdhin calls the adhan and dogs bark, so he may hit them if he thinks they will stop by his hitting; otherwise he should not.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the sunnan (recommended acts) of the adhan. It begins by listing some sunnahs: the mu'adhdhin should turn in the minaret (i.e. rotate his body to face different directions), place his fingers in his ears, perform tathwib (saying 'as-salat khayr min al-nawm' in the Fajr adhan), and sit between the adhan and iqamah for Maghrib. The correct view is that he says 'as-salat' and 'al-falah' on the right and left respectively, though some disagree. The author then discusses the ruling on turning the body: the mu'adhdhin should not move his feet from their place; rather, he turns his upper body. This is based on a hadith from al-Daraqutni via Bilal that the Prophet commanded not to move the feet during adhan or iqamah. However, there is a difference of opinion whether turning is also done in the iqamah. The author mentions three views: from al-Ghunya that he turns; from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that he does not, because iqamah is for those already present; and a third that he turns if the mosque is spacious. Next, the passage explains that if turning the face is insufficient for conveying the call, the mu'adhdhin should physically rotate in the minaret. The word 'sawma'a' is clarified: it originally means a monk's cell, but here refers to the minaret. A historical note is added: there was no minaret in the Prophet's time; Bilal would call the adhan from the roof of a tall house, as narrated by Abu Dawud. Finally, a practical ruling is given from al-Qunyah: if dogs bark during the adhan, the mu'adhdhin may beat them if he believes they will stop; otherwise he should not. This shows that adhan should be performed without disturbance, but the mu'adhdhin has limited authority to handle nuisance.

Key Terms
صومعة (sawma'a): The minaret from which the adhan is called; originally a monk's cell.
التفات (iltifat): Turning the face or upper body to the right and left while delivering the adhan.
تثويب (tathwib): Saying 'as-salat khayr min al-nawm' in the Fajr adhan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is mustahabb to move them
B) The mu'adhdhin should not move his feet from their place
C) He must walk in a circle
D) Only the Imam may move his feet

Key Takeaway
The mu'adhdhin should turn his upper body without moving his feet during adhan, based on the Prophet's command.

Ruling on Dogs Barking During the Adhan
Provides a conditional ruling on hitting dogs that bark during adhan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on hitting dogs that bark during the adhan according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A mu'adhdhin may hit dogs only if he believes it will stop them; otherwise, he should not.

The adhan is a sacred call, and the mu'adhdhin should be able to deliver it without disturbance. A short ruling in al-Qunyah addresses the situation where dogs bark during the adhan. It provides a conditional permission to strike them, but only if it is likely to be effective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The mu'adhdhin is calling the adhan, and dogs start barking, potentially disrupting the call.
2
State the ruling
The mu'adhdhin may hit the dogs if he believes (zann) that hitting will make them stop. If he does not think it will work, he should not hit them.
The ruling is conditional on effectiveness.
3
Understand the reasoning
The permission is granted to remove a disturbance from the adhan. However, hitting without benefit is not allowed because it would be pointless and potentially cruel.
This is a practical ruling based on necessity.

Ruling on the Adhan of the Junub and Five Situations Requiring Restart
Expanding the ruling on adhan validity and restart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid disliked adhan (junub) and invalid need-to-repeat adhan (woman, drunkard, etc.), and state the five cases where restart is required and the Hanafi preference on obligation level.

Core Idea
A junub's adhan is valid but disliked; unreliable callers' adhan must be repeated.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies why the adhan of a person in major impurity (junub) is treated differently from that of other unreliable callers. It also lists five specific emergencies that, according to al-Khulasa, obligate restarting the adhan. However, later Hanafi authorities soften this obligation to recommendation, based on the underlying rationale of preventing confusion over prayer times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for each caller
Read the passage and list the hukm for the junub, woman, drunkard, madman, idiot, child, and fasiq. Note which are valid and which require repetition.
The junub's adhan is valid but makruh; the others are invalid and must be repeated.
2
Understand the reasoning for repetition
The key reason is 'عدم الاعتماد' (lack of reliance) for women, drunkards, etc. Their adhan cannot be trusted, so people might wait for a correct adhan and risk missing prayer. The junub is excluded because his adhan is reliable.
3
List the five situations from al-Khulasa
Extract the five cases that obligate restart: fainting, death, breaking wudu and leaving, being stuck without a prompter, and becoming mute.
These apply to any mu'adhdhin, not just the five categories above.
4
Analyze the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The text provides a rational argument: if the mu'adhdhin starts then stops, listeners think it was erroneous, wait for another adhan, and potentially miss prayer. Hence, restart is wajib to prevent harm.
This proof is based on preventing loss of prayer (darar).
5
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Khulasa says wajib, but al-Mujtaba and al-Zahiriyya say mustahabb. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq sides with istihbab. Understand the shift and the mufta bihi position.
The earlier wajib is often interpreted as 'confirmed recommendation'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أغلظ الحدثين دون أخفهما، فظاهره كغيره أن كراهة أذان الجنب تحريمية الطهارة فيه عن لترك الواجب وإن كانت إعادته مستحبة ويعاد أذان المرأة والسكران والجنون والمعتوه والصبي الذي لا يعقل لعدم الاعتماد على أذان هؤلاء فلا يلتفت إليهم فربما ينتظر الناس الأذان المعتبر والحال أنه معتبر فيؤدّي إلى تفويت الصلاة أو الشك في صحة المؤدي أو إيقاعها في وقت مكروه، وهذا لا ينتهض في الجنب، وغاية ما يمكن أن ينهض فسقه. وصرح بكراهة أذان الفاسق ولا يعاد فالإعادة فيه ليقع على وجه السنة. وفي الخلاصة : خمس خصال إذا وجدت في الأذان والإقامة وجب الاستقبال : إذا غشي على المؤذن في أحدهما أو مات أو سبقه حدث فذهب وتوضأ أو حصر فيه ولا ملقن أو خرس يجب الاستقبال وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : معناه فإن حمل الوجوب على ظاهره احتيج إلى الفرق بين نفس الأذان فإنه سنة واستقباله بعد الشروع فيه وتحقق العجز عن إتمامه. وقد يقال فيه إذا شرع فيه ثم قطع تبادر إلى ظن السامعين أن قطعه للخطأ فينتظرون الأذان الحق وقد تفوت بذلك الصلاة فوجب إزالة ما يفضي إلى ذلك بخلاف ما إذا لم يكن أذان أصلاً حيث لا ينتظرون بل يراقب كل منهم وقت الصلاة بنفسه أو ينصبون لهم مراقباً إلا أن هذا يقتضي وجوب الإعادة فيمن ذكرناهم آنفاً إلا الجنب كذا في فتح القدير. والظاهر أن الوجوب ليس على حقيقته بل بمعنى الثبوت لما في المجتبى : وإذا غشي عليه في أذانه أو أحدث فتوضأ أو مات أو ارتد فالأحب استقبال الأذان وكذا صرح بالاستحباب في الظهيرية.
The more severe of the two events without the lighter one. So its apparent meaning is like others that the dislike of the adhan of the junub is prohibitive? cleanliness in it for leaving the obligatory, even though its repetition is recommended. And the adhan of a woman, a drunkard, a madman, an idiot, and a child who does not reason is repeated due to lack of reliance on their adhan, so no attention is paid to them. For perhaps people wait for the reliable adhan while it is reliable, leading to missing the prayer or doubt in the validity of what is performed or performing it at a disliked time. And this does not apply to the junub; at most it can apply to his sin. And he explicitly stated the dislike of the adhan of the fasiq and it is not repeated, so repetition in it is so that it occurs in a sunna manner. And in al-Khulasa: Five characteristics when found in the adhan and iqama, restart becomes obligatory: if the mu'adhdhin faints during either, or dies, or an event precedes him so he goes and performs wudu, or he is stuck and has no prompter, or becomes mute, restart is obligatory. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: its meaning: for if obligation is taken literally, a distinction is needed between the adhan itself, for it is sunna, and restarting it after beginning and incapacity to complete it. And it may be said about it: if he begins it then stops, it occurs to the listeners that his stopping is due to an error, so they wait for the correct adhan, and thus prayer may be missed; so removal of what leads to that is obligatory, unlike the case where there was no adhan at all, for then they do not wait but each monitors prayer time himself or they appoint a monitor for them. Except this necessitates obligation of repetition for those we mentioned earlier except the junub, as in Fath al-Qadir. And the apparent meaning is that obligation is not literal but means confirmation, as in al-Mujtaba: and if he faints during his adhan or breaks wudu and does wudu, or dies, or apostatizes, then restarting the adhan is preferable. And similarly he stated recommendation in al-Zahiriyya.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the ruling regarding the adhan of a person in major impurity (junub) and five specific situations where the adhan must be restarted. The passage opens by comparing the adhan of a junub with that of a woman, drunkard, madman, etc. The key distinction is that while the adhan of the latter categories is invalid and must be repeated because their word is unreliable, the adhan of a junub is valid but makruh (disliked). The author then presents five cases from al-Khulasa where restarting the adhan is wajib: if the mu'adhdhin faints, dies, breaks wudu and leaves to renew it, becomes stuck without a prompter, or becomes mute. The text discusses whether this 'wajib' is literal or figurative. Fatawa Qadikhan suggests that if taken literally, it would contradict the sunna status of adhan itself. However, rational reasoning explains that if an adhan is interrupted suddenly, people may wait for a proper adhan, potentially missing the prayer. Therefore, to prevent confusion and harm, restart is required. This rationale does not apply to the junub because his adhan is valid, so there is no fear of missed prayer. The passage concludes with a clarification from al-Mujtaba and al-Zahiriyya that the obligation is actually a recommendation (istihbab), emphasizing that the ruling is based on precaution and public interest, not on the inherent invalidity of the interrupted adhan.

Key Terms
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
الاستقبال (al-istiqbal): Restarting the adhan from the beginning after interruption or invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the five cases requiring restart of the adhan?
A) The mu'adhdhin faints
B) The mu'adhdhin dies
C) The mu'adhdhin becomes junub
D) The mu'adhdhin breaks his wudu and leaves to renew it

Key Takeaway
The adhan of a junub is valid but disliked; however, if the mu'adhdhin becomes incapacitated mid-call, the adhan must be restarted to avoid confusion, though Hanafi authorities prefer to call it recommended rather than obligatory.
