Essential Spots for Purity in Prayer: Feet and Forehead
Core ruling on purity of feet and forehead with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on which spots must be pure for prayer and explain why impurity on hands and knees does not invalidate prayer.

Core Idea
Only the feet and forehead must be on pure ground; other contacts do not invalidate.

When you pray, does every part of your body that touches the ground need to be on pure ground? According to the Hanafi school, the answer is no—only the spots that you are obligated to place (your feet and forehead) must be pure. This lesson clarifies the soundest narration from Abu Hanifa and the agreement of the Sahibayn, and addresses an opposite view from Abu al-Layth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligatory placement points
In prayer, the feet and the forehead are the limbs that must be placed on the ground for the prayer to be valid. The text says the 'place' (makan) means only the spot of the feet and prostration (forehead).
Prostration on the forehead is a rukn; feet placement is for standing.
2
Understand why hands and knees are not required
Prostration on the hands and knees is not a fard (obligatory) act. The Hanafi principle: if the limb is not obligatory to place, placing it on impurity is like not placing it at all. Therefore, impurity there does not invalidate prayer.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu al-Layth held that any contact with impurity invalidates prayer. However, this view is considered shadhdh (rare) and does not affect the relied-upon ruling.
Al-'Uyun confirmed Abu al-Layth's view but later scholars preferred the soundest narration from Abu Hanifa.
4
Apply to a simple scenario
If a person places their forehead on a pure spot but their hands touch impurity directly, the prayer is valid. If they stand with one foot on impurity, they must lift that foot; otherwise the prayer is invalid for that foot.
Raising the impure foot avoids the contact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأراد بالمكان موضع القدم والسجود فقط، أما طهارة موضع القدم فباتفاق الروايات بشرط أن يضعهما على النجاسة، أما إن رفع القدم التي موضعها نجس وصلى جاز. وإما طهارة موضع السجود ففي أصح الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة وهو قولهما، وأما إن كانت النجاسة في موضع يديه وركبتيه وحذاء إبطيه وصدره جازت صلاته لأن الوضع على النجاسة كلا وضع، والسجود على اليدين والركبتين غير واجب فكأنه لم يسجد عليها وهذا ظاهر الرواية. واختار أبو الليث أن صلاته تفسد وصححه في العيون ولو صلى على مكان طاهر إلا أنه إذا سجد تقع ثيابه على أرض نجسة جازت صلاته بالطريق الأولى لأن قيامه على مكان طاهر. ولو صلى على بساط وعلى طرف منه نجاسة فالأصح أنه يجوز كبيراً كان أو صغيراً، لأنه بمنزلة الأرض فلا يصير مستعملاً للنجاسة وهو بالطريق الأولى لأن النجاسة إذا كانت لا تمنع في موضع الركبتين واليدين فههنا أولى. وفي الخلاصة : ولو بسط بساطاً رقيقاً على الموضع النجس، وصلى عليه؛ إن كان البساط بحال يصلح ساتر للعورة تجوز الصلاة وإن كانت رطبة فالقى عليها ثوباً وصلى؛ إن كان ثوباً يمكن أن يجعل من عرضه ثوباً يجوز عند محمد، وإن كان لا يمكن لا يجوز . وكذا لو ألقى عليها لبدأ فصلى عليه يجوز. وقال الحلواني : لا يجوز حتى يلقي على هذا الطرف الطرف الآخر فيصير بمنزلة ثوبين. وإن كانت النجاسة يابسة جازت يعني إذا كان يصلح ساتراً ا هـ. ولو صلى على ما له بطانة متنجسة وهو قائم على ما يلي موضع الطهارة، عن محمد يجوز. وعن أبي يوسف لا يجوز. وقيل جواب محمد في غير المضرب فيكون حكمه حكم ثوبين وجواب أبي يوسف في المضرب فحكمه حكم ثوب واحد فلا خلاف بينهما . قال في التنجيس والأصح أن المضرب على الخلاف ذكره الحلواني. ولو قام على النجاسة وفي رجليه نعلان أو جوربان لم تجز صلاته لأنه قام على مكان نجس، ولو افترش نعليه وقام عليهما جازت الصلاة بمنزلة ما لو بسط الثوب الطاهر على الأرض النجسة وصلى عليه جاز. وفي المبسوط من كتاب التحري : يجوز لبس الثوب النجس لغير الصلاة ولا يلزمه الاجتناب . وذكر في البغية تلخيص القنية خلافاً فيه.
And by 'place' he meant only the place of the feet and prostration. As for the purity of the place of the feet, it is agreed upon in the narrations, on condition that he places them on the impurity. But if he lifts the foot whose place is impure and prays, it is valid. As for the purity of the place of prostration, it is in the soundest of two narrations from Abu Hanifa and it is the view of both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And if there is impurity in the place of his hands, knees, armpits, and chest, his prayer is valid because placing the limb on impurity is not considered placing, and prostration on the hands and knees is not obligatory, so it is as if he did not prostrate on them. This is the apparent narration. Abu al-Layth chose that his prayer is invalid and confirmed it in al-'Uyun. And if he prays on a pure place but when he prostrates his clothes fall on impure ground, his prayer is valid a fortiori because his standing is on a pure place. And if he prays on a mat and there is impurity on its edge, the correct view is that it is permissible whether the mat is big or small, because it is like the ground, so he does not become a user of the impurity, and it is a fortiori because if impurity does not prevent in the place of knees and hands, then here even more so. In al-Khulasah: If he spreads a thin mat over an impure place and prays on it, if the mat is such that it can serve as a cover for the 'awrah, the prayer is valid. If the impurity is moist and he throws a cloth over it and prays, if the cloth can be made into a garment from its width, it is permissible according to Muhammad; if not, it is not permissible. Similarly, if he throws a felt sheet over it and prays, it is permissible. Al-Halwani said: It is not permissible until he places one edge over the other so that it becomes like two garments. If the impurity is dry, it is permissible, meaning if it can serve as a cover. End. And if he prays on something with an impure lining while he stands on the part facing the pure place, according to Muhammad it is permissible. According to Abu Yusuf, it is not permissible. It is said that Muhammad's answer applies to a non-padded covering (ghayr al-midrab), so its ruling is the ruling of two garments, and Abu Yusuf's answer applies to a padded covering (midrab), so its ruling is the ruling of one garment; thus there is no disagreement. He said in al-Tunjis: The correct view is that the midrab is subject to disagreement, as al-Halwani mentioned. And if he stands on impurity with sandals or socks on his feet, his prayer is not valid because he stood on an impure place. If he spreads his sandals and stands on them, the prayer is valid, just as if he spreads a pure cloth on impure ground and prays on it, it is valid. In al-Mabsut from Kitab al-Tahari: It is permissible to wear an impure garment for non-prayer purposes, and he is not required to avoid it. Mentioned in al-Bughyah: Talkhis al-Quniyah mentions a disagreement on this.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage addresses the requirement of purity for the place (makan) of prayer, specifically the spots where the body contacts the ground. The author clarifies that 'place' means only the area of the feet and the forehead (prostration spot). For the feet, purity is required only when they are placed on the ground; if lifted, prayer is valid even if the ground is impure. For the prostration spot, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa; the soundest (sahih) is that it must be pure, and this is also the view of the Sahibayn. However, for the hands, knees, armpits, and chest, impurity does not invalidate prayer because placing these limbs is not obligatory (prostration on hands and knees is not fard). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu al-Layth held that prayer is invalid if these places are impure, and this was confirmed in al-'Uyun. The text then discusses various scenarios: praying on a pure place but clothes fall on impure ground (valid a fortiori), praying on a mat with impurity on its edge (valid), spreading a thin mat over impurity (valid if it can cover ‘awrah, etc.), and cases of moist/ dry impurity with cloth or felt. There is a difference between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding an impure lining, but it is reconciled by the type of covering (midrab vs. ghayr midrab). Wearing sandals on impure ground invalidates if directly on the ground, but spreading them to stand on is valid. Finally, wearing impure clothing outside prayer is permissible. The passage emphasizes that the pure ground acts as a barrier, and impurity that does not directly contact the body in obligatory positions does not invalidate.

Key Terms
مكان الصلاة (makan al-salah): The physical spot on the ground where the prayer is performed, specifically the area of the feet and prostration (forehead).
موضع السجود (mawdi' al-sujud): The place where the forehead rests during prostration; its purity is required according to the soundest narration.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The explicit and predominant transmission from the early Hanafi masters (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) as recorded in the six works of Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the soundest Hanafi position, if a person prays and his knees are on najasah, but his feet and forehead are on pure ground, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because the knees are on impurity.
B) The prayer is valid because prostration on the knees is not obligatory.
C) The prayer is invalid unless the impurity is less than a dirham.
D) The prayer is valid only if the person intended not to place weight on the knees.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi prayer, only the feet (if placed) and the forehead must be on pure ground; other contacts do not invalidate.

Practical Scenarios: Barriers, Mats, and Footwear
Detailed practical scenarios for barriers and barriers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for various scenarios involving impurity on or underneath barriers (mats, clothing, sandals) during prayer.

Core Idea
A pure barrier can insulate from ground impurity, but the barrier must be adequate and correctly placed.

What if you spread a mat over impure ground, or wear sandals over impurity? The scholars derived detailed rules for these common situations. This lesson walks through the rulings for mats with edge impurity, thin vs. thick barriers, impure linings, and standing with sandals or socks—all building on the core principle that the obligatory contact points must be pure.

Guided Path
1
Analyze prayer on a mat with impurity on its edge
If the mat is pure where the feet and forehead are, but impurity is on the edge, the prayer is valid because the mat acts like the ground and does not transfer impurity to the worshipper. This applies whether the mat is large or small.
The mat is considered a barrier, not a conveyer.
2
Evaluate thin spread over impurity
If a thin cloth is spread over impurity, check if it can cover the ‘awrah (private parts). If yes, it is a sufficient barrier; if too thin (transparent), it may not suffice. The moisture of impurity also matters: if the impurity is moist, the cloth must be thick enough to prevent seepage.
Al-Halwani adds that for moist impurity, a single layer may not suffice; the cloth should be doubled.
3
Distinguish between padded and non-padded garments (midrab)
If a garment has an impure lining but the outer (pure) part is where the feet stand, opinions differ. Muhammad says it is valid (like two separate garments), Abu Yusuf says it is invalid (like one garment). The reconciliation: Muhammad's view applies to non-padded garments (ghayr midrab), Abu Yusuf's to padded ones (midrab).
Al-Tunjis says the midrab case is subject to disagreement.
4
Apply the ruling for sandals/socks on impure ground
If one stands with sandals or socks directly on impure ground, the prayer is invalid because the foot is not lifted and the sandal/sock contacts impurity. But if one spreads the sandals (e.g., placing them as a barrier) and stands on them, it is like spreading a pure cloth—valid.
The key is whether the barrier is considered a separation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأراد بالمكان موضع القدم والسجود فقط، أما طهارة موضع القدم فباتفاق الروايات بشرط أن يضعهما على النجاسة، أما إن رفع القدم التي موضعها نجس وصلى جاز. وإما طهارة موضع السجود ففي أصح الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة وهو قولهما، وأما إن كانت النجاسة في موضع يديه وركبتيه وحذاء إبطيه وصدره جازت صلاته لأن الوضع على النجاسة كلا وضع، والسجود على اليدين والركبتين غير واجب فكأنه لم يسجد عليها وهذا ظاهر الرواية. واختار أبو الليث أن صلاته تفسد وصححه في العيون ولو صلى على مكان طاهر إلا أنه إذا سجد تقع ثيابه على أرض نجسة جازت صلاته بالطريق الأولى لأن قيامه على مكان طاهر. ولو صلى على بساط وعلى طرف منه نجاسة فالأصح أنه يجوز كبيراً كان أو صغيراً، لأنه بمنزلة الأرض فلا يصير مستعملاً للنجاسة وهو بالطريق الأولى لأن النجاسة إذا كانت لا تمنع في موضع الركبتين واليدين فههنا أولى. وفي الخلاصة : ولو بسط بساطاً رقيقاً على الموضع النجس، وصلى عليه؛ إن كان البساط بحال يصلح ساتر للعورة تجوز الصلاة وإن كانت رطبة فالقى عليها ثوباً وصلى؛ إن كان ثوباً يمكن أن يجعل من عرضه ثوباً يجوز عند محمد، وإن كان لا يمكن لا يجوز . وكذا لو ألقى عليها لبدأ فصلى عليه يجوز. وقال الحلواني : لا يجوز حتى يلقي على هذا الطرف الطرف الآخر فيصير بمنزلة ثوبين. وإن كانت النجاسة يابسة جازت يعني إذا كان يصلح ساتراً ا هـ. ولو صلى على ما له بطانة متنجسة وهو قائم على ما يلي موضع الطهارة، عن محمد يجوز. وعن أبي يوسف لا يجوز. وقيل جواب محمد في غير المضرب فيكون حكمه حكم ثوبين وجواب أبي يوسف في المضرب فحكمه حكم ثوب واحد فلا خلاف بينهما . قال في التنجيس والأصح أن المضرب على الخلاف ذكره الحلواني. ولو قام على النجاسة وفي رجليه نعلان أو جوربان لم تجز صلاته لأنه قام على مكان نجس، ولو افترش نعليه وقام عليهما جازت الصلاة بمنزلة ما لو بسط الثوب الطاهر على الأرض النجسة وصلى عليه جاز. وفي المبسوط من كتاب التحري : يجوز لبس الثوب النجس لغير الصلاة ولا يلزمه الاجتناب . وذكر في البغية تلخيص القنية خلافاً فيه.

Commentary
This passage addresses the requirement of purity for the place (makan) of prayer, specifically the spots where the body contacts the ground. The author clarifies that 'place' means only the area of the feet and the forehead (prostration spot). For the feet, purity is required only when they are placed on the ground; if lifted, prayer is valid even if the ground is impure. For the prostration spot, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa; the soundest (sahih) is that it must be pure, and this is also the view of the Sahibayn. However, for the hands, knees, armpits, and chest, impurity does not invalidate prayer because placing these limbs is not obligatory (prostration on hands and knees is not fard). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu al-Layth held that prayer is invalid if these places are impure, and this was confirmed in al-'Uyun. The text then discusses various scenarios: praying on a pure place but clothes fall on impure ground (valid a fortiori), praying on a mat with impurity on its edge (valid), spreading a thin mat over impurity (valid if it can cover ‘awrah, etc.), and cases of moist/ dry impurity with cloth or felt. There is a difference between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding an impure lining, but it is reconciled by the type of covering (midrab vs. ghayr midrab). Wearing sandals on impure ground invalidates if directly on the ground, but spreading them to stand on is valid. Finally, wearing impure clothing outside prayer is permissible. The passage emphasizes that the pure ground acts as a barrier, and impurity that does not directly contact the body in obligatory positions does not invalidate.

Key Terms
بساط (bisat): A mat or rug used for prayer.
المضرب (al-midrab): A padded garment or covering; its lining is attached in a way that it functions as one fabric.
الطريق الأولى (al-tariq al-awla): A fortiori argument; if a lighter case is permitted, the heavier case is all the more permitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person spreads a thin cloth over dry impurity and prays on it, what condition must the cloth meet for the prayer to be valid?
A) It must be large enough to cover the entire body.
B) It must be capable of covering the ‘awrah (i.e., non-transparent).
C) It must be made of cotton.
D) It must be thicker than a coin.

Key Takeaway
A pure barrier can make prayer valid even on impure ground, but its thickness and placement must meet criteria, and direct contact with impurity without lifting invalidates.

beginner

Obligation of Covering 'Awrah in Prayer with Evidence
Establishes the obligation with three proofs and dismisses a rare opposing view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three proofs for the obligation of covering 'awrah in prayer and explain why the dissenting view does not affect the established ruling.

Core Idea
Covering 'awrah in prayer is fard by definitive ijma', supported by Quranic command and prophetic hadith.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes that covering the 'awrah during prayer is an obligatory condition (fard). The author cites three proofs: the consensus (ijma') of the Muslim community, the Quranic verse commanding 'adornment at every mosque,' and the prophetic hadith that Allah does not accept the prayer of a mature woman without a khimar. The text also addresses a rare dissenting view from some later Malikis, explaining that once ijma' is established, subsequent opposition is irrelevant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that covering the 'awrah is fard (obligatory) for the validity of prayer. Understand that this is not merely recommended but required.
The ruling is unconditional for both men and women, with definitions of 'awrah varying.
2
Locate the primary proof: Ijma'
The author first cites ijma' (consensus) as the main evidence, transmitted by multiple scholars. Ijma' makes the ruling definitive.
Ijma' is a source of law in Hanafi usul; once established, later opposition is invalid.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
The Quran (al-A'raf 7:31) commands: 'Take your adornment at every mosque.' The imperative 'khudhu' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. 'Zinah' is interpreted as the garment covering the 'awrah.
This is a dalil naqli (textual proof) with clear indication.
4
Analyze the hadith evidence
The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Allah does not accept the prayer of a menstruating woman except with a khimar.' 'Ha'id' means a mature woman. The negation of acceptance implies the prayer is invalid without the covering.
This hadith is ahad but accepted as proof for obligation.
5
Evaluate the dissenting view
The passage mentions that some Malikis (e.g., Qadi Isma'il) opposed the obligation. However, because ijma' was already established, their view is not considered.
This demonstrates the principle that later ikhtilaf does not break a previously established ijma'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وستر عورته للإجماع على أنه فرض في الصلاة كما نقله غير واحد من النقل إلى أن حدث بعض المالكية فخالف فيه كالقاضي اسماعيل وهو لا يجوز بعد تقرر الإجماع. ويعضده قوله تعالى يا بني آدم خذوا زينتكم عند كل مسجد) [الأعراف: ٣١] أي محلها. والمراد ما يواري عورته عند كل صلاة إطلاقاً لاسم الحال على المحل في الأول وعكسه في الثاني. وقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم « لا يقبل الله صلاة حائض إلا بخمار)(١) أي البالغة سميت
His statement: (And covering his private parts) because there is consensus (ijma') that it is obligatory (fard) in prayer, as transmitted by more than one scholar, until some Malikis contradicted it, like Qadi Isma'il, but that is not permissible after the establishment of consensus. And it is supported by the Almighty's saying: 'O children of Adam, take your adornment at every mosque' [al-A'raf: 31] meaning its place. And the intended meaning is what covers his private parts at every prayer, by applying the name of the state to the place in the first, and vice versa in the second. And his saying, peace be upon him: 'Allah does not accept the prayer of a menstruating woman except with a khimar' i.e., the mature woman named...
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage establishes the obligation (fard) of covering the 'awrah during prayer. The author states that there is consensus (ijma') among scholars on this, and he notes that a small number of later Malikis (like Qadi Isma'il) dissented, but their view is not considered after the consensus was established. The Quranic evidence is Surah al-A'raf, verse 31: 'Take your adornment at every mosque.' The word 'adornment' (zinah) is interpreted as the garment that covers the 'awrah, and 'every mosque' means every prayer. The hadith evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that Allah does not accept the prayer of a woman who has reached puberty (ha'id – meaning mature woman) without a head covering (khimar). This hadith is narrated by Ibn Majah, al-Tirmidhi, and Ahmad. The passage highlights that the obligation is established by definitive evidence (ijma' and clear Quranic command), and the rare opposition does not affect the established ruling.

Key Terms
ستر العورة (satr al-'awrah): The requirement to cover the private parts during prayer; for men, from navel to knees (including knees and navel), for women, the entire body except face and hands.
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the scholars of the Muslim community on a ruling; here it is the consensus on the obligation of covering 'awrah in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary evidence for the obligation of covering 'awrah during prayer?
A) The hadith about the dog.
B) The consensus (ijma') and the Quranic verse.
C) The opinion of Qadi Isma'il.
D) The ruling from al-Muhit.

Key Takeaway
Covering the 'awrah during prayer is fard, proven by ijma', Quran, and hadith; later dissenting views do not affect the established ruling.

Rulings on Praying on Impure Ground with a Barrier (Mat or Thin Covering)
Rulings on barriers and impurity in prayer place

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on praying on a mat with impurity on one edge and apply the principle that a mat is like the earth.

Core Idea
A mat is like the earth: impurity on one part does not invalidate prayer on the clean part.

This lesson examines the basic principle that standing on a pure spot of otherwise impure ground renders prayer valid. The text then extends this to a mat (bisat) with impurity on one edge, illustrating the Hanafi reasoning that the mat is treated like the earth itself. We will also explore the scenario of a thin covering over wet impurity, including a disagreement between Imam Muhammad and al-Halwani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
The text begins with a direct ruling: if a person stands on a pure spot on impure ground, his prayer is permissible. This is by primary reasoning (qiyas jali).
2
Apply the analogy to a mat
The ruling extends to praying on a mat (bisat) when there is impurity on one edge. The mat is like the earth, so impurity on one part does not affect the rest. The prayer is permissible whether the mat is large or small.
The reasoning is that the mat does not become a user of impurity (musta'mil li al-najasa).
3
Examine the wet impurity case
If the impurity is wet and a thin garment is thrown over it, there is a difference of opinion. Muhammad permits if the garment can be made into a cover; al-Halwani requires folding the two ends to form a double layer.
The condition is that the barrier must be suitable as a cover for the private parts (satr).
4
Consider dry impurity
If the impurity is dry, prayer is permissible if the covering can serve as a satr. Dry impurity does not transfer easily.
This is based on the principle that dry impurity does not spread unless it becomes wet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب شروط الصلاة
نجسة جازت صلاته بالطريق الأولى لأن قيامه على مكان طاهر. ولو صلى على بساط وعلى طرف منه نجاسة فالأصح أنه يجوز كبيراً كان أو صغيراً، لأنه بمنزلة الأرض فلا يصير مستعملاً للنجاسة وهو بالطريق الأولى لأن النجاسة إذا كانت لا تمنع في موضع الركبتين واليدين فههنا أولى. وفي الخلاصة : ولو بسط بساطاً رقيقاً على الموضع النجس، وصلى عليه؛ إن كان البساط بحال يصلح ساتر للعورة تجوز الصلاة وإن كانت رطبة فالقى عليها ثوباً وصلى؛ إن كان ثوباً يمكن أن يجعل من عرضه ثوباً يجوز عند محمد، وإن كان لا يمكن لا يجوز . وكذا لو ألقى عليها لبدأ فصلى عليه يجوز. وقال الحلواني : لا يجوز حتى يلقي على هذا الطرف الطرف الآخر فيصير بمنزلة ثوبين. وإن كانت النجاسة يابسة جازت يعني إذا كان يصلح ساتراً ا هـ. ولو صلى على ما له بطانة متنجسة وهو قائم على ما يلي موضع الطهارة، عن محمد يجوز. وعن أبي يوسف لا يجوز. وقيل جواب محمد في غير المضرب فيكون حكمه حكم ثوبين وجواب أبي يوسف في المضرب فحكمه حكم ثوب واحد فلا خلاف بينهما . قال في التنجيس والأصح أن المضرب على الخلاف ذكره الحلواني. ولو قام على النجاسة وفي رجليه نعلان أو جوربان لم تجز صلاته لأنه قام على مكان نجس، ولو افترش نعليه وقام عليهما جازت الصلاة بمنزلة ما لو بسط الثوب الطاهر على الأرض النجسة وصلى عليه جاز. وفي المبسوط من كتاب التحري : يجوز لبس الثوب النجس لغير الصلاة ولا يلزمه الاجتناب . وذكر في البغية تلخيص القنية خلافاً فيه. وقال في العيون : هذه رواية شاذة والصحيح أن يقال : إن كان في موضع ركبتيه لا تجوز صلاته اهـ . ونقل شارحها الشيخ إبراهيم الحلبي عبارة الخانية السابقة ثم قال : فعلم أنه لا فرق بين الركبتين واليدين وبين موضع السجود والقدمين وهو الصحيح لأن اتصال العضو بالنجاسة بمنزلة حملها وإن كان وضع ذلك العضو ليس بفرض اهـ.
The Book of Prayer - Chapter on Conditions of Prayer
If it is impure, his prayer is permissible by primary reasoning because he is standing on a pure place. If he prays on a mat and there is impurity on one of its edges, the most correct view is that it is permissible, whether the mat is large or small, because it is like the ground, so it does not become a user of the impurity, and it is by primary reasoning because if impurity does not prevent in the place of the knees and hands, then here it is even more so. In al-Khulasa: If he spreads a thin mat over an impure place and prays on it; if the mat is such that it can serve as a cover for the private parts, the prayer is permissible. If the impurity is wet and he throws a garment over it and prays; if the garment is such that it can be made into a garment from its width, it is permissible according to Muhammad; if it cannot, it is not permissible. Similarly, if he throws a felt cloth over it and prays on it, it is permissible. Al-Halwani said: It is not permissible until he throws one end over the other, so that it becomes like two garments. If the impurity is dry, it is permissible, meaning if it can serve as a cover. End quote. If he prays on something that has an impure lining while he is standing on the part that faces the pure area, according to Muhammad it is permissible; according to Abu Yusuf it is not permissible. It is said that Muhammad's answer applies to a non-bedspread, so its ruling is like two garments, and Abu Yusuf's answer applies to a bedspread, so its ruling is like one garment, so there is no difference between them. In al-Tanjees it is said: The most correct is that the bedspread is subject to difference, mentioned by al-Halwani. If he stands on impurity with sandals or socks on his feet, his prayer is not permissible because he is standing on an impure place. If he spreads his sandals and stands on them, the prayer is permissible, just as if he spread a pure garment on impure ground and prayed on it, it is permissible. In al-Mabsut from the book of al-Tahari: It is permissible to wear an impure garment for other than prayer, and he is not obliged to avoid it. In al-Bughya, Talkhis al-Qunyah mentions a difference of opinion regarding it. In al-Uyun: This is a rare transmission; the correct view is to say: If it is in the place of his knees, his prayer is not permissible. End quote. Its commentator, Shaykh Ibrahim al-Halabi, transmitted the earlier phrasing of al-Khaniyya and then said: It is known from this that there is no difference between the knees and hands and between the place of prostration and feet, and this is correct, because the contact of a limb with impurity is like carrying it, even if placing that limb is not obligatory. End quote.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the rulings on impurity in the place of prayer and various scenarios where barriers are placed between the worshipper and the impurity. The first ruling states that if a person stands on a pure spot on otherwise impure ground, the prayer is valid, because he is not directly contacting the impurity. This is derived by way of primary reasoning (qiyas jali): if impurity on the knees does not invalidate prayer, then standing on a pure spot on impure ground is even more permissible. The text then addresses praying on a mat (bisat) with impurity on one side: the preferred view (al-asahh) is that it is permissible, as the mat is like the earth and does not become a conveyor of impurity. From al-Khulasa, a more detailed ruling: if a thin mat (satr) covering the private parts is placed over impurity, prayer is valid; if the impurity is wet and a garment is thrown over it, there is a dispute between Imam Muhammad and al-Halwani. Muhammad permits if the garment can be folded to serve as a cover; al-Halwani requires folding the two ends to create a double layer. The text then addresses a bedspread (midrab) with an impure lining: Muhammad permits if the clean side is stood upon, while Abu Yusuf does not. A reconciliation is offered: Muhammad's view applies when the bedspread is not a single unit (like two garments), while Abu Yusuf's applies to an actual bedspread (single unit), resolving the apparent conflict. Further rulings: standing on impurity with footwear invalidates prayer, but spreading the sandals and standing on them (like a pure garment on impure ground) is valid. Wearing impure clothes outside prayer is permitted without avoidance according to al-Mabsut, though al-Bughya notes a difference. Finally, a comment from al-Uyun about a rare transmission concerning the knees: the correct view is that if the knees contact impurity, prayer is invalid, and no distinction is made between knees, hands, feet, or the place of prostration, since contact with impurity is analogous to carrying it.

Key Terms
بساط (bisāṭ): A mat or carpet; the text states it is like the earth (ard) so impurity on one part does not affect the rest.
ساتر (sātir): Cover; the barrier must be suitable as a cover for the private parts to constitute a valid barrier.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, praying on a mat with impurity on one edge is permissible because the mat is considered:
A) A separate object that must be pure
B) Like the earth, not a conveyor of impurity
C) A barrier that must be doubled
D) Impure if the impurity is wet

Key Takeaway
A mat or barrier is like the earth; impurity on one part does not invalidate prayer on another part.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Praying on a Bedspread with an Impure Lining
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bedspread with impure lining

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding praying on a bedspread with an impure lining and identify the reconciliation between their views.

Core Idea
Muhammad treats a bedspread as two garments; Abu Yusuf treats it as one – reconciled by distinguishing the type of covering.

This lesson focuses on a specific intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a bedspread (midrab) with an impure lining. Imam Muhammad permits prayer if the worshipper stands on the clean side, while Abu Yusuf forbids it. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq offers a reconciliation by stating that Muhammad's view applies to coverings that are not actually bedspreads, while Abu Yusuf's applies to true bedspreads, thereby resolving the contradiction.

Guided Path
1
State the positions
Muhammad says prayer is permissible if standing on the clean side of a bedspread with impure lining; Abu Yusuf says it is not permissible.
2
Understand the reasoning
Muhammad considers the clean side as a separate barrier; Abu Yusuf sees the bedspread as a single unit where impurity affects the whole.
This is a qiyas khafi difference in the conception of the object.
3
Learn the reconciliation
The text offers a resolution: Muhammad's ruling is for a non-bedspread (like two separate garments), and Abu Yusuf's ruling is for an actual bedspread (one garment). Hence, there is no real contradiction.
This reconciliation is credited to a later source (qila).
4
Consider the final note
Al-Tanjees and al-Halwani say the most correct view is that the bedspread is subject to difference (ala al-khilaf), meaning no single view is definitively preferred.
The mufta bihi may depend on the specific type of covering.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب شروط الصلاة

Key Terms
مضرب (miḍrab): A bedspread or thick covering; the dispute centers on whether it is considered one garment (so impurity affects all) or two garments (so standing on clean side suffices).
بطانة (biṭānah): Lining; the inner layer of a garment or covering. In this context, the lining is impure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) For any covering with an impure lining
B) For a non-bedspread
C) For a true bedspread (midrab)
D) For a thin mat

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on bedspreads is reconciled by distinguishing the type of covering; the matter remains on ikhtilaf.

Rulings on Standing on Impurity with Footwear and Wearing Impure Clothes
Rulings on footwear, barriers, and wearing impure clothes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on standing on impurity with sandals or socks and explain the exception for spreading sandals as a barrier.

Core Idea
Standing on impurity with footwear invalidates prayer; but spreading the footwear as a barrier makes it permissible.

This lesson covers two scenarios: first, when a person stands on impurity while wearing sandals or socks – the prayer is invalid because the person is directly contacting the impurity. Second, if the person spreads the sandals on the ground and stands on them, the prayer becomes valid, analogous to spreading a pure garment on impure ground. The lesson also addresses the permissibility of wearing impure clothes outside prayer and the ruling on contact of limbs with impurity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule for standing on impurity with footwear
If a person stands on impurity with sandals or socks on his feet, the prayer is invalid because he is considered to be standing on an impure place.
The footwear does not act as a barrier because it is worn, not spread.
2
Contrast with spreading sandals as barrier
If he takes off his sandals, spreads them on the ground, and stands on them, the prayer is valid. This is analogous to spreading a pure garment on impure ground and praying on it.
The key is that the sandals are no longer worn but placed as a barrier.
3
Note the ruling on wearing impure clothes outside prayer
According to al-Mabsut, it is permissible to wear an impure garment outside prayer, and one is not obliged to avoid it. However, al-Bughya mentions a difference of opinion.
This is a separate issue from the place of prayer.
4
Understand the final point on limbs contacting impurity
The commentator Ibrahim al-Halabi states that there is no difference between knees, hands, feet, and the place of prostration: if any limb contacts impurity during prayer, the prayer is invalid, because it is like carrying the impurity.
This overrides the earlier suggestion that impurity on knees might be excused.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب شروط الصلاة
نجسة جازت صلاته بالطريق الأولى لأن قيامه على مكان طاهر. ولو صلى على بساط وعلى طرف منه نجاسة فالأصح أنه يجوز كبيراً كان أو صغيراً، لأنه بمنزلة الأرض فلا يصير مستعملاً للنجاسة وهو بالطريق الأولى لأن النجاسة إذا كانت لا تمنع في موضع الركبتين واليدين فههنا أولى. وفي الخلاصة : ولو بسط بساطاً رقيقاً على الموضع النجس، وصلى عليه؛ إن كان البساط بحال يصلح ساتر للعورة تجوز الصلاة وإن كانت رطبة فالقى عليها ثوباً وصلى؛ إن كان ثوباً يمكن أن يجعل من عرضه ثوباً يجوز عند محمد، وإن كان لا يمكن لا يجوز . وكذا لو ألقى عليها لبدأ فصلى عليه يجوز. وقال الحلواني : لا يجوز حتى يلقي على هذا الطرف الطرف الآخر فيصير بمنزلة ثوبين. وإن كانت النجاسة يابسة جازت يعني إذا كان يصلح ساتراً ا هـ. ولو صلى على ما له بطانة متنجسة وهو قائم على ما يلي موضع الطهارة، عن محمد يجوز. وعن أبي يوسف لا يجوز. وقيل جواب محمد في غير المضرب فيكون حكمه حكم ثوبين وجواب أبي يوسف في المضرب فحكمه حكم ثوب واحد فلا خلاف بينهما . قال في التنجيس والأصح أن المضرب على الخلاف ذكره الحلواني. ولو قام على النجاسة وفي رجليه نعلان أو جوربان لم تجز صلاته لأنه قام على مكان نجس، ولو افترش نعليه وقام عليهما جازت الصلاة بمنزلة ما لو بسط الثوب الطاهر على الأرض النجسة وصلى عليه جاز. وفي المبسوط من كتاب التحري : يجوز لبس الثوب النجس لغير الصلاة ولا يلزمه الاجتناب . وذكر في البغية تلخيص القنية خلافاً فيه. وقال في العيون : هذه رواية شاذة والصحيح أن يقال : إن كان في موضع ركبتيه لا تجوز صلاته اهـ . ونقل شارحها الشيخ إبراهيم الحلبي عبارة الخانية السابقة ثم قال : فعلم أنه لا فرق بين الركبتين واليدين وبين موضع السجود والقدمين وهو الصحيح لأن اتصال العضو بالنجاسة بمنزلة حملها وإن كان وضع ذلك العضو ليس بفرض اهـ.
The Book of Prayer - Chapter on Conditions of Prayer
If it is impure, his prayer is permissible by primary reasoning because he is standing on a pure place. If he prays on a mat and there is impurity on one of its edges, the most correct view is that it is permissible, whether the mat is large or small, because it is like the ground, so it does not become a user of the impurity, and it is by primary reasoning because if impurity does not prevent in the place of the knees and hands, then here it is even more so. In al-Khulasa: If he spreads a thin mat over an impure place and prays on it; if the mat is such that it can serve as a cover for the private parts, the prayer is permissible. If the impurity is wet and he throws a garment over it and prays; if the garment is such that it can be made into a garment from its width, it is permissible according to Muhammad; if it cannot, it is not permissible. Similarly, if he throws a felt cloth over it and prays on it, it is permissible. Al-Halwani said: It is not permissible until he throws one end over the other, so that it becomes like two garments. If the impurity is dry, it is permissible, meaning if it can serve as a cover. End quote. If he prays on something that has an impure lining while he is standing on the part that faces the pure area, according to Muhammad it is permissible; according to Abu Yusuf it is not permissible. It is said that Muhammad's answer applies to a non-bedspread, so its ruling is like two garments, and Abu Yusuf's answer applies to a bedspread, so its ruling is like one garment, so there is no difference between them. In al-Tanjees it is said: The most correct is that the bedspread is subject to difference, mentioned by al-Halwani. If he stands on impurity with sandals or socks on his feet, his prayer is not permissible because he is standing on an impure place. If he spreads his sandals and stands on them, the prayer is permissible, just as if he spread a pure garment on impure ground and prayed on it, it is permissible. In al-Mabsut from the book of al-Tahari: It is permissible to wear an impure garment for other than prayer, and he is not obliged to avoid it. In al-Bughya, Talkhis al-Qunyah mentions a difference of opinion regarding it. In al-Uyun: This is a rare transmission; the correct view is to say: If it is in the place of his knees, his prayer is not permissible. End quote. Its commentator, Shaykh Ibrahim al-Halabi, transmitted the earlier phrasing of al-Khaniyya and then said: It is known from this that there is no difference between the knees and hands and between the place of prostration and feet, and this is correct, because the contact of a limb with impurity is like carrying it, even if placing that limb is not obligatory. End quote.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the rulings on impurity in the place of prayer and various scenarios where barriers are placed between the worshipper and the impurity. The first ruling states that if a person stands on a pure spot on otherwise impure ground, the prayer is valid, because he is not directly contacting the impurity. This is derived by way of primary reasoning (qiyas jali): if impurity on the knees does not invalidate prayer, then standing on a pure spot on impure ground is even more permissible. The text then addresses praying on a mat (bisat) with impurity on one side: the preferred view (al-asahh) is that it is permissible, as the mat is like the earth and does not become a conveyor of impurity. From al-Khulasa, a more detailed ruling: if a thin mat (satr) covering the private parts is placed over impurity, prayer is valid; if the impurity is wet and a garment is thrown over it, there is a dispute between Imam Muhammad and al-Halwani. Muhammad permits if the garment can be folded to serve as a cover; al-Halwani requires folding the two ends to create a double layer. The text then addresses a bedspread (midrab) with an impure lining: Muhammad permits if the clean side is stood upon, while Abu Yusuf does not. A reconciliation is offered: Muhammad's view applies when the bedspread is not a single unit (like two garments), while Abu Yusuf's applies to an actual bedspread (single unit), resolving the apparent conflict. Further rulings: standing on impurity with footwear invalidates prayer, but spreading the sandals and standing on them (like a pure garment on impure ground) is valid. Wearing impure clothes outside prayer is permitted without avoidance according to al-Mabsut, though al-Bughya notes a difference. Finally, a comment from al-Uyun about a rare transmission concerning the knees: the correct view is that if the knees contact impurity, prayer is invalid, and no distinction is made between knees, hands, feet, or the place of prostration, since contact with impurity is analogous to carrying it.

Key Terms
نعل (na'l): Sandals; the text distinguishes between wearing them (prayer invalid) and spreading them as a barrier (prayer valid).
جورب (jawrab): Socks; same ruling as sandals when standing on impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, what is the ruling if a person stands on impurity while wearing sandals?
A) Prayer is valid because the sandals are a barrier.
B) Prayer is invalid because he is standing on an impure place.
C) Prayer is valid only if the sandals are thick.
D) Prayer is invalid only if the impurity is wet.

Key Takeaway
Standing on impurity with footwear invalidates prayer; only if the footwear is spread as a barrier does it become valid.

Definition of Male ‘Awrah and Conditions of Covering in Prayer
Ruling with proof: definition of male ‘awrah and conditions of covering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of a free man's ‘awrah, identify the conditions for valid covering, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the navel and seeing one's own ‘awrah.

Core Idea
The male ‘awrah is from below the navel to below the knee; the navel is not included, the knee is.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq, the commentator elaborates on the definition of the ‘awrah for a free man and the conditions for covering in prayer. The discussion includes the supporting hadith, the requirement that the garment be opaque, and nuanced cases such as prayer in water or in darkness. There is also an intra-Hanafi difference regarding whether the navel is ‘awrah and whether seeing one's own ‘awrah invalidates the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi definition of a free man's ‘awrah: from below the navel to below the knee, with the navel excluded and the knee included.
The text emphasizes 'below the navel' and 'below the knee', so the navel itself is not part of the ‘awrah.
2
Locate the dalil
Locate the hadiths cited: al-Hakim's 'What is between the navel and the knee is ‘awrah', al-Daraqutni's 'What is below the navel to the knee is ‘awrah', and al-Bayhaqi's 'The thigh is ‘awrah'.
All are ahad hadiths, hence zanni al-thubut, but sufficient for obligation.
3
Understand the condition of covering
The covering must be opaque; a thin garment that describes the skin is invalid. This is derived from the principle that the skin must be hidden.
This applies even if no one else is present, as covering is a right of Allah.
4
Examine exceptions
Prayer in turbid water where the ‘awrah is hidden is valid; in clear water where it is visible, invalid. Prayer in darkness without excuse is invalid by consensus.
These cases illustrate that the criterion is actual concealment, not just absence of observers.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a narration from Abu Hanifah that the navel is ‘awrah, but the majority (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and later scholars) hold it is not. Also, Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf say seeing one's own ‘awrah does not invalidate prayer, while Muhammad may differ; the relied-upon view is that it is makruh but not invalid.
The tarjih favors the majority due to the hadith evidence and the principle of precaution.

The Book of Prayer - Chapter on Conditions of Prayer. ... a menstruating woman because she has reached the age of menstruation, and restricting to menstruating excludes the one who has not reached puberty, as stated in al-Muhit: a girl approaching puberty who prayed without ablution or naked is commanded to repeat, but if she prayed without a headcover her prayer is complete by istihsan due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Let not a menstruating woman pray without a headcover,' so it does not apply to non-menstruating, and because covering the head’s ‘awrah is dropped due to the excuse of slavery, so due to the excuse of childhood it is more appropriate because the address of obligations is dropped due to the excuse of childhood unlike other conditions that are not dropped due to the excuse of childhood. The linguists said: The ‘awrah is called ‘awrah because of the ugliness of its appearance and the lowering of the eyes from it, derived from al-‘awr which is deficiency, defect, and ugliness, including the defect of the eye and the ugly word. It is general regarding what one covers with, including what is permissible to wear and what is not. So if one covers it with a silk garment and prays, the prayer is valid but he sins, like praying in usurped land. If he finds no other than it, he prays in it not naked. The limit of covering is that nothing beneath it is seen, so if one covers it with a thin garment that describes what is beneath it, it is not permissible. It includes whether someone is present or not, so if one prays naked in a dark room even if there is a pure garment, it is not permissible by consensus because covering comprises the right of Allah and the right of people, and although it is observed generally due to hiding from them, the right of Allah is not like that. If it is said: covering does not screen from Allah because He sees the covered as He sees the uncovered, the answer is that He sees the uncovered as abandoning propriety and the covered as observing propriety, and this propriety is obligatory to observe when able. If one prays in water naked, if it is turbid his prayer is valid; if it is clear such that his ‘awrah can be seen, it is not valid. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. The form of prayer in water is prayer over a janazah, otherwise there is no depiction. And he intended: it is valid by covering from others, not from himself, so even if he sees his private part from his opening or it is such that if he looked at it he would see it, it is valid according to the majority and this is the correct view, as in al-Muhit and others, but in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: regarding the state which is adornment, and the place which is the cover; and in the second view vice versa, meaning that the name of the place (the mosque) is used and the state (prayer) is intended, for covering is not obligatory for the mosque itself as evidenced by the permissibility of circumambulating naked. From this it is known that his covering is for prayer, not for the sake of people, as in Miraj al-Dirayah, i.e., because people in markets are more than in mosques, so if it were for people he would have mentioned every market. And it is reported from his teacher the scholar that the first is of the type of using the name of the effect for the cause. He said: because the garment is the cause of adornment and the place of adornment is the person. His statement: (and otherwise the depiction is not valid). He said in al-Nahr: It is not valid in other than it because the difference between clear and turbid water indicates that he has a garment, since the one who lacks it is equal regarding clear and turbid, and then it is not permissible for him to gesture for the obligatory prayer. The scholar Shaykh Ismail said: I have reservations about both statements because it is possible to depict his bowing and prostration in turbid water such that nothing of his body appears if he blocks his openings, indeed what the diver does to rescue the drowning is more than that. His statement: (but in al-Siraj etc.) The reason for the objection is that his saying 'he must button it' indicates obligation, which is apparent from the aforementioned hadith. Al-Burhan al-Halabi said in Sharh al-Munyah: The evidence supports it, that covering is obligated as a condition for prayer itself, not for fear of seeing the ‘awrah therein, and if he is in a state where if he looked he would see without effort, the condition (covering) is not fulfilled. Therefore... his navel to below his knees, and the body of a free woman is ‘awrah except her face, hands, and feet, and uncovering a quarter of her shin... If one prays in a shirt without buttons, he must button it, as narrated from Salamah ibn al-Akwa‘ who said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, shall I pray in one shirt? He said: Button it upon you, even with a thorn. And it is recommended to pray in three garments: shirt, waist-wrapper, and turban, and it is makruh to pray in a single sirwal (trousers). Thus in al-Muhit. From this it is known that wearing trousers in prayer is not obligatory because covering from below is not necessary, rather it is necessary from the sides and above. Hence it is said in Munyat al-Musalli: Whoever prays in a shirt having no other garment, so if a person looks from underneath he sees his ‘awrah, this is nothing. Know that covering the ‘awrah outside of prayer in the presence of people is obligatory by consensus except in certain places, and in seclusion there is a difference, and the correct view is obligation if the exposure is not for a valid purpose. Thus in Sharh al-Munyah. His statement: (It is from below his navel to below his knees) meaning what is between them, so the navel is not ‘awrah and the knee is ‘awrah, for the limit here does not include the limited, because of what al-Hakim narrated without critique: 'What is between the navel and the knee is ‘awrah', and al-Daraqutni's narration: 'What is below the navel to the knee is ‘awrah', and al-Bayhaqi's narration: 'The thigh is ‘awrah'. As for his thigh being exposed in the alley of Khaybar, it was not intentional. And because the knee is the junction of the thigh and shin bones, and distinguishing between them is difficult, so the prohibited and the permitted combine, and the prohibited prevails as a precaution. Thus they said. But it may be said that this implies that the navel is ‘awrah, as is a narration from Abu Hanifah, for there is a conflict regarding... If one prays naked in darkness without excuse, it is not valid by consensus. If the obligation were due to fear of sight, it would be permissible, but it may be said: Covering is prescribed in prayer by consensus, but there is no consensus regarding when the worshipper is such that if he looked he would see his own ‘awrah, because of the statement of Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf that it is not invalid, so what is appropriate is karahah (dislike) not invalidity, due to leaving a wajib not a condition, and their statement that his prayer is not invalid does not negate karahah, so this is the chosen view of the author: (It is from below his navel to below his knees). Shaykh Ismail from al-Barjandi said: What is below the navel is what is under the line that passes through the navel and encircles the circumference of his body such that its distance from its position on all sides is equal. And as for the knee, it will come that it is the junction of the shin and thigh bones. In the Hashiyah of al-Khayr al-Ramli, Ibn Hajar al-Haytami al-Shafi‘i said: I have not seen any of our imams define the knee. Al-Qamus defined it as the joint between the ends of the thigh and the upper part of the shin. He said: And the explicit meaning of what comes in the eighth and after is that it is from the beginning of the descent from the end of the thigh to the beginning of the upper shin. Based on this, they seem to have relied on custom in this because of the difficulty of restricting rulings to its linguistic definition due to its extreme scarcity, unless it is said that by 'joint' he meant what we have stated, which is close. Then I saw in al-Sihah that it said: 'And the knee is known,' so it is clear that the criterion is custom, and the discussion is in the Sacred Law, which indicates that
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa’iq, deals with the conditions of prayer, specifically the definition and covering of the ‘awrah. It begins by discussing the ‘awrah of a free woman (detailed elsewhere) and then focuses on the male ‘awrah. The key ruling is that the ‘awrah of a free man is from below the navel to below the knee. The navel itself is not ‘awrah, but the knee is. This is supported by multiple hadith narrations. The passage clarifies that covering is a condition for prayer, not merely to avoid being seen, as evidenced by the invalidity of prayer in darkness even if no one sees. The text also addresses nuances: if one prays in a thin garment that reveals the skin, it is invalid; if one prays in a silk garment, the prayer is valid but the act is sinful; if water is turbid and the ‘awrah is hidden, prayer is valid. There is an intra-Hanafi discussion: according to Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf, if the worshipper can see his own ‘awrah but others cannot, the prayer is valid but disliked (makruh). The relied-upon position is that it is not invalid, but it is disliked. The passage also covers the ruling on buttoning a shirt (wajib if one has only one garment) and recommends wearing three garments. Finally, it discusses whether the navel is included in the ‘awrah, noting a narration from Abu Hanifah suggesting it is, but the majority position is that it is not.

Key Terms
عورة (‘awrah): The parts of the body that must be covered in prayer and in front of others.
ستر (satr): Covering the ‘awrah with something that prevents the skin from being seen.
ركبة (rukbah): The knee joint, considered part of the ‘awrah in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the definition of the ‘awrah of a free man in prayer?
A) From the navel to the knees, including both.
B) From below the navel to below the knees, excluding the navel but including the knees.
C) From the chest to the knees.
D) The entire body except the face and hands.

Key Takeaway
The male ‘awrah is from below navel to below knee; covering it with an opaque garment is a condition for prayer.

The Forearm as 'Awrah: Text and Dispute
Ruling on forearm with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the forearm as 'awrah and identify the disagreement of Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The forearm is 'awrah by clear text; Abu Yusuf permits exposure due to need.

This lesson examines the forearm (dhira') as part of a woman's 'awrah in prayer. The established Hanafi position holds it is 'awrah, but Imam Abu Yusuf differed due to the need for maidservants to expose it. We will analyze the reasoning and the principle that being 'awrah does not automatically forbid looking.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What does the text say about the forearm? It is 'awrah according to the madhhab.
The text says 'al-madhhab bi al-nass'.
2
Note the alternate view
Abu Yusuf says it is not 'awrah due to need for service.
He also considers it apparent adornment.
3
Analyze the proof basis
The Hanafi view is based on clear text (nass); Abu Yusuf uses ibtila' (hardship).
4
Apply the principle of no correlation
Even if not 'awrah, looking may be prohibited due to fitnah.
The passage gives the example of the face.
5
Understand the madhhab
The mufta bihi is that it is 'awrah (zahir al-riwayah).
Sharh al-Munya confirms this.

And the madhhab is by the text, and this trial (ibtila) as it is realized in the inner palm is realized in its outer side. Otherwise. And for the specification that the forearm is awrah, and from Abu Yusuf it is not awrah, and he chose it in al-Ikhtiyar due to the need to uncover it for service, and because it is from the apparent adornment, which is the bracelet. And it was corrected in al-Mabsut that it is awrah, and some corrected that it is awrah in prayer but not outside it, and the madhhab is what is in the texts because it is the apparent narration as clarified in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And know that there is no correlation between it not being awrah and the permissibility of looking at it, so the permissibility of looking is contingent on the absence of fear of desire along with the negation of awrah, and for this reason looking at her face and the face of an amrad is prohibited, if there is doubt about desire even if there is no awrah. Thus in Sharh al-Munya. Our mashayikh said: A young woman is prevented from uncovering her face among men in our time due to fitnah. And his speech includes the flowing hair, and there are two narrations, and in al-Muhit the correct view is that it is awrah. As for washing it in janabah, it is based on the correct view. And the author excluded the foot due to trial in exposing it, especially for poor women, and there is difference in narration from Abu Hanifa and the mashayikh, so in al-Hidayah and Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir for Qadikhan it is corrected that it is not awrah, and he chose it in al-Muhit, and al-Aqta' and Qadikhan in his fatawa corrected that it is awrah, and al-Isbijabi and al-Marghinani chose it. And the author of al-Ikhtiyar corrected that it is not awrah in prayer and awrah outside it, and in Sharh al-Munya he gave preponderance to it being awrah absolutely with hadith including that narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim from Umm Salama that she asked the Prophet, 'Can a woman pray in a shift and a headcover without a waist-wrapper?' He said, 'If the shift is long enough to cover the tops of her feet,' and due to the apparent meaning of the verse according to its interpretation from A'isha and Ibn Abbas as a mawquf and marfu'. And it is stated explicitly in al-Nawazil that the vocal tone (naghama) of a woman is awrah, and he built upon it that teaching her the Quran by a woman is more beloved to me than teaching her by a blind man, and for this reason the Prophet said, 'Tasbih is for men and clapping for women,' so it is not permissible for a man to hear it, and the author acted upon it in al-Kafi when he said, 'And she should not recite the talbiyah loudly because her voice is awrah.' And the author of al-Muhit acted upon it in the chapter of adhan, and in Fath al-Qadir: based on this, if it is said that if she recites the Quran aloud in prayer the prayer becomes invalid, it would be pertinent... And in Sharh al-Munya: the more similar view is that her voice is not awrah, but rather it leads to fitnah, as al-Hidayah's author and others reasoned in the issue of talbiyah, and perhaps women are prevented from raising the voice in tasbih in prayer for this meaning, and it does not follow from the prohibition of her raising her voice in the presence of strangers that it is awrah, as we have mentioned. And in al-Zahiriyya: a very young girl's awrah is not awrah and there is no harm in looking at her or touching her. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: as for the awrah of a boy and girl, as long as they have not reached the age of desire, it is the front and back. Then it becomes more severe after that until ten years, then it becomes like that of an adult, because that is the time when a woman can reach puberty. And regarding any organ that is awrah of a woman if it is separated from her, is it permissible to look at it? There are two narrations: one permits it just as it is permissible to look at her saliva and tears, and the second does not permit it, and that is the correct view. Likewise the severed penis of a man and his pubic hair when shaved, and the correct view is that it is not permissible. His statement: 'And uncovering a quarter of her shin prevents, and likewise the hair, belly, thigh, and the thick awrah' because little uncovering is forgiven according to us due to necessity, for the clothes of the poor are not free from small holes like light impurity, and much is invalidating, so the quarter is considered and it is established in place of the whole as a precaution, because the quarter resembles the whole, as in the head where it necessitates blood if he shaves a quarter of it. And regarding what occurred in al-Hidayah of analogy to a quarter of the head, there is an issue, for the obligation there was not to wipe the entire head because the text only addressed wiping a part. As for ihram, the text addressed all of it: Allah said, 'And do not shave your heads' [2:196], so its quarter was established in place of the whole. He spoke generally about hair so it includes what is on the head and flowing, and regarding the second there is a difference and we have already mentioned that the correct view is that it is awrah. And by 'thick awrah' he meant the front and back and what is around them, and by 'light awrah' everything else from the man and woman. And he specified the thick one to refute al-Karkhi who said that in the thick one what exceeds a dirham is considered by analogy to thick impurity. The author said in al-Kafi: This is not strong because he intended to make it strict in the thick, but in reality it is a concession because he considered in the anus more than a dirham, and the anus is not more than that, so this would permit prayer even if all was uncovered, which is contradictory. And Fath al-Qadir responded that it was said that the thick awrah is the front and back with what surrounds them.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addresses the rulings of 'awrah for women in the Hanafi school, particularly in the context of prayer. The author begins by discussing the forearm (dhira') and the foot (qadam). The established madhhab (al-madhhab) is that the forearm is 'awrah, based on the clear texts (zahir al-riwayah). However, there is a narration from Abu Yusuf that it is not 'awrah due to necessity for service (such as a maidservant). The author rejects correlation between being 'awrah and being permissible to look; even if not 'awrah, looking may be haram due to fear of fitnah. This principle is emphasized: even a woman's face, though not 'awrah in the Hanafi view, is sometimes prohibited to look at due to fitnah, as stated by later mashayikh for their time. The author then addresses the foot: there are multiple narrations and opinions. Some corrected that it is not 'awrah (Hidayah, Qadikhan, al-Muhit), others that it is 'awrah (al-Aqta', al-Isbijabi, al-Marghinani). A middle view holds it is 'awrah only outside prayer. The preponderant view in Sharh al-Munya is that it is 'awrah absolutely, based on the hadith of Umm Salama requiring the dress to cover the tops of the feet, and the tafsir of the verse of hijab. The author then discusses the hair: flowing hair (mustarsil) has two narrations, but the correct view in al-Muhit is that it is 'awrah. He then moves to the voice (naghama). In al-Nawazil, a woman's melodic tone is considered 'awrah, and it is built upon that it is preferable for a woman to learn the Quran from a woman rather than a blind man (who cannot see her but can hear her). The hadith about tasbih for men and clapping for women indicates that women should not be heard. However, Sharh al-Munya argues that the voice itself is not 'awrah, but rather leads to fitnah, and the prohibition is due to the danger of temptation. This nuance is important: the same practical ruling (do not raise her voice) but different legal cause. The passage then covers the 'awrah of young children: for prepubescent boys and girls, the 'awrah is only the private parts (front and back). After age ten (when puberty may begin), it becomes like an adult. Regarding severed parts of the 'awrah (e.g., amputated breast), there are two narrations: one permits looking (like saliva), the other prohibits (the correct view). Similarly for a man's severed penis or shaved pubic hair. Finally, the author discusses the ruling when a quarter of a part that is 'awrah is exposed. The Hanafi view is that a small amount (less than a quarter) is forgiven due to necessity, like minor impurity. If a quarter or more is exposed, the prayer becomes invalid. This is likened to the head in ihram: shaving a quarter of the head requires dam (expiation) just like shaving the whole head. The author refutes al-Karkhi's analogy to thick impurity (which is forgiven if less than a dirham's area) because the 'awrah ruling is based on the organ's importance, not area.

Key Terms
عورة ('awrah): Parts of the body that must be concealed in prayer and from those to whom it is unlawful to look.
ابتلاء (ibtila'): Hardship or trial, used here as reason to exempt certain body parts from being 'awrah due to frequent need to expose them (e.g., feet of poor women).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preponderant Hanafi view in this passage, what is the ruling on the forearm of a woman in prayer?
A) It is not 'awrah.
B) It is 'awrah.
C) It is 'awrah only outside prayer.
D) It depends on the need.

Key Takeaway
The forearm is 'awrah by clear text, but necessity can be considered in exceptional cases.

The Foot as 'Awrah: Evidence and Tarjih
Ruling on foot with inter-Hanafi dispute and dalil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preponderant Hanafi view on the foot as 'awrah and evaluate the evidence from hadith and tafsir.

Core Idea
The foot is 'awrah by clear hadith and tafsir, despite hardship for the poor.

The foot (qadam) of a woman in prayer is a disputed issue within the Hanafi school. Some scholars exempted it due to hardship (ibtila'), especially for poor women. Others held it is 'awrah based on the hadith of Umm Salama and the tafsir of the hijab verse. This lesson examines the evidence and the preponderant view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Is the foot 'awrah? There are multiple narrations from Abu Hanifa and later scholars.
Some say not 'awrah, some say 'awrah in prayer only, some say absolutely.
2
Examine the easing view
Those who exempt the foot cite hardship (ibtila') for poor women.
This view is found in al-Hidayah and chosen by Qadikhan.
3
Examine the stricter view
The foot is 'awrah based on the hadith requiring covering the tops of the feet and the tafsir of A'isha and Ibn Abbas.
This view is chosen by al-Isbijabi, al-Marghinani, and Sharh al-Munya.
4
Analyze the hadith
The hadith of Umm Salama: 'If the shift is long enough to cover the tops of her feet,' indicates the feet must be covered.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and al-Hakim.
5
Determine the tarjih
Sharh al-Munya gives preponderance to the view that the foot is 'awrah absolutely.
This is the mufta bihi according to later scholars.
