والمذهب بالنص، وهذا الابتلاء كما هو متحقق في باطن الكف متحقق في ظاهرها . خلافه. وللتنصيص على أن الذراع عورة وعن أبي يوسف ليس بعورة واختاره في الاختيار للحاجة إلى كشفه للخدمة، ولأنه من الزينة الظاهرة وهو السوار. وصحح في المبسوط أنه عورة وصحح بعضهم أنه عورة في الصلاة لا خارجها، والمذهب ما في المتون لأنه ظاهر الرواية كما صرح به في شرح منية المصلي. واعلم أنه لا ملازمة بين كونه ليس بعورة وجواز النظر إليه، فحل النظر منوط بعدم خشية الشهوة مع انتفاء العورة، ولذا حرم النظر إلى وجهها ووجه الأمرد . رد إذا شك في الشهوة ولا عورة. كذا في شرح المنية. قال مشايخنا : تمنع المرأة الشابة من كشف وجهها بين الرجال في زماننا للفتنة. وشمل كلامه الشعر المسترسل وفيه روايتان وفي المحيط والأصح أنه عورة. وأما غسله في الجنابة فموضوع على الصحيح. واستثنى المصنف القدم للابتلاء في إبدائه خصوصاً الفقيرات وفيه اختلاف الرواية عن أبي حنيفة والمشايخ فصحح في الهداية وشرح الجامع الصغير لقاضيخان أنه ليس بعورة واختاره في المحيط، وصحح الأقطع وقاضيخان في فتاواه على أنه عورة، واختاره الاسبيجابي والمرغياني. وصحح صاحب الاختيار أنه ليس بعورة في الصلاة وعورة خارجها، ورجح في شرح المنية كونه عورة مطلقاً بأحاديث منها ما رواه أبو داود والحاكم عن أم سلمة أنها سألت النبي أتصلي المرأة في درع وخمار وليس عليها إزار ؟ فقال : إذا كان الدرع سابغاً يغطي ظهور قدميها ولظاهر الآية على ما تقدم من تفسيرها عن عائشة وابن عباس موقوفاً ومرفوعاً .. وصرح في النوازل بأن نغمة المرأة عورة وبنى عليه أن تعلمها القرآن من المرأة أحب إلي من تعلمها من الأعمى ولهذا قال صلى الله عليه وسلم التسبيح للرجال والتصفيق للنساء» فلا يجوز أن يسمعها الرجل ومشى عليه المصنف في الكافي فقال : ولا تلبي جهراً لأن صوتها عورة. ومشى عليه صاحب المحيط في باب الأذان وفي فتح القدير : على هذا لو قيل إذا جهرت بالقرآن في الصلاة فسدت كان متجهاً ا وفي شرح المنية : الأشبه أن صوتها ليس بعورة وإنما يؤدّي إلى الفتنة كما علل به صاحب الهداية وغيره في مسألة التلبية، ولعلهن إنما منعن من رفع الصوت بالتسبيح في الصلاة لهذا المعنى ولا يلزم من حرمة رفع صوتها بحضرة الأجانب أن يكون عورة كما قدمناه وفي الظهيرية الصغيرة جداً لا تكون عورة ولا بأس بالنظر إليها ومسها . وفي السراج الوهاج وأما عورة الصبي والصبية فما داما لم يشتهيا فالقبل والدبر ثم يتغلظ بعد ذلك إلى عشر سنين، ثم يكون كعورة البالغين لأن ذلك زمان يمكن بلوغ المرأة فيه وكل عضو هو عورة من المرأة إذا انفصل منها هل يجوز النظر إليه ؟ فيه روايتان إحداهما يجوز كما يجوز النظر إلى ريقها ودمعها والثانية لا يجوز وهو الأصح، وكذا الذكر المقطوع من الرجل وشعر عانته إذا حلق والأصح أنه لا يجوز. قوله : (وكشف ربع ساقها يمنع وكذا الشعر والبطن والفخذ والعورة الغليظة) لأن قليل الانكشاف عفو عندنا للضرورة فإن ثياب الفقراء لا تخلو عن قليل خرق كالنجاسة القليلة والكثير مفسد لعدمها فاعتبر الربع وأقيم مقام الكل احتياطاً لأن للربع شبهاً بالكل كما في الرأس فإنه يجب به الدم كما لو حلق كله وأما ما وقع في الهداية من التشبيه ربع الرأس ففيه إشكال فإنه لم يكن الواجب فيه مسح جميع الرأس لأن النص لم يتناول إلا بمسح البعض. أما في الإحرام فالنص تناوله كله قال الله تعالى ولا تحلقوا رؤوسكم﴾ [البقرة: ١٩٦] فأقيم ربعه مقام كله أطلق في الشعر فشمل ما على الرأس والمسترسل، وفي الثاني خلاف وقد قدمنا أن الصحيح أنه عورة. وأراد بالغليظة القبل والدبر وما حولهما، والخفيفة ما عدا ذلك من الرجل والمرأة. ونص على الغليظة . للرد على الكرخي القائل بأنه يعتبر في الغليظة ما زاد على قدر الدرهم قياساً على النجاسة المغلظة قال المصنف في الكافي : وهذا ليس بقوي لأنه قصد به التغليظ في الغليظة وهو في الحقيقة تخفيف لأنه اعتبر في الدبر أكثر من قدر الدرهم والدبر لا يكون أكثر منه ، فهذا يقتضي جواز الصلاة وإن كان الكل مكشوفاً وهو تناقض، وقد أجاب عنه في فتح القدير بأنه قد قيل الغليظة القبل والدبر مع ما حولهما
And the madhhab is by the text, and this trial (ibtila) as it is realized in the inner palm is realized in its outer side. Otherwise. And for the specification that the forearm is awrah, and from Abu Yusuf it is not awrah, and he chose it in al-Ikhtiyar due to the need to uncover it for service, and because it is from the apparent adornment, which is the bracelet. And it was corrected in al-Mabsut that it is awrah, and some corrected that it is awrah in prayer but not outside it, and the madhhab is what is in the texts because it is the apparent narration as clarified in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And know that there is no correlation between it not being awrah and the permissibility of looking at it, so the permissibility of looking is contingent on the absence of fear of desire along with the negation of awrah, and for this reason looking at her face and the face of an amrad is prohibited, if there is doubt about desire even if there is no awrah. Thus in Sharh al-Munya. Our mashayikh said: A young woman is prevented from uncovering her face among men in our time due to fitnah. And his speech includes the flowing hair, and there are two narrations, and in al-Muhit the correct view is that it is awrah. As for washing it in janabah, it is based on the correct view. And the author excluded the foot due to trial in exposing it, especially for poor women, and there is difference in narration from Abu Hanifa and the mashayikh, so in al-Hidayah and Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir for Qadikhan it is corrected that it is not awrah, and he chose it in al-Muhit, and al-Aqta' and Qadikhan in his fatawa corrected that it is awrah, and al-Isbijabi and al-Marghinani chose it. And the author of al-Ikhtiyar corrected that it is not awrah in prayer and awrah outside it, and in Sharh al-Munya he gave preponderance to it being awrah absolutely with hadith including that narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim from Umm Salama that she asked the Prophet, 'Can a woman pray in a shift and a headcover without a waist-wrapper?' He said, 'If the shift is long enough to cover the tops of her feet,' and due to the apparent meaning of the verse according to its interpretation from A'isha and Ibn Abbas as a mawquf and marfu'. And it is stated explicitly in al-Nawazil that the vocal tone (naghama) of a woman is awrah, and he built upon it that teaching her the Quran by a woman is more beloved to me than teaching her by a blind man, and for this reason the Prophet said, 'Tasbih is for men and clapping for women,' so it is not permissible for a man to hear it, and the author acted upon it in al-Kafi when he said, 'And she should not recite the talbiyah loudly because her voice is awrah.' And the author of al-Muhit acted upon it in the chapter of adhan, and in Fath al-Qadir: based on this, if it is said that if she recites the Quran aloud in prayer the prayer becomes invalid, it would be pertinent... And in Sharh al-Munya: the more similar view is that her voice is not awrah, but rather it leads to fitnah, as al-Hidayah's author and others reasoned in the issue of talbiyah, and perhaps women are prevented from raising the voice in tasbih in prayer for this meaning, and it does not follow from the prohibition of her raising her voice in the presence of strangers that it is awrah, as we have mentioned. And in al-Zahiriyya: a very young girl's awrah is not awrah and there is no harm in looking at her or touching her. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: as for the awrah of a boy and girl, as long as they have not reached the age of desire, it is the front and back. Then it becomes more severe after that until ten years, then it becomes like that of an adult, because that is the time when a woman can reach puberty. And regarding any organ that is awrah of a woman if it is separated from her, is it permissible to look at it? There are two narrations: one permits it just as it is permissible to look at her saliva and tears, and the second does not permit it, and that is the correct view. Likewise the severed penis of a man and his pubic hair when shaved, and the correct view is that it is not permissible. His statement: 'And uncovering a quarter of her shin prevents, and likewise the hair, belly, thigh, and the thick awrah' because little uncovering is forgiven according to us due to necessity, for the clothes of the poor are not free from small holes like light impurity, and much is invalidating, so the quarter is considered and it is established in place of the whole as a precaution, because the quarter resembles the whole, as in the head where it necessitates blood if he shaves a quarter of it. And regarding what occurred in al-Hidayah of analogy to a quarter of the head, there is an issue, for the obligation there was not to wipe the entire head because the text only addressed wiping a part. As for ihram, the text addressed all of it: Allah said, 'And do not shave your heads' [2:196], so its quarter was established in place of the whole. He spoke generally about hair so it includes what is on the head and flowing, and regarding the second there is a difference and we have already mentioned that the correct view is that it is awrah. And by 'thick awrah' he meant the front and back and what is around them, and by 'light awrah' everything else from the man and woman. And he specified the thick one to refute al-Karkhi who said that in the thick one what exceeds a dirham is considered by analogy to thick impurity. The author said in al-Kafi: This is not strong because he intended to make it strict in the thick, but in reality it is a concession because he considered in the anus more than a dirham, and the anus is not more than that, so this would permit prayer even if all was uncovered, which is contradictory. And Fath al-Qadir responded that it was said that the thick awrah is the front and back with what surrounds them.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addresses the rulings of 'awrah for women in the Hanafi school, particularly in the context of prayer. The author begins by discussing the forearm (dhira') and the foot (qadam). The established madhhab (al-madhhab) is that the forearm is 'awrah, based on the clear texts (zahir al-riwayah). However, there is a narration from Abu Yusuf that it is not 'awrah due to necessity for service (such as a maidservant). The author rejects correlation between being 'awrah and being permissible to look; even if not 'awrah, looking may be haram due to fear of fitnah. This principle is emphasized: even a woman's face, though not 'awrah in the Hanafi view, is sometimes prohibited to look at due to fitnah, as stated by later mashayikh for their time. The author then addresses the foot: there are multiple narrations and opinions. Some corrected that it is not 'awrah (Hidayah, Qadikhan, al-Muhit), others that it is 'awrah (al-Aqta', al-Isbijabi, al-Marghinani). A middle view holds it is 'awrah only outside prayer. The preponderant view in Sharh al-Munya is that it is 'awrah absolutely, based on the hadith of Umm Salama requiring the dress to cover the tops of the feet, and the tafsir of the verse of hijab. The author then discusses the hair: flowing hair (mustarsil) has two narrations, but the correct view in al-Muhit is that it is 'awrah. He then moves to the voice (naghama). In al-Nawazil, a woman's melodic tone is considered 'awrah, and it is built upon that it is preferable for a woman to learn the Quran from a woman rather than a blind man (who cannot see her but can hear her). The hadith about tasbih for men and clapping for women indicates that women should not be heard. However, Sharh al-Munya argues that the voice itself is not 'awrah, but rather leads to fitnah, and the prohibition is due to the danger of temptation. This nuance is important: the same practical ruling (do not raise her voice) but different legal cause. The passage then covers the 'awrah of young children: for prepubescent boys and girls, the 'awrah is only the private parts (front and back). After age ten (when puberty may begin), it becomes like an adult. Regarding severed parts of the 'awrah (e.g., amputated breast), there are two narrations: one permits looking (like saliva), the other prohibits (the correct view). Similarly for a man's severed penis or shaved pubic hair. Finally, the author discusses the ruling when a quarter of a part that is 'awrah is exposed. The Hanafi view is that a small amount (less than a quarter) is forgiven due to necessity, like minor impurity. If a quarter or more is exposed, the prayer becomes invalid. This is likened to the head in ihram: shaving a quarter of the head requires dam (expiation) just like shaving the whole head. The author refutes al-Karkhi's analogy to thick impurity (which is forgiven if less than a dirham's area) because the 'awrah ruling is based on the organ's importance, not area.

Key Terms
عورة ('awrah): Parts of the body that must be concealed in prayer and from those to whom it is unlawful to look.
ابتلاء (ibtila'): Hardship or trial, used here as reason to exempt certain body parts from being 'awrah due to frequent need to expose them (e.g., feet of poor women).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preponderant Hanafi view in Sharh al-Munya, what is the ruling on the foot of a woman in prayer?
A) It is not 'awrah.
B) It is 'awrah absolutely.
C) It is 'awrah only outside prayer.
D) It is 'awrah only if she is not poor.

Key Takeaway
The preponderant Hanafi view is that the foot is 'awrah, based on clear textual evidence.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Hair and Voice: Are They 'Awrah?
Ruling on hair as 'awrah and voice dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on hair and voice as 'awrah and distinguish between 'awrah status and prohibition due to fitnah.

Core Idea
Hair is 'awrah; the voice is not 'awrah but may be prohibited due to fitnah.

Hair and voice are two additional aspects of a woman's 'awrah that are discussed in this passage. Hair, including flowing hair, is considered 'awrah according to the correct view. The voice (naghama) raises a different issue: some scholars consider it 'awrah, but the more similar view is that it is not 'awrah, only a source of fitnah. This lesson clarifies the rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on hair
The passage states that flowing hair (al-sha'r al-mustarsil) has two narrations, but the correct view in al-Muhit is that it is 'awrah.
This includes hair on the head.
2
Examine the voice dispute
In al-Nawazil, the melodic tone (naghama) of a woman is considered 'awrah, but Sharh al-Munya disagrees.
The hadith of tasbih and clapping is used.
3
Analyze the evidence for voice
Those who say it is 'awrah cite that teaching by a woman is preferred to a blind man, and the hadith of tasbih. The response is that these only show prohibition, not 'awrah status.
The key difference: 'awrah = must be concealed; fitnah = may be heard but with caution.
4
Apply the principle of fitnah
Even if the voice is not 'awrah, it is prohibited to listen to it if it leads to desire.
This parallels the earlier principle on looking.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi is that the voice is not 'awrah, but it must be guarded against fitnah.
Sharh al-Munya favors this view.

And the madhhab is by the text, and this trial (ibtila) as it is realized in the inner palm is realized in its outer side. Otherwise. And for the specification that the forearm is awrah, and from Abu Yusuf it is not awrah, and he chose it in al-Ikhtiyar due to the need to uncover it for service, and because it is from the apparent adornment, which is the bracelet. And it was corrected in al-Mabsut that it is awrah, and some corrected that it is awrah in prayer but not outside it, and the madhhab is what is in the texts because it is the apparent narration as clarified in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And know that there is no correlation between it not being awrah and the permissibility of looking at it, so the permissibility of looking is contingent on the absence of fear of desire along with the negation of awrah, and for this reason looking at her face and the face of an amrad is prohibited, if there is doubt about desire even if there is no awrah. Thus in Sharh al-Munya. Our mashayikh said: A young woman is prevented from uncovering her face among men in our time due to fitnah. And his speech includes the flowing hair, and there are two narrations, and in al-Muhit the correct view is that it is awrah. As for washing it in janabah, it is based on the correct view. And the author excluded the foot due to trial in exposing it, especially for poor women, and there is difference in narration from Abu Hanifa and the mashayikh, so in al-Hidayah and Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir for Qadikhan it is corrected that it is not awrah, and he chose it in al-Muhit, and al-Aqta' and Qadikhan in his fatawa corrected that it is awrah, and al-Isbijabi and al-Marghinani chose it. And the author of al-Ikhtiyar corrected that it is not awrah in prayer and awrah outside it, and in Sharh al-Munya he gave preponderance to it being awrah absolutely with hadith including that narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim from Umm Salama that she asked the Prophet, 'Can a woman pray in a shift and a headcover without a waist-wrapper?' He said, 'If the shift is long enough to cover the tops of her feet,' and due to the apparent meaning of the verse according to its interpretation from A'isha and Ibn Abbas as a mawquf and marfu'. And it is stated explicitly in al-Nawazil that the vocal tone (naghama) of a woman is awrah, and he built upon it that teaching her the Quran by a woman is more beloved to me than teaching her by a blind man, and for this reason the Prophet said, 'Tasbih is for men and clapping for women,' so it is not permissible for a man to hear it, and the author acted upon it in al-Kafi when he said, 'And she should not recite the talbiyah loudly because her voice is awrah.' And the author of al-Muhit acted upon it in the chapter of adhan, and in Fath al-Qadir: based on this, if it is said that if she recites the Quran aloud in prayer the prayer becomes invalid, it would be pertinent... And in Sharh al-Munya: the more similar view is that her voice is not awrah, but rather it leads to fitnah, as al-Hidayah's author and others reasoned in the issue of talbiyah, and perhaps women are prevented from raising the voice in tasbih in prayer for this meaning, and it does not follow from the prohibition of her raising her voice in the presence of strangers that it is awrah, as we have mentioned. And in al-Zahiriyya: a very young girl's awrah is not awrah and there is no harm in looking at her or touching her. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: as for the awrah of a boy and girl, as long as they have not reached the age of desire, it is the front and back. Then it becomes more severe after that until ten years, then it becomes like that of an adult, because that is the time when a woman can reach puberty. And regarding any organ that is awrah of a woman if it is separated from her, is it permissible to look at it? There are two narrations: one permits it just as it is permissible to look at her saliva and tears, and the second does not permit it, and that is the correct view. Likewise the severed penis of a man and his pubic hair when shaved, and the correct view is that it is not permissible. His statement: 'And uncovering a quarter of her shin prevents, and likewise the hair, belly, thigh, and the thick awrah' because little uncovering is forgiven according to us due to necessity, for the clothes of the poor are not free from small holes like light impurity, and much is invalidating, so the quarter is considered and it is established in place of the whole as a precaution, because the quarter resembles the whole, as in the head where it necessitates blood if he shaves a quarter of it. And regarding what occurred in al-Hidayah of analogy to a quarter of the head, there is an issue, for the obligation there was not to wipe the entire head because the text only addressed wiping a part. As for ihram, the text addressed all of it: Allah said, 'And do not shave your heads' [2:196], so its quarter was established in place of the whole. He spoke generally about hair so it includes what is on the head and flowing, and regarding the second there is a difference and we have already mentioned that the correct view is that it is awrah. And by 'thick awrah' he meant the front and back and what is around them, and by 'light awrah' everything else from the man and woman. And he specified the thick one to refute al-Karkhi who said that in the thick one what exceeds a dirham is considered by analogy to thick impurity. The author said in al-Kafi: This is not strong because he intended to make it strict in the thick, but in reality it is a concession because he considered in the anus more than a dirham, and the anus is not more than that, so this would permit prayer even if all was uncovered, which is contradictory. And Fath al-Qadir responded that it was said that the thick awrah is the front and back with what surrounds them.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addresses the rulings of 'awrah for women in the Hanafi school, particularly in the context of prayer. The author begins by discussing the forearm (dhira') and the foot (qadam). The established madhhab (al-madhhab) is that the forearm is 'awrah, based on the clear texts (zahir al-riwayah). However, there is a narration from Abu Yusuf that it is not 'awrah due to necessity for service (such as a maidservant). The author rejects correlation between being 'awrah and being permissible to look; even if not 'awrah, looking may be haram due to fear of fitnah. This principle is emphasized: even a woman's face, though not 'awrah in the Hanafi view, is sometimes prohibited to look at due to fitnah, as stated by later mashayikh for their time. The author then addresses the foot: there are multiple narrations and opinions. Some corrected that it is not 'awrah (Hidayah, Qadikhan, al-Muhit), others that it is 'awrah (al-Aqta', al-Isbijabi, al-Marghinani). A middle view holds it is 'awrah only outside prayer. The preponderant view in Sharh al-Munya is that it is 'awrah absolutely, based on the hadith of Umm Salama requiring the dress to cover the tops of the feet, and the tafsir of the verse of hijab. The author then discusses the hair: flowing hair (mustarsil) has two narrations, but the correct view in al-Muhit is that it is 'awrah. He then moves to the voice (naghama). In al-Nawazil, a woman's melodic tone is considered 'awrah, and it is built upon that it is preferable for a woman to learn the Quran from a woman rather than a blind man (who cannot see her but can hear her). The hadith about tasbih for men and clapping for women indicates that women should not be heard. However, Sharh al-Munya argues that the voice itself is not 'awrah, but rather leads to fitnah, and the prohibition is due to the danger of temptation. This nuance is important: the same practical ruling (do not raise her voice) but different legal cause. The passage then covers the 'awrah of young children: for prepubescent boys and girls, the 'awrah is only the private parts (front and back). After age ten (when puberty may begin), it becomes like an adult. Regarding severed parts of the 'awrah (e.g., amputated breast), there are two narrations: one permits looking (like saliva), the other prohibits (the correct view). Similarly for a man's severed penis or shaved pubic hair. Finally, the author discusses the ruling when a quarter of a part that is 'awrah is exposed. The Hanafi view is that a small amount (less than a quarter) is forgiven due to necessity, like minor impurity. If a quarter or more is exposed, the prayer becomes invalid. This is likened to the head in ihram: shaving a quarter of the head requires dam (expiation) just like shaving the whole head. The author refutes al-Karkhi's analogy to thick impurity (which is forgiven if less than a dirham's area) because the 'awrah ruling is based on the organ's importance, not area.

Key Terms
نغمة (naghama): A melodious or soft tone of voice that may incite desire.
عورة ('awrah): Parts of the body that must be concealed in prayer and from those to whom it is unlawful to look.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preponderant Hanafi view in Sharh al-Munya, what is the status of a woman's voice?
A) It is 'awrah and must be completely hidden.
B) It is not 'awrah, but it may lead to fitnah.
C) It is 'awrah only when singing.
D) It is permissible in all circumstances.

Key Takeaway
Hair is 'awrah; the voice is not, but must be guarded against fitnah.

The Quarter Rule and Related 'Awrah Rulings
Rule on quarter exposure and related 'awrah rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi quarter rule for exposure of 'awrah in prayer and identify the rulings for children and severed parts.

Core Idea
Exposing a quarter or more of an 'awrah part invalidates prayer; small amounts are forgiven.

The Hanafi school has a specific threshold for when exposure of 'awrah invalidates prayer: a quarter of the exposed part. This lesson also covers the 'awrah of children and rulings on severed body parts. The passage refutes an analogy to impurity, emphasizing the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the quarter rule
The passage states that uncovering a quarter of a limb that is 'awrah (e.g., shin) prevents the validity of prayer. Less than a quarter is forgiven due to necessity.
This is analogous to the head in ihram.
2
Apply to different parts
The rule applies to hair, belly, thigh, and the thick 'awrah (private parts). For each, if a quarter is exposed, prayer is invalid.
The thick 'awrah is the front and back.
3
Learn the children's 'awrah
For prepubescent children (before age of desire), only the private parts are 'awrah. After ten, it becomes like an adult.
This is from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
4
Note the rulings on severed parts
If an organ that is 'awrah is separated from the body (e.g., amputated), the correct view is that it is not permissible to look at it, unlike saliva or tears.
There is a difference of opinion.
5
Analyze the refutation of al-Karkhi
Al-Karkhi compared 'awrah exposure to impurity (najasa), but the refutation shows that the quarter rule is based on strictness, not leniency.
The analogy is weak because it would allow all exposure of the anus.

ولهذا قال صلى الله عليه وسلم التسبيح للرجال والتصفيق للنساء» فلا يجوز أن يسمعها الرجل ومشى عليه المصنف في الكافي فقال : ولا تلبي جهراً لأن صوتها عورة. ومشى عليه صاحب المحيط في باب الأذان وفي فتح القدير : على هذا لو قيل إذا جهرت بالقرآن في الصلاة فسدت كان متجهاً ا وفي شرح المنية : الأشبه أن صوتها ليس بعورة وإنما يؤدّي إلى الفتنة كما علل به صاحب الهداية وغيره في مسألة التلبية، ولعلهن إنما منعن Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addresses the rulings of 'awrah for women in the Hanafi school, particularly in the context of prayer. The author begins by discussing the forearm (dhira') and the foot (qadam). The established madhhab (al-madhhab) is that the forearm is 'awrah, based on the clear texts (zahir al-riwayah). However, there is a narration from Abu Yusuf that it is not 'awrah due to necessity for service (such as a maidservant). The author rejects correlation between being 'awrah and being permissible to look; even if not 'awrah, looking may be haram due to fear of fitnah. This principle is emphasized: even a woman's face, though not 'awrah in the Hanafi view, is sometimes prohibited to look at due to fitnah, as stated by later mashayikh for their time. The author then addresses the foot: there are multiple narrations and opinions. Some corrected that it is not 'awrah (Hidayah, Qadikhan, al-Muhit), others that it is 'awrah (al-Aqta', al-Isbijabi, al-Marghinani). A middle view holds it is 'awrah only outside prayer. The preponderant view in Sharh al-Munya is that it is 'awrah absolutely, based on the hadith of Umm Salama requiring the dress to cover the tops of the feet, and the tafsir of the verse of hijab. The author then discusses the hair: flowing hair (mustarsil) has two narrations, but the correct view in al-Muhit is that it is 'awrah. He then moves to the voice (naghama). In al-Nawazil, a woman's melodic tone is considered 'awrah, and it is built upon that it is preferable for a woman to learn the Quran from a woman rather than a blind man (who cannot see her but can hear her). The hadith about tasbih for men and clapping for women indicates that women should not be heard. However, Sharh al-Munya argues that the voice itself is not 'awrah, but rather leads to fitnah, and the prohibition is due to the danger of temptation. This nuance is important: the same practical ruling (do not raise her voice) but different legal cause. The passage then covers the 'awrah of young children: for prepubescent boys and girls, the 'awrah is only the private parts (front and back). After age ten (when puberty may begin), it becomes like an adult. Regarding severed parts of the 'awrah (e.g., amputated breast), there are two narrations: one permits looking (like saliva), the other prohibits (the correct view). Similarly for a man's severed penis or shaved pubic hair. Finally, the author discusses the ruling when a quarter of a part that is 'awrah is exposed. The Hanafi view is that a small amount (less than a quarter) is forgiven due to necessity, like minor impurity. If a quarter or more is exposed, the prayer becomes invalid. This is likened to the head in ihram: shaving a quarter of the head requires dam (expiation) just like shaving the whole head. The author refutes al-Karkhi's analogy to thick impurity (which is forgiven if less than a dirham's area) because the 'awrah ruling is based on the organ's importance, not area.

Key Terms
ربع (rub'): The quarter of a limb or organ; exposing a quarter or more of an 'awrah part invalidates prayer.
عورة ('awrah): Parts of the body that must be concealed in prayer and from those to whom it is unlawful to look.
غليظة (ghalizah): Thick 'awrah: the front and back private parts and surrounding areas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum exposure of an 'awrah part that invalidates prayer?
A) Any exposure.
B) Half of the part.
C) A quarter of the part.
D) More than a dirham in area.

Key Takeaway
Exposing a quarter or more of an 'awrah part in prayer invalidates it; small amounts are forgiven.

The Quarter Rule for Awrah Exposure: Proof and Dispute
Commentary on the quarter threshold for awrah exposure, with qiyas proof and refutation of al-Karkhi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi quarter rule for awrah exposure and explain why al-Karkhi's analogy to heavy impurity is rejected.

Core Idea
Exposure of a quarter of any awrah limb invalidates prayer; less is excused, like minor impurity.

Covering the awrah is a condition for valid prayer, but Hanafi law excuses minor exposure due to necessity. This lesson examines the precise threshold—a quarter of a limb—its analogical proof from impurity, the intra-Hanafi dispute with al-Karkhi, and how to calculate exposure across multiple limbs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is prayer; covering the awrah is a condition (shart). Exposure beyond a quarter invalidates (mufsid) prayer. Small amounts are excused (ma'fu 'anhu).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to impurity (najasa) on clothing: a small amount is excused, a large amount invalidates prayer.
The quarter threshold is established by treating a quarter as equivalent to the whole limb, out of precaution (ihtiyat).
3
Examine the 'illa (effective cause)
Both exposure of awrah and impurity are deficiencies (naqs) that prevent perfection of prayer. The 'illa is the presence of a deficiency that is normally avoidable but minor amounts are unavoidable in daily life.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with al-Karkhi
Al-Karkhi analogized thick awrah (genitals) to heavy impurity (najasa mughallaza), requiring a dirham-sized exposure to invalidate. The author refutes this: the anus is always smaller than a dirham, so this would permit all exposure—a contradiction.
The Hanafi ruling remains that any quarter of a limb (including thick awrah) invalidates.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that quarter of any awrah limb invalidates. For multiple limbs, one gathers exposures; if the total equals a quarter of the smallest exposed limb, prayer is invalid.
This is confirmed by al-Ziyadat and al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

And likewise hair, belly, thigh, and thick private part prevent (prayer validity). And the female slave is like a man regarding her back and belly. She recited aloud in prayer, then it becomes invalid; it was directed. In Sharh al-Munyah: The more correct view is that her voice is not awrah, but it leads to fitna, as the author of Hidayah and others reasoned in the matter of talbiyah. Perhaps they prohibited them from raising voices in takbir in prayer for this meaning, and it does not follow from the prohibition of raising her voice in front of non-mahrams that it is awrah, as we have mentioned earlier. In al-Zahiriyyah: A very young girl does not have awrah, and there is no problem looking at her or touching her. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: As for the awrah of a boy and girl, as long as they do not desire, it is the front and back; then it becomes stricter after that until ten years; then it becomes like the awrah of adults, because that is the time when a woman could possibly reach puberty. Every limb that is awrah of a woman, if it is separated from her, is it permissible to look at it? In it two narrations: one permits, as it is permissible to look at her saliva and tears; the second does not permit, and it is the most correct. Similarly, a severed male organ from a man and his pubic hair if shaved: the most correct is that it is not permissible. His saying: (Exposing a quarter of her shin prevents, and likewise hair, belly, thigh, and thick awrah) because a small amount of exposure is excused according to us due to necessity, for the clothes of the poor are not free of a small tear, like a small impurity, and much invalidates due to its absence; so a quarter is considered and made to stand in place of the whole out of precaution because the quarter resembles the whole, as in the head, where a blood penalty becomes obligatory as if he shaved all of it. But what occurred in al-Hidayah of analogy to a quarter of the head has difficulty, because wiping all the head was not obligatory, since the text only required wiping part. But in ihram, the text encompassed all: Allah said, 'And do not shave your heads' [al-Baqarah 196], so a quarter is made to stand in place of the whole. It is general regarding hair, covering what is on the head and the hanging part. On the second there is a difference, and we have already stated that the correct view is that it is awrah. He meant by 'thick' the front and back (private parts) and what is around them, and 'thin' is everything else from both men and women. He specified 'thick' to refute al-Karkhi who says that in thick awrah, more than a dirham's amount is considered, by analogy to heavy impurity. The author said in al-Kafi: This is not strong because he intended to make thick awrah strict, but it is actually a leniency, because he considered in the back (anus) more than a dirham, and the back cannot be more than that. This would imply the validity of prayer even if all of it is exposed, which is contradictory. In Fath al-Qadir he replied: It has been said that the thick is the front and back with what is around them. Shaving awrah: we mean by that her speech, because that is not correct, for we allow talking with foreign women and conversing with them when there is need, but we do not allow them to raise their voices, nor stretch, soften, or cut them, because that attracts men and moves desires. Hence, a woman is not allowed to give adhan. This indicates that the awrah is raising the voice that usually has melody, not absolute speech. Since recitation is not free of that, he said: 'I prefer' - so contemplate. His saying: (And in Sharh al-Munyah, etc.): In al-Nahr: It is what should be relied upon. His saying: (Then it becomes stricter after that until ten years): In al-Nahr: It should have considered seven, because they are commanded to pray at that age. His saying: (It is strange) i.e., what he replied in Fath al-Qadir, because what he transmitted from prayer. [PAGE_472] Book of Prayer - Chapter on Conditions of Prayer. ...so it is possible he considered that, so the objection does not apply. It is strange because it is not understood from what was said that the whole is one limb, but rather clarification of the thick awrah. How can it be when they explicitly said that both the penis and testicles are independent limbs? And it is declared correct in al-Hidayah and al-Khaniyyah because each of them is considered a separate limb in diyah, so likewise here for precaution. In one narration, the whole is one limb. In any case, no one said that the front and back are one limb, unless it is said that he meant the front with its surroundings is one limb, and the back with its surroundings is one limb. As for the knee with the thigh, the correct view is that they are one limb, as in al-Tanjis, and it is the chosen view as in al-Khulasa, because the knee is the meeting point of the shin and thigh bones, so it is not an independent limb in reality. It is made awrah following the thigh out of precaution. Therefore, if he prayed with his knees exposed and the thigh covered, it is permissible. Similarly in al-Munyah. In its commentary: The correct view is that the ankle is not an independent limb but is one limb with the shin. Therefore, only a quarter of the shin with a quarter of the ankle or the amount of a quarter of both prevents. The anus is one limb, and each buttock is one limb - this is the most correct. Each ear is a separate limb. A woman's breast if it is nihadah (firm) is following her chest; if it is munkasirah (sagging) it is an origin in itself. Nihadah means protruding from the chest, not relaxed. 'Thady' can be masculine or feminine, masculine is more famous; al-Mughrib only mentions masculine. The area between the navel and pubis is one limb, intended around the entire body. As in al-Muhit. In al-Ziyadat: A woman prayed, and something of her thigh, something of her shin, something of her chest, and something of her thick awrah were exposed. If gathered, it reached a quarter of a small limb among them, her prayer is not valid at the time of exposure, as if from one limb. So they gather like scattered impurity in places, and perfume for a muhrim in places, unlike holes as we mentioned in wiping over khuffs. The commentator mentioned that it should be... because all the limbs... the statement is clarification of the thick awrah, and that does not imply the whole is one limb, since no one said the front and back are one limb. His saying: (And the commentator mentioned, etc.). In al-Nahr after mentioning the expression of al-Zayla'i and it is approved in Fath al-Qadir and others, he said in 'Uqad al-Fara'id: His apparent understanding is that the rule is that the invalidator is only a quarter of what is exposed. This is contrary because the invalidator is like that only if the exposure is in one limb, and there it is considered in parts, as if his thigh is exposed in multiple places. In our scenario, exposure occurs in multiple limbs, each of which is awrah, and precaution is to consider the smallest of them, because by it the obstacle exists. So one looks at the amount exposed from all of them. If it reaches the exposure of the smallest of them, it invalidates out of precaution; otherwise, it would necessitate validity of prayer with a quarter of a quarter of awrah from the exposed, which is the transmitted rule from Muhammad, and this follows from the consideration in parts, and no one says it. So when you realize this, it becomes clear that what Ibn al-Malik said is in agreement with al-Ziyadat. His statement in al-Bahr that it is a detail without evidence is not accepted. Badī' al-Dīn said: What is in al-Ziyadat is a text on two matters that people are heedless of: one is that the gathering is not restricted to parts like sixths and eighths but by amount; the second is that the exposed from all if it is the amount of a quarter...
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on conditions of prayer, specifically on awrah exposure. It addresses multiple rulings regarding what counts as awrah and how much exposure invalidates prayer. The author begins by stating that exposing a quarter of certain body parts (shin, hair, belly, thigh, thick private part) prevents validity of prayer. The basis for quarter threshold is necessity: minor exposure is excused like minor impurity, but a quarter is treated as the whole for precaution. Then it discusses the awrah of a woman's voice, children's awrah, and severed private parts. The main focus is the dispute with al-Karkhi, who analogized thick awrah to heavy impurity requiring a dirham amount. The author refutes this, showing it leads to contradiction. Then it explains that the 'thick awrah' refers to the front and back and their surroundings. The passage then discusses whether different body parts are considered one member or separate for exposure calculation. For example, the knee is part of the thigh; the ankle is part of the shin. It emphasizes that each ear is separate, the anus and buttock are separate. Finally, it presents a scenario from al-Ziyadat where a woman's exposure in multiple limbs (thigh, shin, chest, thick awrah) is gathered, and if it reaches a quarter of the smallest limb, the prayer is invalid. This is because the effect is like impurity scattered in multiple places. The commentator then critiques a previous understanding that the invalidator is always a quarter of the exposed area; instead, for multiple members, the smallest member's quarter is the threshold.

Key Terms
العورة الغليظة (al-'awrah al-ghalizah): The thick awrah: the front and back private parts (genitals and anus) and their surroundings.
ربع (rub'): Quarter of a limb; used as the threshold for significant exposure that invalidates prayer.
الانکشاف (al-inkishaf): Exposure of awrah; if it reaches a quarter of a limb, it invalidates prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a woman prays and a quarter of one of her limbs' awrah is exposed, but she had multiple exposures totalling a quarter of her smallest limb, what is the ruling?
A) Her prayer is valid because each exposure is less than a quarter.
B) Her prayer is invalid because the total exposure reaches the quarter of the smallest limb.
C) Her prayer is valid only if the exposure is from the same limb.
D) Her prayer is invalid only if the thick awrah is exposed.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, exposure of a quarter of any awrah limb invalidates prayer; for multiple limbs, the total exposure is compared to the quarter of the smallest limb.

Slave Woman Freed Mid-Prayer: Covering the Head
Ruling with proof on slave freed during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a slave woman's prayer when she is freed during prayer and apply the conditions (action size, timing, and knowledge) to determine whether her prayer is valid or requires repetition.

Core Idea
A slave freed mid-prayer may continue if she covers her head with a small action before the next pillar; knowledge of freedom is a point of ikhtilaf.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific scenario: an enslaved woman (whose awrah excludes the head in the Hanafi school) is freed while performing salah. She must now cover her head, but the timing and nature of her action—and whether she knew of her emancipation—affect the validity of her prayer. We will unpack the conditions, the intra-madhhab dispute, and the preferred ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and baseline ruling
Recognize that the scenario is a slave woman whose head is uncovered during prayer due to her initial status. Upon emancipation, her awrah changes, and she must cover. The baseline ruling is that covering with a small action before the next rukn renders her prayer valid; otherwise it is invalid.
The head of a slave woman is not awrah in the Hanafi school, so she was allowed to pray uncovered before emancipation.
2
Locate the conditions for validity
The text specifies two conditions: (1) the covering action must be 'small' (qalil), not 'large' (kathir), and (2) it must occur before performing the next rukn (pillar). If she covers after a rukn or with a large action, the prayer is invalid.
A small action is one that does not disrupt the prayer's form, e.g., pulling a cloth over the head with one hand.
3
Examine the dispute over knowledge of emancipation
Al-Zayla'i conditions that she must have knowledge (ilm) of her freedom before performing the next pillar. However, explicit texts in al-Mujtaba and Fatawa Qadikhan indicate that knowledge is irrelevant: if her awrah is uncovered and she performs a rukn, the prayer is invalid regardless of knowledge.
Al-Zayla'i's view is derived from analogy to a person who becomes Muslim during prayer.
4
Analyze the proofs from the texts
Al-Mujtaba states: if a slave prayed for a month without a headcover and later learned she was freed at the beginning, she must repeat all those prayers. Fatawa Qadikhan states: if anyone's awrah becomes uncovered and they perform a rukn, the prayer is invalid whether they knew or not. The author considers these explicit statements (mantuq) stronger than the implicit understanding (mafhum mukhalaf) from al-Zayla'i.
5
Determine the tarjih and practical consequence
The author prefers the view that knowledge is not a condition, because the explicit texts are stronger. Therefore, the mufta bihi is that the obligation to cover arises at the moment of emancipation, regardless of knowledge. If she covers immediately with a small action before the next rukn, her prayer is valid; if she does not, she must repeat.
This has significant implications: a slave who remains unaware for months must repeat all prayers from the time of freedom.

عورة أو لا، فذكرت أنه عورة ثم رأيته في القنية قال : الجنب تبع البطن والأوجه أن ما يلي البطن تبع له ا هـ . ولو أعتقت وهي في الصلاة مكشوفة الرأس ونحوه فسترته بعمل قليل قبل أداء ركن جازت لا بكثير أو بعد ركن كذا في كثير من الكتب. وقيده الشارح بأن تؤدي ركناً بعد العلم بالعتق فشرط علمها تبعاً لما في الظهيرية . والمصرح به في المجتبى أنها لو صلت شهراً بغير قناع ثم علمت بالعتق منذ شهر تعيدها. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : إذا انكشفت عورته وأدى ركناً معه فسدت علم بذلك أو لم يعلم، وذكر نحوه مسائل كثيرة . وهذان المنطوقان أوجه من ذلك المفهوم المخالف. وفي عدة :الفتاوى : رجل مات بمكة فلزم امرأة أن تعيد صلاة سنة فقل : هو رجل علق عتق جاريته بموته فمات بمكة وهي لم تعلم بموته وصلت مكشوفة الرأس فإنها تعيد الصلاة من وقت موته ا هـ . . وفي المحيط : بخلاف العاري إذا وجد الكسوة في خلال الصلاة فإنه يلزمه الاستقبال لأنه يلزمه الستر بسبب سابق على الشروع وهو كشف العورة وهو متحقق قبل الصلاة فلما توجه إليه الخطاب بالستر في الصلاة استند إلى سببه فصار كأنه توجه إليه قبل الصلاة وقد تركه بخلافها إذ العتق سبب خطابها بالستر وقد وجد حالة الصلاة وقد سترت كما قدرت وظاهره أنها لو كانت عاجزة عن الستر فلم تستتر كالحرة لا تبطل صلاتها وهو مصرح به في شرح منية المصلي معزياً إلى البدائع. وفي شرح السراج الوهاج : الخنثى إذا كان رقيقاً فعورته عورة الأمة، وإن كان حراً أمرناه أن يستر جميع بدنه لجواز أن يكون امرأة، فإن ستر ما بين سرته إلى ركبته وصلى قال تلزمه الإعادة لجواز أن يكون امرأة، وقال بعضهم لا تلزمه الإعادة لجواز أن يكون بعضهم رجلاً. فرع حسن لم أره منقولاً لأئمتنا وهو مذكور في شرح المهذب : إذا قال لأمته إن صليت صلاة صحيحة فأنت حرة قبلها فصلت مكشوفة الرأس؛ إن كان في حال عجزها عن ستره صحت صلاتها وعتقت وإن كانت قادرة على الستر صحت صلاتها ولا تعتق، لأنها لو عتقت لصارت حرة قبل الصلاة وحينئذ لا تصح صلاتها مكشوفة الرأس، وإذا لم تصح تعتق، فإثبات العتق يؤدي إلى بطلانه وبطلان الصلاة فبطل وصحت الصلاة ا هـ . وسيأتي في الطلاق أن الراجح في مسألة الدور وهي إن طلقتك فأنت طالق ثلاثاً قبله» أن يلغو قوله «قبله» وإذا طلقها وقع الثلاث كما في فتح القدير، فمقتضاه هنا أن يلغو قوله «قبلها» ويقع العتق كما لا يخفى .
Whether it is an awrah or not, he mentioned that it is an awrah then I saw in al-Qunyah: He (al-Quduri) said: the side (janb) follows the belly, and the most correct is that what is adjacent to the belly follows it. And if she is freed while in prayer with her head uncovered and similar, and she covers it with a small action before performing a pillar, it is permissible; not with a large action or after a pillar, as found in many books. The commentator (al-Zayla'i) restricted it by saying: if she performs a pillar after knowing of the emancipation, so condition of her knowledge follows what is in al-Zahiriyyah. What is explicitly stated in al-Mujtaba is that if she prayed for a month without a headcover then learns she was freed a month ago, she repeats them. In Fatawa Qadikhan: If his awrah becomes uncovered and he performs a pillar with it, the prayer is invalidated whether he knew or not, and similar many issues are mentioned. These two explicit statements are stronger than that implicit opposite. In iddat al-Fatawa: A man died in Mecca, so it becomes obligatory for a woman to repeat a year's prayer—I say: He is a man who suspended the emancipation of his slave girl on his death, so he died in Mecca and she did not know of his death and prayed with uncovered head; then she must repeat prayer from the time of his death. In al-Muhit: Contrary to the naked person who finds clothing during prayer, for he must restart because covering is obligatory due to a cause prior to starting, which is uncovering of awrah and it is actualized before prayer; when the address to cover in prayer came, it is based on its cause, so it is as if it was addressed to him before prayer and he left it. Contrary to her, because emancipation is the cause of the address to cover, and it occurred during prayer, and she covered as she was able. Its apparent meaning is that if she was unable to cover and did not cover like a free woman, her prayer is not invalidated, as explicitly stated in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli referencing al-Bada'i. In Sharh al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The hermaphrodite: if a slave, his awrah is that of a slave girl; if free, we order him to cover his entire body because it is possible he is a woman; if he covers from navel to knee and prays, it is said he must repeat because it is possible he is a woman, and some said he does not repeat because it is possible he is a man. A good subsidiary issue I have not seen transmitted from our imams, mentioned in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab: If a man says to his slave girl: 'If you pray a valid prayer, you are free before it,' and she prays with uncovered head: if she is unable to cover, her prayer is valid and she becomes free; if she is able to cover, her prayer is valid and she does not become free, because if she became free, she would be free before the prayer, and then her prayer with uncovered head would not be valid, and if not valid, she becomes free, so proving freedom leads to its invalidation and the prayer's invalidation, so it is invalidated and the prayer is valid. And it will come in the chapter of divorce that the preponderant view in the case of circularity (if I divorce you, you are thrice divorced before it) is that his word 'before it' is canceled, and if he divorces her, the three fall, as in Fath al-Qadir. So by analogy here, his word 'before it' is canceled and the emancipation occurs, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on multiple rulings regarding the awrah of a woman who was a slave and becomes free during prayer. It begins by discussing the definition of 'janb' (side) from al-Qunyah, noting that what is adjacent to the belly follows the belly, and the correct view is that areas adjacent to the belly are part of the belly's coverage, while those adjacent to the back follow the back. The author then addresses the case of an enslaved woman being freed during prayer while her head is uncovered. If she covers her head with a small action before performing a pillar of prayer, the prayer is valid. If she uses a large action or covers after a pillar, it is invalid. The commentator al-Zayla'i conditions that she must have knowledge of the emancipation before performing the next pillar. This condition is supported by al-Zahiriyyah. However, in al-Mujtaba, it is stated that if she prayed for a month without a headcover and later learns she was freed from the beginning of that month, she must repeat all those prayers. In Fatawa Qadikhan, it is ruled that if anyone's awrah becomes uncovered and they perform a pillar with that state, the prayer is invalidated regardless of knowledge. The author prefers these explicit texts over the implicit understanding from al-Zayla'i. Then a case from iddat al-Fatawa: a man dies in Mecca, and his female relative must repeat a year's prayer; but the author clarifies this concerns a slave girl whose emancipation was tied to his death, and she prayed without knowledge, so she must repeat from the time of death. Next, a comparison with a naked person who finds clothing during prayer: he must restart because the obligation to cover existed before prayer due to his already being naked. For the slave woman, the obligation to cover arises only with emancipation during prayer, so she can cover immediately without restarting. If she is unable to cover, like a free woman who cannot cover, her prayer remains valid. The passage then discusses a hermaphrodite: if a slave, his awrah is that of a slave girl (navel to knee? Actually, for an enslaved female, awrah includes head? The text says 'awrah of a slave girl'—the Hanafi view is that the awrah of a slave girl is from navel to knee, but the head is not awrah, whereas for a free woman, the head is awrah. So if the hermaphrodite is free, he must cover his entire body because he might be a woman; if he covers only navel to knee, some say he must repeat, others not. Finally, a subsidiary issue: a master says to his slave girl, 'If you pray a valid prayer, you are free before it.' She prays with uncovered head. If she was unable to cover (e.g., no cloth), her prayer is valid and she becomes free. If she was able to cover but did not, her prayer is valid but she does not become free, because if she became free, she would have been free before the prayer, making the prayer invalid as a free woman with uncovered head, and if invalid, she wouldn't be freed—leading to a circularity. The preferred solution is to cancel the word 'before it' so she becomes free at the time of prayer, making the prayer valid if she covered properly, but here she didn't, so it's invalid. However, the author references a similar rule in divorce (if I divorce you, you are thrice divorced before it) where 'before it' is canceled, so here also 'before it' is canceled and the emancipation occurs, making her free before the prayer, thus the prayer with uncovered head is invalid and she remains free. This resolves the circularity.

Key Terms
الجنب (al-janb): The side of the body, specifically the area between the armpit and hip.
الأمة (al-ammah): A female slave whose awrah in prayer is from navel to knee according to Hanafi school (head is not awrah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Repeat all prayers of that month.
B) Repeat only the first prayer of the month.
C) Not repeat any because she did not know.
D) Repeat only the prayers after the moment she learned.

Key Takeaway
The prayer of a slave woman freed mid-prayer is valid if she covers her head with a small action before the next rukn; the preponderant Hanafi view is that knowledge of emancipation is not required for the validity of covering.

Ruling on Finding a Partially Pure Garment While Naked in Prayer
Explains the ruling on praying in a partially pure garment with quarter threshold and subsequent choices

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying in a partially pure garment, distinguish the obligatory wearing when a quarter is pure from the optional choices when less, and apply the order of preference among the options.

Core Idea
A quarter of a pure garment makes wearing it wajib; less than a quarter gives a choice with ranked options.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the ruling for a person who is praying naked but finds a garment that is partially pure (some parts najis). The base ruling is clear: if a quarter (rub') of the garment is pure, it becomes wajib to wear it and pray. If less than a quarter is pure, the person has a choice among several options, each with a different level of superiority. Understanding this ruling requires knowing the Hanafi principle that a quarter stands for the whole in cases of necessity, as well as the intra-madhhab disagreement on whether gesturing while standing is allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The matn states: if one finds a garment of which a quarter is pure and prays naked, it is not valid (lam yajuz). The commentator explains that a quarter stands for the whole, so wearing it becomes obligatory (wajib).
This is based on the analogy (qiyas) that a quarter suffices in necessity.
2
Understand the qiyas (quarter analogy)
The illa (effective cause) is that a quarter of a thing takes the ruling of the whole in situations of necessity. Thus, the garment is treated as fully pure, and wearing it is obligatory unless one can remove or reduce the impurity.
The qiyas is jaliy (clear) and supported by istihsan.
3
Distinguish when less than a quarter is pure
If the pure part is less than a quarter, the person has a choice (takhayyur) among three (or four) options. The best option is to wear the garment anyway, because it combines covering the 'awrah with full bowing and prostration.
The options are ranked by superiority, and the ranking involves an ikhtilaf about gesturing while standing.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on gesturing while standing
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, gesturing while standing (al-imā' qā'iman) is allowed, making it one of the options. Imam Muhammad holds that finding any pure garment is like finding a full covering, which invalidates the option to pray naked. The commentator prefers the view of the two imams.
The dispute is over the fourth option: gesturing standing vs sitting.
5
Determine the order of preference (afdaliyya)
The overall order from best to least is: 1) praying in the garment standing with full movements, 2) naked sitting with gestures, 3) naked sitting with full movements, 4) naked standing with full movements, 5) naked standing with gestures. The fourth is debated.
The commentator notes that although standing covers more 'awrah, it is ranked lower due to disagreement on its validity.

يقللها فإن وجد في الصورتين وجب استعماله بخلاف ما إذا وجد ماء يكفي بعض أعضاء الوضوء فإنه يتيمم ولا يجب استعماله كما عرف في بابه، وعلم حكم ما إذا كان الأكثر من الربع طاهراً بالأولى. قوله (وخير إن طهر أن قائماً عرياناً بركوع وسجود وهو دونهما في الفضل. وفي ملتقى البحار إن شاء صلى عرياناً بالركوع والسجود أو مومياً بهما إما قاعداً وإما قائماً فهذا نص على جواز الإيماء قائماً. وظاهر الهداية أنه لا يجوز. وعلى الأول المخير فيه أربعة أشياء، وينبغي أن يكون الرابع دون الثالث في الفضل وإن كان ستر العورة فيه أكثر للاختلاف في صحته. وهذا كله عندهما، وعند محمد ليس بخلاف العاري إذا وجد الساتر فإنها تبطل بمجرد وجدانه له قوله : (فهذا) نص على جواز الإيماء قائماً) وفي شرح الشيخ إسمعيل قال : ونقل عن فتاوى الزاهدي أنه يصلي قائماً يومىء بالركوع والسجود. ومقتضى ما في المنبع أن عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمه الله التخيير بين الإيماء قائماً وقاعداً. وتبعه ابن ملك . وفي المفتاح أوما القائم أو ركع أو سجد القاعد جاز اهـ. قلت : وما في النهر من قوله «وظاهر الرواية منعه فالظاهر أنه تحريف من الناسخ والأصل، وظاهر His saying: (And if he finds a garment of which a quarter is pure and prays naked, it is not permissible) because a quarter of a thing stands in the place of the whole, so it is considered as if the whole is pure in a situation of necessity, so it is obligatory upon him to pray in it. And it is not hidden that its place is when he does not find something to remove the impurity nor to reduce it; if he finds in either of the two situations, it becomes obligatory to use it, contrary to if he finds water sufficient for some limbs of ablution, then he performs tayammum and it is not obligatory to use it, as known in its chapter. And the ruling when most of the quarter is pure is known a fortiori. His saying: (And he has a choice if less than a quarter is pure) meaning between praying in it—which is superior because it includes bowing and prostration and covering the awrah—and between praying naked while sitting, gesturing in bowing and prostration—which is next in superiority because it covers the major awrah—and between standing naked with bowing and prostration, which is below both in virtue. In Multaqa al-Bihar: If he wishes, he may pray naked with bowing and prostration, or gesturing in them, either sitting or standing. So this is a text permitting gesturing while standing. The apparent view of al-Hidayah is that it is not permissible. According to the first, he has a choice among four things, and it is fitting that the fourth be inferior to the third in virtue, although covering the awrah is more (in the fourth) because of the difference of opinion regarding its validity. And all this according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and according to Muhammad there is no difference from the naked person who finds a covering, for it is invalidated by merely finding it. His saying: (So this) is a text allowing gesturing while standing. In Sharh al-Shaykh Isma'il: It is narrated from Fatawa al-Zahidi that he prays standing, gesturing in bowing and prostration. The implication of what is in al-Manbi' is that according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, there is a choice between gesturing standing and sitting. Ibn Malik followed him. In al-Miftah: Whether the standing person gestures or the sitting person bows or prostrates, it is permissible. I say: What is in al-Nahr: 'The apparent narration prevents it,' so it appears that it is a corruption by the copyist, and the original apparent view of al-Hidayah is as expressed in al-Bahr, and supported by the saying of al-Nahr later, as mentioned from al-Hidayah, pay attention. The overall result is that he has a choice among: his prayer in it (garment) standing with bowing and prostration, then naked sitting gesturing, then naked sitting with bowing and prostration, then naked standing with bowing and prostration, then naked standing gesturing. And the order of superiority should be this. His saying: (And it is fitting that the fourth be inferior to the third in virtue) means by the fourth: gesturing standing, and by the third: what he mentioned in his saying: 'and between praying standing naked with bowing and prostration,' and he called it fourth because it is the intended from quoting the expression of Multaqa al-Bihar in addition to the three he mentioned initially, and to indicate the difference of opinion therein. Indeed, the expression of al-Multaqa indicates another form not mentioned initially, which is his prayer naked sitting with bowing and prostration, and I have not seen its rank mentioned.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling when a person who is naked in prayer finds a garment that is partially pure (some part najis). The base ruling from the matn is: if he finds a garment of which a quarter is pure and he prays naked, his prayer is not valid. The commentator explains that a quarter of a thing stands in for the whole in cases of necessity, so the garment is considered pure enough to be obligatory to wear. If he finds something to remove or reduce the impurity, he must use that first. Then he discusses the case when less than a quarter is pure: he has a choice (takhayyur) between three options: 1) praying in the garment (best), 2) praying naked sitting with gestures (second best because it covers the major awrah of the private parts), 3) praying naked standing with bowing and prostration (less good). However, the Multaqa al-Bihar adds a fourth option: gesturing while standing, making it four choices. There is a dispute: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, gesturing while standing is allowed, but according to al-Hidayah, it is not. The commentator prefers the view that it is allowed, citing Fatawa al-Zahidi and others. The order of superiority is: 1) praying in the garment standing with full movements, 2) naked sitting with gestures, 3) naked sitting with full movements, 4) naked standing with full movements, 5) naked standing with gestures. The author notes that while the fourth (standing with gestures) covers the awrah more (since standing keeps the body more hidden), it is inferior because of disagreement on its validity. The passage concludes by noting an additional form: naked sitting with bowing and prostration (i.e., full movements while sitting) but its rank is not recorded.

Key Terms
الربع (al-rubu'): One quarter (25%) of the garment, considered sufficient to deem the garment as predominantly pure for obligatory covering.
الإيماء (al-imā'): Gesturing with the head or body in place of bowing and prostration when unable to perform them fully.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, if a naked person in prayer finds a garment of which a quarter is pure, what must he do?
A) He must wear it and pray.
B) He has a choice to wear it or pray naked.
C) He must pray naked.
D) He must wash the pure part and wear it.

Key Takeaway
When a quarter of a garment is pure, wearing it becomes obligatory; when less, one has a choice among options, with the best being to wear it anyway.

Prayer in Impure Garments: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Quarter Rule
Intra-Hanafi dispute on obligation to pray in impure garment, with quarter rule and examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on praying in an impure garment and apply the quarter rule to determine the ruling when multiple garments are present.

Core Idea
When only an impure garment is available, Abu Hanifa requires praying in it; the Sahibayn give a choice.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: must a person who has only an impure garment pray in it, or may he choose to pray naked? Imam Abu Hanifa insists on covering the awrah despite the impurity, while his two companions give a choice. The commentator then expands with detailed examples involving the quarter threshold and the general principle that when facing two afflictions of different severity, one must choose the easier.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core intra-Hanafi dispute
Read the opening lines and note the two positions: Abu Hanifa says the person must pray in the impure garment; the Sahibayn say he may choose between praying naked or in the garment.
The dispute hinges on whether the obligation to cover the awrah is conditional upon purity.
2
Analyze the dalil for each position
Abu Hanifa argues that the command to purify is dropped due to inability, but the command to cover remains because covering is possible. The Sahibayn argue that the command is to cover with purity; since purity is impossible, the entire obligation drops.
This is a classic example of how mujtahidun balance conflicting obligations.
3
Apply the quarter rule to multiple garments
Study the examples: if one garment has a quarter pure, it is treated as pure; if impurity is less than a quarter, it is excused. Use this to determine in which garment one must pray.
The quarter rule is a specific Hanafi measure for impurity in garments.
4
Apply the principle of choosing the easier
Read the general principle: when two afflictions are equal, one may choose; when they differ, one must choose the easier. Apply this to the examples of the woman sitting, partial head covering, and the wounded person.
This principle is derived from the spirit of the Sharia to ease hardship.

Source Text

بمخير ولا تجوز صلاته إلا في الثوب لأن خطاب التطهير سقط عنه لعجزه ولم يسقط عنه خطاب الستر لقدرته عليه فصار كالطاهر في حقه. ولهما أن المأمور به هو الستر بالطاهر فإذا لم يقدر عليه سقط فيميل إلى أيهما شاء ولو قال المصنف وخير إن طهر الأقل أو كان كله نجساً لكان أفود إذا الحكم كذلك مذهباً وخلافاً كما في النهاية وغيرها، أو اقتصر على الثاني ليفهم منه الأول بالأولى لكان أولى. وفي الأسرار : قول محمد أحسن بخلاف ما لو لم يجد إلا جلد ميتة غير مدبوغ فإنه لا يجوز أن يستر به عورته ولم تجز صلاته فيه لأن نجاسة البول أو الدم أو نحوهما في الثوب كله تزول بالماء، ونجاسة الجلد لا يزيلها الماء فكانت أغلظ . وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو كان معه ثوبان ربع أحدهما طاهر والآخر أقل من الربع، فإنه يصلي في الذي ربعه طاهر ولا يجوز عكسه لما أن طهارة الربع كطهارة الكل. ويستفاد منه أن نجاسة أحدهما لو كانت قدر الربع والآخر أقل وجب أن يصلي في أقلهما ولا يجوز عكسه لأن للربع حكم الكل، ولما دون الربع حكم العدم وإلى أنه لو كان في كل واحد منهما قدر الربع أو في أحدهما أكثر لكن لا يبلغ ثلاثة أرباعه وفي الآخر قدر الربع فإنه يصلي في أيهما شاء لاستوائهما في الحكم. وكذا لو كان معه ثوبان نجاسة كل واحد منهما أكثر من قدر الدرهم يتخير ما لم يبلغ أحدهما ربع الثوب لاستوائهما في المنع. وفي المحيط : ولو كان الدم في ناحية من الثوب والطاهر منه بقدر ما يمكنه أن يتزر به لم يجز إلا أن يصلي فيه لأنه يمكنه ستر العورة بثوب طاهر ولم يفصل بينهما إذا تحرك الطرف الآخر أو لم يتحرك ا هـ . وبهذا علم أن التفصيل المتقدم إنما هو عند الاختيار، أما عند الضرورة فلا تفصيل. ثم الأصل في جنس هذه المسائل أن من ابتلي ببليتين وهما متساويتان يأخذ بأيهما شاء، وإن اختلفا فعليه أن يختار أهونهما، ولهذا لو أن امرأة لو صلت قائمة ينكشف من عورتها ما يمنع جواز الصلاة، ولو صلت قاعدة لا ينكشف منها شيء فإنها تصلي قاعدة لما أن ترك القيام أهون. ولو كان الثوب يغطي جسدها وربع رأسها فتركت تغطية الرأس لا يجوز ولو كان يغطي أقل من الربع لا يضر والستر أفضل تقليلاً للانكشاف. ولو كان جريح لو سجد سال جرحه وإن لم يسجد لم يكن الفضيلة. وينبغي أن تكون فوق القيام عرياناً بركوع وسجود كما قدمناه لأن الستر فيها أبلغ تأمل . قوله : (وفي الأسرار قول محمد أحسن نظر فيه في فتح القدير فراجعه قوله : (بخلاف ما لو لم يجد إلا جلد ميتة الخ) يعني أن الخلاف في النجاسة العارضة لا الأصلية فلا يجوز الستر بذلك اتفاقاً كما في النهر، لكن في كون نجاسة جلد الميتة أصلية نظر بل هي عارضة بالموت تأمل. قوله: (وبهذا علم أن التفصيل المتقدم الخ) قال في النهر : لأنه لا أثر لتحرك الطرف في الآخر هنا إذ الظاهر منه أن يبلغ ربعاً تحتم لبسه، سواء تحرك أو لا، أو أقل منه خيراً لا عند محمد رحمه الله على ما علمت. نعم المناسب حمل الإطلاق على قوله قوله : (قياساً على المتيمم إذا كان. الماء في آخره) أقول : يرجو
He is not given a choice, and his prayer is not valid except in the garment, because the command of purification is dropped from him due to his inability, but the command of covering is not dropped from him due to his ability over it, so he becomes like the pure one in his regard. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is commanded is covering with purity, so if he is unable to do it, it is dropped, so he may lean towards whichever he wishes. If the author said 'and he is given choice if the lesser is purified or if all of it is impure', it would be more beneficial, because the ruling is so both as a madhhab and contrary, as in al-Nihayah and others, or if he limited to the second to understand the first by priority, it would be better. In al-Asrar: The statement of Muhammad is better, contrary to if he finds only an untanned dead animal skin, then it is not permissible for him to cover his awrah with it, and his prayer therein is not valid, because the impurity of urine, blood, or similar in the entire garment is removed by water, but the impurity of the skin is not removed by water, so it is more severe. The author indicated that if he has two garments, one of which a quarter is pure and the other less than a quarter, then he prays in the one whose quarter is pure, and the opposite is not permissible, because the purity of the quarter is like the purity of the whole. It is understood from this that if the impurity of one of them is the measure of a quarter and the other is less, he must pray in the lesser of the two, and the opposite is not permissible, because a quarter has the ruling of the whole, and what is less than a quarter has the ruling of non-existence. And it also indicates that if each of them contains a quarter's impurity, or one has more but does not reach three-quarters and the other has a quarter, then he prays in whichever he wishes due to their equality in ruling. Similarly, if he has two garments, each with impurity more than the measure of a dirham, he chooses as long as neither reaches a quarter of the garment, due to their equality in prohibition. In al-Muhit: If blood is in a corner of the garment and the pure part is sufficient for him to wrap around his waist, then it is not permissible except to pray in it, because he can cover his awrah with a pure garment, and no distinction is made between when the other corner moves or not. And with this it is known that the detailed ruling mentioned earlier is only in case of choice, but in case of necessity there is no detail. Then the principle in this type of issues is that whoever is afflicted by two afflictions that are equal takes whichever he wishes, but if they differ, he must choose the easier of them. Hence, if a woman when standing exposes from her awrah what prevents the validity of prayer, but when sitting nothing is exposed, then she prays sitting, because leaving standing is easier. And if the garment covers her body and a quarter of her head, then leaving covering the head is not permissible; if it covers less than a quarter, it does not harm, and covering is better to minimize exposure. And if a wounded person when prostrating his wound flows, and if he does not prostrate it does not have the virtue, then it is preferable to stand naked with bowing and prostration as we have mentioned, because covering is more effective in that case. Reflect. His statement: (In al-Asrar, the statement of Muhammad is better) is examined in Fath al-Qadir, so refer to it. His statement: (Contrary to if he finds only dead animal skin, etc.) means that the difference is in accidental impurity, not original; so covering with it is not permissible by agreement, as in al-Nahr. However, the impurity of dead animal skin being original is questionable; rather it is accidental by death. Reflect. His statement: (And with this it is known that the detailed ruling earlier, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: Because there is no effect of the movement of the other corner on the other here, since the apparent from it is that it reaches a quarter, it is permissible to wear it whether it moves or not, or less than that he has choice, not according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, as you have known. Yes, the appropriate is to apply the absolute on his statement. His statement: (By analogy with the one performing tayammum if water is at the end of the time) I say: He hopes.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on a matn (likely al-Kanz) regarding the conditions of prayer, specifically the ruling on one who has only an impure garment to cover his awrah. The passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the person must pray in the impure garment because the command to purify the garment is dropped due to inability, but the command to cover the awrah remains, as he is able to cover with that garment. Therefore, he is not given a choice to pray naked. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the obligation is to cover with a pure garment; since he cannot achieve purity, the entire obligation to cover is dropped, so he may choose to pray naked. The commentator notes that Muhammad's view is preferred in al-Asrar. The passage then expands with multiple practical examples: the ruling on two garments with different levels of impurity (the quarter rule), the case of blood in a corner of a garment where a pure portion exists, and the general principle that when facing two equal difficulties one may choose, but when they differ, one must choose the easier. Examples are given for a woman who may sit to avoid exposure, a garment covering only part of the head, and a wounded person who may stand to avoid blood flow. The commentary also discusses the difference between accidental and original impurity, noting that dead animal skin not tanned is never permissible due to the severity of its impurity. The passage is rich in practical fiqh and highlights the Hanafi methodology of balancing between obligations and abilities.

Key Terms
الطهارة (al-taharah): Here it means the purity of the garment from physical impurities (najāsa).
الستر (al-satr): Covering the awrah during prayer, which is a condition for validity.
الربع (al-rubu'): One quarter of the garment; used as a threshold: impurity less than a quarter is excused; a quarter or more renders the garment unusable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the ruling when a person has two garments, one with impurity exactly a quarter and the other with impurity less than a quarter?
A) He must pray in the garment with exactly a quarter impurity.
B) He must pray in the garment with less than a quarter impurity.
C) He may choose either garment.
D) He must combine both garments to cover himself.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school offers two valid views on praying in an impure garment, and the quarter rule provides a precise method for determining which garment to use when multiple are available.
