Ruling for the One Lacking Clothing
Ruling with proof for praying naked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a person lacking clothing in prayer, explain the definition of 'adam (lack of covering), and apply the Hanafi position on waiting for a promised garment.

Core Idea
Covering the 'awrah is prioritized over prayer timeliness; the 'aryan prays sitting with gestures.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the proper prayer of someone without clothing. It not only states the ruling but also defines what constitutes a lack of covering and addresses a secondary scenario where a garment is promised. Understanding these details protects against invalidating one's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The text states that if a person lacks a garment covering the 'awrah, he should pray sitting with gestures for ruku' and sujud, and this is better than standing.
The ruling is conditional upon actual inability to obtain covering.
2
Define 'adam (lack) of clothing
Lack is established by two criteria: absence in ownership (possessing no such covering) and absence of permissibility (e.g., a garment is not offered or available lawfully). If a garment is available (e.g., offered), the person is considered capable and must wear it.
Even unconventional materials like plants or clay suffice if they cover the majority of the 'awrah.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The Companions, when shipwrecked and naked, prayed sitting with gestures. This action is used as evidence that sitting with gestures is permissible and preferable when covering is lacking.
The hadith is a single narration (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in the Hanafi school.
4
Examine the subsidiary ruling on waiting
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, if a person is promised a garment after the prayer time begins, he should wait for that garment even if he fears the time will pass. This shows that covering takes precedence over performing prayer at its earliest time.
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf held that one only waits if not fearing loss of time, but the mufta bihi follows Muhammad.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The difference is only in the waiting rule. The main ruling (sitting with gestures when lacking clothing) is agreed upon.
The mufta bihi position prioritizes covering over timeliness, based on the principle that covering the 'awrah is a condition for prayer validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عدم ثوباً صلى قاعداً مومياً بركوع وسجود وهو أفضل من القيام بركوع وسجود والنية يسل فإنه يصلي قاعداً مومياً لأن ترك السجود أهون من الصلاة الحدث، ألا ترى أن ترك السجود جائز حالة الاختيار في التطوع على الدابة، ومع الحدث لا يجوز بحال. فإن قام وقرأ وركع ثم قعد وأومأ للسجود جاز لما قلنا والأول أفضل، وكذا شيخ لا يقدر على القراءة قائماً ويقدر عليها قاعداً يصلي قاعداً لأنه يجوز حالة الاختيار في النفل ولا يجوز ترك القراءة بحال، ولو صلى في الفصلين قائماً مع الحدث وترك القراءة لم يجز . قوله : ( ولو عدم ثوباً صلى قاعداً مومياً بركوع وسجود وهو أفضل من القيام بركوع وسجود) لما عن أنس أن أصحاب رسول الله وركبوا في السفينة فانكسرت بهم فخرجوا من البحر عراة فصلوا قعوداً بإيماء. أراد بالثوب ما يستر عامة عورته ولو حريراً أو حشيشاً أو نباتاً أو كلاً أو طيناً يلطخ به عورته ويبقى عليه حتى يصلي لا الزجاج الذي يصف ما تحته. والعدم المذكور يثبت بعدم الوجود في ملكه وبعدم الإباحة له حتى لو أبيح له ثوب تثبت القدرة به على الأصح ، فلو صلى عارياً لم يجز كالمتيمم إذا أبيح له الماء. وعن محمد في العريان يعده صاحبه أنه يعطيه الثوب إذا صلى فإنه ينتظره ولا يصلي عرياناً وإن خاف فوت الوقت. كذا في السراج الوهاج
If he lacks a garment, he prays sitting with gestures for bowing and prostration, and that is better than standing with bowing and prostration. And the intention [??] then he prays sitting with gestures, because leaving prostration is lighter than praying while in a state of hadath. Do you not see that leaving prostration is permissible in a voluntary choice upon an animal, and with hadath it is not permissible at all. If he stands, recites, bows, then sits and gestures for prostration, it is permissible for what we said, but the first is better. Similarly, an old man who cannot recite standing but can do so sitting prays sitting, because it is permissible in voluntary choice in nafl and leaving recitation is not permissible in any case. If he prays in the two rak'ahs standing while in hadath and leaves recitation, it is not permissible. His statement: (And if he lacks a garment, he prays sitting with gestures for bowing and prostration, and that is better than standing with bowing and prostration) is due to what is from Anas that the Companions of the Messenger of Allah rode in a ship, it broke with them, so they came out of the sea naked and prayed sitting with gestures. He intended by 'garment' what covers the majority of his 'awrah, even if it be silk, or grass, or plants, or moss, or clay that he smears on his 'awrah and it remains on him until he prays, not glass that shows what is underneath. The mentioned lack is established by the absence of existence in his ownership and by the absence of permissibility for him, such that if a garment is permissible for him, ability is established on the most correct view. So if he prays naked, it is not permissible, like the mutayammim if water is permissible for him. And from Muhammad regarding the naked person whose companion promises him that he will give him the garment after he prays: he waits for him and does not pray naked even if he fears the time will pass. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm with dalil) from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The main ruling: one who lacks clothing (al-'aryan) must pray sitting with gestures (ima') for ruku' and sujud, and this is better than standing. The commentator provides the hadith of the Companions' shipwreck as proof. He defines 'garment' broadly: anything that covers the majority of the 'awrah, even unconventional materials like silk, plants, or clay, but not transparent glass. The 'lack' is determined by both absence in ownership and lack of permissibility—if a garment is offered (permissible), then he is considered capable and must wear it. If he prays naked without excuse, the prayer is invalid, analogous to tayammum when water is available. A subsidiary from Muhammad al-Shaybani: if someone promises to give him a garment after he prays, he should wait and not pray naked, even if he fears missing the time. This shows the importance of covering the 'awrah over performing the prayer at its earliest time.

Key Terms
العريان (al-'aryan): One who lacks clothing to cover the 'awrah, whether due to absence in ownership or lack of permissibility.
الإيماء (al-ima'): A gesture for ruku' and sujud instead of full movement, used when one cannot perform full postures.
العدم (al-'adam): Lack of ability to obtain covering, either by non-ownership or by prohibition (e.g., a usurped garment not available).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a naked person is promised a garment after prayer but fears the time will pass?
A) He must pray naked immediately.
B) He should wait for the promised garment even if the time passes.
C) He should combine the prayers later.
D) He can choose between waiting and praying.

Key Takeaway
The one lacking clothing must pray sitting with gestures, and if there is hope of obtaining covering, he should wait even if time passes.

Waiting for a Promised Garment: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on waiting and qiyas on mutayammim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on whether the 'ari should wait for a promised garment, and apply the qiyas on the mutayammim to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
Waiting for clothing is like waiting for water: hope of the condition justifies delay.

In this passage from Bahr al-Raiq, we encounter a fascinating intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a person without clothing ('ari) should delay prayer in hopes of obtaining a garment. The commentary draws a compelling analogy to the case of tayammum, where one hopes for water. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to see how qiyas operates within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: wait only if not fearing time loss. Muhammad: wait even if time passes.
The dispute is about the extent of waiting, not about the basic permission.
2
Locate the proof
The commentary uses qiyas on the mutayammim who hopes for water – just as he delays tayammum until the end of the time, the 'ari delays until he fears missing the prayer.
This is a legal analogy (qiyas) based on the hope of obtaining a necessary condition.
3
Analyze the illa
The effective cause (illa) is the hope of obtaining the covering (water/clothing) before the prayer time ends.
If there is no hope, the analogy fails, and he prays immediately.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If one follows Muhammad, he may miss the prayer if the garment does not arrive. If one follows Abu Hanifa, he ensures the prayer is performed on time but perhaps without covering.
The mufta bihi position is Muhammad's, meaning one should wait even if time passes, but this view is debated among later scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية عن أبي حنيفة : ينتظره ما لم يخف فوت الوقت وأبو يوسف مع أبي حنيفة. وينبغي ترجيحه قياساً على المتيمم إذا كان يرجو الماء في آخره. في الصلاة قاعداً فشمل ما إذا كان نهاراً أو ليلاً في بيت أو صحراء وهو الصحيح كما بينه في منية المصلي، ومن المشايخ من خصه بالنهار، أما في الليل فيصلي قائماً لأن ظلمة الليل تستر عورته قال في الذخيرة وهذا ليس بمرضي لأن الستر الذي يحصل في ظلمة الليل لا عبرة به ألا ترى أن حالة القدرة على الثوب إذا صلى عرياناً في ظلمة الليل لا يجوز فصار وجوده وعدمه بمنزلة واحدة ا هـ. وتعقبه في شرح منية المصلي بأن الاستشهاد المذكور غير متجه للفرق بين حالة الاختيار وحالة الاضطرار وأطال إلى أن قال : ويؤيده ما أخرجه عبد الرزاق سئل علي رضي الله عنه عن صلاة العريان قال: إن كان حيث يراه الناس صلى جالساً، وإن كان حيث لا يراه الناس صلى قائماً. وهو وإن كان سنده ضعيفاً فلا يقصر عن إفادة الاستئناس وأما واقعة الصحابة المتقدمة فقد تطرق إليها احتمالات، إما لأنهم اختاروا الأولى لما فيه من تقليل الانكشاف أو لأنهم كانوا مترائين أو لم يكن ليلاً فسقط بها الاستدلال، ولم يبين المصنف صفة القعود للاختلاف فيها. ففي منية المصلي : يقعد كما يقعد في الصلاة. فعلى هذا يختلف في الرجل والمرأة، فهو يفترش وهي تتورك. وفي الذخيرة: يقعد ويمد رجليه إلى القبلة ويضع يديه على عورته الغليظة والذي يظهر ترجيح الأول وأنه أولى لأنه يحصل به من المبالغة في الستر ما لا يحصل بالهيئة المذكورة مع خلو هذه الهيئة عن فعل ما ليس بأولى وهو مد رجليه إلى القبلة من غير ضرورة، والحاصل أن القعود على هيئة متعينة ليس بمتعين بل يجوز كيفما كان، وإنما كان القعود أفضل من القيام لأن ستر العورة أهم من أداء الأركان لأنه فرض مطلقاً والأركان فرائض الصلاة لا غير وقد أتى ببدلها. وإنما كان القيام جائزاً لأنه وإن ترك فرض الستر فقد كمل الأركان الثلاثة وبه حاجة إلى تكميلها. كذا في البدائع.
And in al-Qunyah from Abu Hanifa: he waits for him as long as he does not fear the time will pass, and Abu Yusuf is with Abu Hanifa. And it should be preferred by analogy to the mutayammim if he hopes for water at the end of the time. [The discussion of] praying sitting includes whether it is day or night, in a house or desert, and that is the correct view as explained in Munyat al-Musalli. Among the mashayikh are those who specify it for daytime; as for night, he prays standing because the darkness of night covers his 'awrah. Al-Dhakhirah said: This is not satisfactory because the covering obtained in night darkness is not considered; do you not see that in the case of ability to have a garment, if he prays naked in night darkness, it is not permissible? So its existence and non-existence are equal. It was criticized in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli that the cited evidence is not directed at the difference between the optional situation and the necessity situation, and he elaborated until he said: It is supported by what Abd al-Razzaq narrated: Ali (r.a.) was asked about the prayer of the naked person; he said: If he is where people see him, he prays sitting; if he is where people do not see him, he prays standing. Although its chain is weak, it is not less than providing familiarity. As for the earlier incident of the Companions, possible interpretations have been suggested: either they chose the better because it involves less exposure, or because they were visible to each other, or because it was not night. Thus the inference falls. The author did not explain the manner of sitting due to the difference about it. In Munyat al-Musalli: he sits as he sits in prayer. According to this, it differs for man and woman: he sits iftirash, she tawarruk. In al-Dhakhirah: he sits and extends his legs towards the qiblah and places his hands on his thick 'awrah. What appears is that the first (as in Munyah) is preferred because it achieves more covering than the mentioned posture, and that posture involves doing something not preferable: extending legs towards the qiblah without necessity. The conclusion: sitting is not determined by a specific posture; rather it is permissible in any manner. And sitting is better than standing because covering the 'awrah is more important than performing the pillars, because it is an absolute obligation, while the pillars are only obligations of the prayer, and he has performed their substitutes. Standing is permissible because although he leaves the obligation of covering, he has completed the three pillars and there is a need to complete them. Thus in al-Bada'i.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage covers two main issues: (1) the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the 'ari should wait for a promised garment, and (2) the superiority of sitting over standing and the mode of sitting. First, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: wait only if not fearing time loss; this is preferred by qiyas on the mutayammim who hopes for water. Second, the correct view is that the ruling applies day or night, in house or desert. Some restricted it to daytime because night covers, but al-Dhakhirah refutes this: darkness provides no valid cover, as praying naked at night with ability is invalid. The commentary then discusses the mode: Munyat al-Musalli says he sits normally (iftirash for men, tawarruk for women); al-Dhakhirah says sits with legs extended and hands covering genitals. The preferred view is the former because it covers better and avoids extending legs to qiblah unnecessarily. The underlying principle: covering 'awrah is more important (fard mutlaq) than performing the pillars; thus sitting is better. Standing is still permissible because it fulfills the three pillars (qiyam, ruku', sujud) despite missing optimal covering.

Key Terms
الافتراش (al-iftirash): The sitting posture for a man in prayer: spreading the left foot and sitting on it with the right foot upright.
التورك (al-tawarruk): The sitting posture for a woman: sitting on the left buttock with legs out to the right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the view that the 'ari should wait for a promised garment?
A) Direct hadith from the Prophet
B) Ijma' of the Companions
C) Qiyas on the mutayammim who hopes for water
D) Istihsan based on necessity

Key Takeaway
The 'ari may wait for a promised garment as long as he does not fear the prayer time will pass, based on qiyas on the mutayammim.

Sitting Over Standing for the 'Ari: Superiority and Posture
Ruling on superiority of sitting and posture for the 'ari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that sitting is superior to standing for the 'ari, and distinguish between the preferred sitting posture (iftirash/tawarruk) and less preferred postures.

Core Idea
Covering 'awrah outweighs completing pillars; thus sitting is best.

After resolving the waiting dispute, the passage turns to the manner of prayer for the 'ari. The central principle is that covering the 'awrah is a universal obligation ('fard mutlaq'), while the pillars of prayer are obligations within the prayer. When necessary, covering takes priority, so sitting (which provides better covering) is superior to standing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
Sitting is better than standing for the 'ari. This is the established position of the madhhab.
The ruling applies whether day or night, in house or desert.
2
Understand the reasoning
Covering 'awrah is a universal obligation (fard mutlaq), while the pillars (qiyam, ruku', sujud) are only obligatory within the prayer. So covering takes precedence.
Since sitting allows better covering (e.g., by crossing legs), it is preferred.
3
Note the dispute about night
Some mashayikh argued that at night, because darkness covers, the 'ari can stand. The author refutes this: darkness does not provide legal cover, as seen from the case where one has a garment but prays naked at night – it is invalid.
Thus the ruling is consistent day and night.
4
Determine the posture
The preferred posture is the normal sitting like in prayer: iftirash for men, tawarruk for women. Another view suggests extending legs and covering with hands, but the first is better because it achieves more covering and avoids pointing feet towards qiblah unnecessarily.
Any sitting posture is permissible, but iftirash/tawarruk is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية عن أبي حنيفة : ينتظره ما لم يخف فوت الوقت وأبو يوسف مع أبي حنيفة. وينبغي ترجيحه قياساً على المتيمم إذا كان يرجو الماء في آخره. في الصلاة قاعداً فشمل ما إذا كان نهاراً أو ليلاً في بيت أو صحراء وهو الصحيح كما بينه في منية المصلي، ومن المشايخ من خصه بالنهار، أما في الليل فيصلي قائماً لأن ظلمة الليل تستر عورته قال في الذخيرة وهذا ليس بمرضي لأن الستر الذي يحصل في ظلمة الليل لا عبرة به ألا ترى أن حالة القدرة على الثوب إذا صلى عرياناً في ظلمة الليل لا يجوز فصار وجوده وعدمه بمنزلة واحدة ا هـ. وتعقبه في شرح منية المصلي بأن الاستشهاد المذكور غير متجه للفرق بين حالة الاختيار وحالة الاضطرار وأطال إلى أن قال : ويؤيده ما أخرجه عبد الرزاق سئل علي رضي الله عنه عن صلاة العريان قال: إن كان حيث يراه الناس صلى جالساً، وإن كان حيث لا يراه الناس صلى قائماً. وهو وإن كان سنده ضعيفاً فلا يقصر عن إفادة الاستئناس وأما واقعة الصحابة المتقدمة فقد تطرق إليها احتمالات، إما لأنهم اختاروا الأولى لما فيه من تقليل الانكشاف أو لأنهم كانوا مترائين أو لم يكن ليلاً فسقط بها الاستدلال، ولم يبين المصنف صفة القعود للاختلاف فيها. ففي منية المصلي : يقعد كما يقعد في الصلاة. فعلى هذا يختلف في الرجل والمرأة، فهو يفترش وهي تتورك. وفي الذخيرة: يقعد ويمد رجليه إلى القبلة ويضع يديه على عورته الغليظة والذي يظهر ترجيح الأول وأنه أولى لأنه يحصل به من المبالغة في الستر ما لا يحصل بالهيئة المذكورة مع خلو هذه الهيئة عن فعل ما ليس بأولى وهو مد رجليه إلى القبلة من غير ضرورة، والحاصل أن القعود على هيئة متعينة ليس بمتعين بل يجوز كيفما كان، وإنما كان القعود أفضل من القيام لأن ستر العورة أهم من أداء الأركان لأنه فرض مطلقاً والأركان فرائض الصلاة لا غير وقد أتى ببدلها. وإنما كان القيام جائزاً لأنه وإن ترك فرض الستر فقد كمل الأركان الثلاثة وبه حاجة إلى تكميلها. كذا في البدائع.
And in al-Qunyah from Abu Hanifa: he waits for him as long as he does not fear the time will pass, and Abu Yusuf is with Abu Hanifa. And it should be preferred by analogy to the mutayammim if he hopes for water at the end of the time. [The discussion of] praying sitting includes whether it is day or night, in a house or desert, and that is the correct view as explained in Munyat al-Musalli. Among the mashayikh are those who specify it for daytime; as for night, he prays standing because the darkness of night covers his 'awrah. Al-Dhakhirah said: This is not satisfactory because the covering obtained in night darkness is not considered; do you not see that in the case of ability to have a garment, if he prays naked in night darkness, it is not permissible? So its existence and non-existence are equal. It was criticized in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli that the cited evidence is not directed at the difference between the optional situation and the necessity situation, and he elaborated until he said: It is supported by what Abd al-Razzaq narrated: Ali (r.a.) was asked about the prayer of the naked person; he said: If he is where people see him, he prays sitting; if he is where people do not see him, he prays standing. Although its chain is weak, it is not less than providing familiarity. As for the earlier incident of the Companions, possible interpretations have been suggested: either they chose the better because it involves less exposure, or because they were visible to each other, or because it was not night. Thus the inference falls. The author did not explain the manner of sitting due to the difference about it. In Munyat al-Musalli: he sits as he sits in prayer. According to this, it differs for man and woman: he sits iftirash, she tawarruk. In al-Dhakhirah: he sits and extends his legs towards the qiblah and places his hands on his thick 'awrah. What appears is that the first (as in Munyah) is preferred because it achieves more covering than the mentioned posture, and that posture involves doing something not preferable: extending legs towards the qiblah without necessity. The conclusion: sitting is not determined by a specific posture; rather it is permissible in any manner. And sitting is better than standing because covering the 'awrah is more important than performing the pillars, because it is an absolute obligation, while the pillars are only obligations of the prayer, and he has performed their substitutes. Standing is permissible because although he leaves the obligation of covering, he has completed the three pillars and there is a need to complete them. Thus in al-Bada'i.

The Ruling of Intention in Prayer
Explaining the condition of intention and its timing in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intention in prayer, explain why it is a condition (shart) not a pillar (rukn), and evaluate the timing requirements relative to takbir.

Core Idea
Intention is a condition for prayer; it may precede takbir if no alien act separates.

In this lesson, we examine the legal status of intention (niyyah) in prayer from the Hanafi perspective. Based on the commentary of al-Bahr al-Raiq, we will see that intention is a condition (shart) for prayer, established by consensus, and that its timing is flexible: it can be made before the opening takbir as long as no alien act intervenes. We will also explore the different proofs, the intra-Hanafi disagreements, and the contrast with the Shafi'i requirement of simultaneity.

Guided Path
1
Classify intention's legal status
Identify that intention is a condition (shart) for prayer, not a pillar (rukn). Note that this is based on consensus of the Muslims.
The Hanafi school distinguishes: omission of a pillar invalidates the act, while a condition must be present for validity.
2
Evaluate the proofs
Analyze the Quranic verse (98:5) and the hadith 'إنما الأعمال بالنيات'. Understand why the Hanafis consider the hadith as zanni al-thubut wa al-dalala, thus indicating recommendation (sunnah) not obligation (fard).
The hadith is ahad and ambiguous, so it cannot impose fardiyyah according to Hanafi usul.
3
Define the alien separator
Learn what constitutes an alien separator (fasil ajnabi): any act inconsistent with prayer, such as eating, drinking, or speaking. Acts like walking or wudu are not alien.
Such an act nullifies the intention and the prayer if it occurs between intention and takbir.
4
Contrast with Shafi'i
Compare the Hanafi position (intention can precede) with the Shafi'i requirement of simultaneity. Understand the reasoning behind each and the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
The Hanafi view facilitates ease and avoids waswas.
5
Apply the ruling
Consider a scenario: a person makes intention for Fajr at home, then walks to the mosque (non-alien act) and prays. According to Hanafi school, the prayer is valid because no alien act separated.
The mufta bihi is that intention can be made before takbir as long as no foreign act occurs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والنية بلا فاصل) يعني من شروط الصلاة لإجماع المسلمين على ذلك كما نقله ابن المنذر وغيره. وأما الاستدلال على اشتراطها بقوله تعالى وما أمروا إلا ليعبدوا الله مخلصين له الدين) [البينة : ٥] كما فعله السراج الهندي في شرح المغني فليس بظاهر لأن الظاهر أن العبادة بمعنى التوحيد بدليل عطف الصلاة والزكاة عليها، وأما الاستدلال بقوله «إنما الأعمال بالنيات كما في الهداية وغيرها فلا يصح لأن الأصوليين ذكروا أن الحديث من قبيل ظني الثبوت والدلالة لأنه خبر واحد مشترك الدلالة فيفيد السنية والاستحباب لا الافتراض، والنية إرادة الصلاة الله تعالى على الخلوص وقد قدمنا في الوضوء الكلام عليها. وقول الشارح أن المصلي يحتاج إلى ثلاث نيات نية الصلاة التي يدخل فيها، ونية الاخلاص الله تعالى ونية استقبال القبلة فيه نظر؛ بل المحتاج إليه نية واحدة وهي ما ذكرناه. فقولنا على الخلوص يغني عن الثانية. وأما نية استقبال القبلة فليست شرطاً على الصحيح كما ذكره في المبسوط، سواء كان يصلي إلى المحراب أو في الصحراء، والمراد بقوله بلا فاصل أي بين النية والتكبير الفاصل الأجنبي وهو عمل لا يليق في الصلاة كالأكل والشرب لأن هذه الأفعال تبطل الصلاة فتبطل النية وشراء الحطب والكلام، وأما المشي والوضوء فليس بأجنبي، ألا ترى أن من أحدث في صلاته له أن يفعل ذلك ولا يمنعه من البناء . وبهذا علم أن الصلاة تجوز بنية متقدمة على الشروط إذا لم يفصل أجنبي كما صرحوا به، فظاهر إطلاقهم يفيد أن النية قبل دخول الوقت صحيحة كالطهارة قبله لكن ذكر ابن أمير حاج عن ابن هبيرة اشتراط دخول الوقت للنية المتقدمة عن أبي حنيفة وهو مشكل وفي ثبوته تردد لا يخفى لعدم وجوده في كتب المذهب وفي الظهيرية وعند محمد يجوز تقديم النية في العبادات : هو الصحيح، وعند أبي يوسف لا يجوز إلا في الصوم ا اهـ. وفي منية المصلي والأحوط أن ينوي مقارناً للتكبير ومخالطاً له كما هو مذهب الشافعي ا هـ. وبه قال الطحاوي لكن عندنا هذا الاحتياط مستحب وليس بشرط ، وعند الشافعي شرط لأن الحاجة إلى النية لتحقق معنى الاخلاص وذلك عند الشروع لا قبله قلنا النص مطلق فلا يجوز تخصيصه بالرأي على أن قوله وإنما لكل امرئ ما نوى يفيد أنه يكون له ما نوى إذا تقدمت النية، فالقول بأنه لا يكون له ما نوى خلاف النص، ولأن اشتراط القرآن لا يخلو عن الحرج مع ما في التزامه من فتح باب الوسواس فلا يشترط كما في الصوم والزكاة والحج، حتى لو خرج من بيته يريد الحج فأحرم ولم تحضره النية جاز. ثم فسر النووي القرآن بأن يأتي بالنية مع أوّل التكبير ويستصحبها إلى آخره، وذكر في شرح المهذب أنه لا يجب التدقيق في تحقيق المقارنة وأنه يكفي المقارنة العرفية في ذلك بحيث يعد مستحضراً لصلاته غير غافل عنها اقتداء بالسلف الصالحين في مسامحتهم في ذلك. وأشار المصنف إلى أنها لا تجوز بنية متأخرة خلافاً للكرخي قياساً على الصوم وهو فاسد، لأن سقوط القران لمكان الحرج والحرج يندفع بتقديم النية فلا ضرورة إلى التأخير، وجوز التأخير في الصوم للحرج. وبهذا علم أن ما في خزانة الفتاوى والعتابي «نسي النية فنوى عند قوله «ولا إله غيرك يصير شارعاً مبني على قول الكرخي على تخريج بعض المشايخ أنه يجوز إلى انتهاء الثناء، وقيل إلى أن يركع وهو مروي عن محمد. كذا في المجتبى . وقيل إلى أن يرفع رأسه من الركوع، وقيل إلى التعوّذ وفي البدائع : لو نوى بعد قوله « الله» قبل أكبر» لا يجوز لأن الشروع يصح معطوف على الأكل والشرب والأولى ذكره عقبه كما يوجد في بعض النسخ. قوله : (لعدم وجوده في كتب المذهب) قال الشيخ اسماعيل : قد وجدت المسألة والله الحمد في مجموع المسائل وهو من كتب المذهب. واختلفوا في النية هل يجوز تقديمها على التكبير أو تكون مقارنة له فقال أبو حنيفة وأحمد رحمهم الله : يجوز تقديم النية للصلاة بعد دخول الوقت وقبل التكبير ما لم يقطع بعمل اهـ.
He said: 'and the intention without a separator' means it is among the conditions of prayer due to the consensus of the Muslims on that, as transmitted by Ibn al-Mundhir and others. As for inferring its prerequisite by His statement {And they were not commanded except to worship Allah, [being] sincere to Him in religion} [Al-Bayyinah: 5] as did al-Siraj al-Hindi in his commentary on al-Mughni, that is not apparent because the apparent meaning of 'worship' is tawhid, evidenced by the conjunction of prayer and zakat upon it. As for inference by his statement, peace be upon him, 'Actions are but by intentions' as in al-Hidayah and others, it is not valid because the usul scholars mentioned that the hadith is of the type of speculative in transmission and meaning because it is a hadith ahad with multiple possible meanings, thus it indicates sunnah and recommendation, not obligation. And intention is the desire to pray to Allah with sincerity, and we have already discussed it in wudu. The commentator's statement that the prayer needs three intentions—intention of the prayer he enters into, intention of sincerity to Allah, and intention of facing the qibla—is questionable; rather, what is needed is one intention which we have mentioned. Our statement 'with sincerity' suffices from the second. As for intention of facing the qibla, it is not a condition according to the correct view as mentioned in al-Mabsut, whether he prays toward the mihrab or in the desert. And the meaning of his statement 'without a separator' is that between the intention and the takbir is an alien separator, which is an act not befitting the prayer, like eating and drinking, because these acts nullify the prayer and thus nullify the intention, and buying firewood and speech. As for walking and wudu, they are not alien. Do you not see that if someone has an event during his prayer, he may do that and it does not prevent him from building upon it. And with this it is known that prayer is valid with an intention that precedes the conditions if no alien act separates, as they have stated clearly. The apparent meaning of their absolute statement is that intention before the time is valid like purification before it, but Ibn Amir Hajj mentioned from Ibn Hubayrah that Abu Hanifa requires the entrance of time for the preceding intention, and that is problematic and its verification is not hidden due to its absence in the books of the madhhab. In al-Zahiriyyah: According to Muhammad, it is permissible to advance intention in acts of worship, and that is the correct view. According to Abu Yusuf, it is not permissible except in fasting. And in Munyat al-Musalli: The most precautionary is that he intend simultaneously with the takbir and mixed with it as is the madhhab of al-Shafi'i. And al-Tahawi said the same, but according to us this precaution is recommended and not a condition. According to al-Shafi'i it is a condition because the need for intention is to realize the meaning of sincerity, and that is at the commencement, not before it. We say: The text is absolute, so it is not permissible to specify it by opinion. Moreover, his statement 'And for each person is what he intended' indicates that he will have what he intended if the intention precedes, so the statement that he will not have what he intended contradicts the text. Also, requiring simultaneity does not avoid hardship, coupled with what is involved in adopting it of opening the door of waswas, so it is not required, just as in fasting, zakat, and hajj. Even if he leaves his house intending hajj and then enters ihram without the intention being present to him, it is valid. Then al-Nawawi interpreted 'simultaneity' as bringing the intention with the beginning of the takbir and maintaining it until the end, and he mentioned in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab that it is not necessary to scrutinize the realization of simultaneity and that customary simultaneity is sufficient such that he is considered present for his prayer, not heedless of it, following the pious predecessors in their leniency in that. And the author indicated that it is not valid with a delayed intention, contrary to al-Karkhi by analogy to fasting, and that is invalid because the dropping of simultaneity is due to hardship, and hardship is repelled by advancing the intention, so there is no need to delay. He permitted delay in fasting due to hardship. And with this it is known that what is in Khizanat al-Fatawa and al-Atabi: 'He forgot the intention and then intended when saying 'and there is no god but You' he becomes commencing' is based on the statement of al-Karkhi, according to some scholars' derivation that it is permissible until the end of the praise; it is said until he bows, which is narrated from Muhammad; similarly in al-Mujtaba; it is said until he raises his head from bowing; it is said until the ta'awwudh. And in al-Bada'i: If he intends after saying 'Allah' before 'Akbar', it is not valid because commencement is a beginning. ... He said: 'Due to its absence in the books of the madhhab'. He said: 'They differed concerning intention: is it permissible to advance it before takbir or must it be simultaneous? Abu Hanifa and Ahmad said: It is permissible to advance intention for prayer after the entrance of time and before the takbir as long as it is not cut off by an action.'
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, addresses the ruling of intention (niyyah) in prayer. The author begins by stating that intention is a condition (shart) for prayer, based on consensus. He then critiques proofs from Quran and Hadith: the verse from Surah al-Bayyinah is interpreted as referring to tawhid, not specific acts; and the famous hadith 'إنما الأعمال بالنيات' is considered by Hanafi usul scholars as a hadith ahad with speculative meaning, thus indicating recommendation (sunnah) rather than obligation (fard). The author clarifies that only one intention is needed—the intention to pray with sincerity. Intention to face the qibla is not a condition. The key point is that there must be no 'alien separator' (fajin) between intention and takbir, defined as acts incompatible with prayer like eating, drinking, or speaking. Acts like walking or performing wudu do not break the continuity. Therefore, intention can precede takbir if no alien act intervenes. The author addresses the timing of intention: according to Imam Muhammad, it is permissible to advance intention in all acts of worship; Abu Yusuf only allows it in fasting. The cautious view is to intend simultaneously with takbir (Shafi'i position), but in the Hanafi school this is merely recommended, not required. The text defends the Hanafi position that advancing intention is valid, citing the general meaning of the hadith and the principle of avoiding hardship (haraj). Delayed intention is not allowed, contrary to al-Karkhi's analogy to fasting. The passage also discusses cases where intention is forgotten and later remembered. The reliance-upon view (mufta bihi) is that intention can be made before takbir as long as no foreign act intervenes.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): The intention to perform a specific act of worship (here prayer) for the sake of Allah alone.
الفاصل الأجنبي (al-fasil al-ajnabi): An alien separator between intention and takbir, i.e., an act inconsistent with the state of prayer, such as eating, drinking, or speaking.
المقارنة (al-muqaranah): Simultaneity of intention with the takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi view on the timing of intention (niyyah) for prayer?
A) Intention must be simultaneous with the takbir.
B) Intention can precede the takbir as long as no alien act intervenes.
C) Intention must be made after the takbir.
D) Intention is not required for prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that intention (niyyah) is a condition for prayer that can precede the opening takbir, provided no alien act intervenes; simultaneity is recommended but not required.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Taharri for Qibla and Its Analogous Rulings on Purity
Explaining rulings on taharri when uncertain of qibla and comparing with taharri for purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer based on taharri for qibla and explain how it differs from taharri for water and garment purity, including the intra-Hanafi dispute on vessels.

Core Idea
Prayer based on taharri remains valid even if wrong, but using impure water or garment requires repetition.

When you are uncertain about the direction of the qibla, Islamic law requires you to make your best effort (taharri) to determine it. This lesson explores the ruling that such a prayer is valid even if you later discover you were mistaken, and contrasts it with cases where you mistakenly use impure water or pray in a garment you thought was pure. The passage also discusses differences among later Hanafi scholars on what happens if your estimate changes during prayer, and the special rules for vessels with mixed pure and impure water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and basic rulings
First, identify the two main scenarios: praying after taharri for qibla, and performing wudu or praying with water/garment thought pure but later found impure. Note the initial ruling for each: the former is valid and not repeated; the latter requires repetition.
This distinction is the core legal point.
2
Analyze the qiyas (analogical reasoning)
The passage compares the two scenarios to highlight that the key difference is the presence of valid taharri. In the qibla case, the person performed a legitimate endeavor (taharri), whereas in the water/garment case, the person had no doubt and acted without such endeavor. Identify this as the illa (effective cause) that justifies the different ruling.
This qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) shows that the ruling depends on whether the person fulfilled their obligation to exert effort.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on changing direction
The passage reports that later scholars differed on whether a person who changes his taharri direction during prayer must repeat the prayer. Understand each view and the preferred (mufta bihi) position according to Ibn al-Humam.
This difference does not affect the core validity of the first prayer but addresses what to do if the estimate changes.
4
Apply the ruling to the vessels case
The passage extends taharri to cases where you have multiple vessels and do not know which is impure. Recognize the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether you must pour away all water before tayammum. Learn the reconciled view that the mufta bihi is the permissibility of tayammum without pouring.
This shows the school's concern for avoiding wasting water (istihsan).
5
Extract the legal principle
Synthesize the general principle: when a person performs taharri (ijtihad) to the best of their ability and acts accordingly, the act is valid even if later proven wrong. However, if the person had no genuine uncertainty and only assumed, the act must be repeated upon discovery of error.
This principle applies to qibla, and analogously to purity cases where taharri is possible (e.g., garments but not all vessels).

It is not from [؟] endeavor. In the Fatawa of al-‘Attabi: If he endeavored but his endeavor did not fall upon anything, it is said he delays, and it is said he prays to four directions, and it is said he has a choice. In al-Zahiriyya: If a man endeavored and the two states were equal to him and he was not certain of anything, but he prayed, then if it appears that he hit the qibla, it is valid; if it appears that he missed, likewise; and if nothing appeared to him, his prayer is valid. In al-Khulasa: From Muhammad: If he prayed four rak'as to four directions, it is valid. Then the later scholars differed regarding when his opinion changes to the first direction by endeavor: some said his prayer [is valid], and some said he begins anew. End. In al-Bughya: If he prayed to a direction by endeavor, then his opinion changed in the second rak'a to another direction, so he changed, and he remembered that he left a prostration from the first rak'a, his prayer is invalid. In al-Zahiriyya: Endeavor is permissible for the prostration of recitation as it is permissible for prayer. He said: from a doubter it is complete. His saying: And if he missed, he does not repeat because he performed the obligatory in his right, which is prayer to the direction of his endeavor, contrary to if he performed wudu with water or prayed in a garment thinking it pure, then it becomes clear it is impure, where he repeats the prayer because he performed wudu [with it]. That the belief of invalidity is not a valid legal proof, so it does not entail invalidity, because what has been presented is that the proof of invalidity is the endeavor or the belief arising from it, and without the considered proof, where does invalidity come from that he should be held accountable? So the appropriate in presenting the answer is what is in Sharh al-Munya by al-‘Allama al-Halabi, where he said: Contrary to the case of no endeavor, for he did not believe invalidity, but he is equal regarding validity and invalidity. So if his hitting [the qibla] appears after completion of the act, one of the two probabilities is removed and the other is established. It is only not permissible to build [on the first] if he knows the hitting before completion, due to what we said of the necessity of building the strong upon the weak, and not so after completion. End. And if he does not know the state neither in prayer nor after it, then the implication of what has passed is repetition, except if after finishing he knows that he hit, then repetition is obligatory. But what will come in explaining the case of one who prayed without doubt and without endeavor, in that he does not have to repeat if he was absent from that place and the situation is not clear, that the origin is validity and nothing removes it, one might think that this reasoning applies here and thus validity is required. And it is answered that the presence of doubt here contradicts that validity is the origin. His saying: (And it is said he has a choice) i.e., if he wishes he delays, and if he wishes he prays the prayer four times to four directions, and this is the most cautious. Thus in Sharh al-Munya. Ibn al-Humam mentioned in Zad al-Faqir the first opinion with certainty and referred to the two opinions after it as 'it is said'. It was mentioned at the end of al-Mustasfa that when three opinions are mentioned, the preponderant is the first or the last, not the middle. It is not clear what he chose in Sharh al-Munya. How could it be, when it involves praying to other than the qibla with certainty, which is prohibited, and facing the qibla is only obligatory when one is able, so it necessitates doing the prohibited for the sake of the commanded, and leaving the prohibited takes precedence over doing the commanded. And the apparent meaning of the last opinion is that he has a choice to pray to whichever direction he wishes, as indicated by what the author transmitted after from al-Zahiriyya, because its gist is that if he prayed to any direction he wished, his prayer is valid even if it appears that he missed, because he is no longer obligated to a specific direction since there is no preponderance in his view of one over another, and obedience is within capacity, and there is no negligence on his part. If it is said: he delays the prayer because his direction is the direction of his endeavor and it is not found, then there is a face; and if it is said he has a choice in direction because endeavor is only obligatory when possible, then there is a face; but that he prays to four directions has no apparent face, so ponder. His saying: (to four directions) i.e., from one who leaves what he is commanded, which is prayer in a pure garment and with purity, while he has performed what he is commanded, which is endeavor. In al-Kafi, there is indication of the permissibility of endeavor in vessels and garments, and there is a detail mentioned in al-Zahiriyya. He said: Endeavor is permitted in a single garment in case of necessity, and in two garments and multiple garments even if the impure is predominant. In two vessels, it is not permitted except in a transmission from Abu Yusuf. But if he performs wudu with both, one after the other, and prays, it is considered: if he performs wudu with the first and prays, it is valid because his wudu from the first is an endeavor that it is pure, just as if he said to his two wives, 'One of you is divorced,' then he had intercourse with one of them, the other is determined for divorce. If he performs wudu with the second and then prays, it is appropriate that his prayer should not be valid because he performed wudu with impure water. And if he did not have an event and did not pray after performing wudu with the first until he performed wudu with the second, the majority said: it is not valid because his limbs become impure. And some said: it is valid, and it is the correct opinion. Because endeavor is not permitted according to us due to prevalence of impurity or equality of pure and impure, he pours away all the water and performs tayammum and prays, or he mixes all the water until all the water becomes impure, then performs tayammum, to avoid wasting water. And if he does not pour it away, tayammum is permissible for him. They said: this is the saying of Abu Hanifa. And the two said: tayammum is not permissible for him except after pouring. And Ibn Ziyad said: he mixes them and then performs tayammum. And if there are three persons and three vessels, one of which is impure, and each one's endeavor falls on a vessel, their prayers are valid individually. And if one of them is the leftover of a donkey and the other is pure, he performs wudu with both, and not... end. He performs tayammum.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the ruling of taharri (personal estimation) when one is uncertain about the direction of qibla or the purity of water and garments. The author begins by citing various fatwa works on the matter. The core ruling is that if a person tries his best to determine the qibla but remains uncertain, he may pray to whichever direction he thinks most likely, and his prayer is valid even if it later turns out he was wrong, provided he did not know during the prayer. This is based on the principle that he has performed the obligation according to his capacity. The passage then compares this to cases of wudu with impure water or praying in an impure garment: in those cases, if he later discovers the impurity, he must repeat because his action was based on false certainty, not on a valid legal endeavor. The author goes into detail about differences among later scholars (mutakkhirin) regarding whether a person who changes his mind during prayer needs to repeat. Some say the first prayer is valid, others say he must start over. The relied-upon position (as per Ibn al-Humam) is that the prayer is valid and need not be repeated. The passage then discusses the permissibility of taharri for the prostration of recitation and the conditions for taharri in garments and vessels. For vessels, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa allows tayammum without pouring away the water, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require pouring it away. The correct opinion (al-sahih) according to later scholars is that tayammum is permissible without pouring if the water cannot be used due to impurity. The passage ends with a scenario of multiple persons and vessels.

Key Terms
تحري (taHarrī): Personal estimation or endeavor to determine the correct direction or legal status when certain knowledge is absent.
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Ka'ba in Makkah towards which Muslims pray.
اجتهاد (ijtihād): In this context, it means the effort to determine the qibla direction by personal reasoning, synonymous with taharri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person prays after performing taharri for qibla and later discovers he was wrong, what is the ruling?
A) He must repeat the prayer
B) His prayer is valid and he does not repeat
C) He must repeat only if he knew during the prayer
D) It depends on whether he was certain at the time

Key Takeaway
Prayer based on valid taharri for qibla is valid and need not be repeated if wrong, unlike cases of doubtful purity where repetition is required.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Taharri in Vessels and Tayammum without Pouring
Intra-Hanafi dispute on taharri and tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum when taharri is not possible in two vessels, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Ibn Ziyad.

Core Idea
When uncertainty prevents taharri, Abu Hanifa allows tayammum without pouring water to avoid waste.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about taharri (diligent estimation) when you have two vessels, one pure and one impure, and cannot determine which is which. The core question: must you pour out the water before performing tayammum, or can you go directly to tayammum? Abu Hanifa takes the latter view to prevent waste, while his two leading students require pouring. We will trace the reasoning, look at a qiyas analogy, and see which view is relied upon in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The passage deals with a person who has two vessels of water, one definitely impure, the other possibly pure. Taharri (estimation) is not possible because the probabilities are equal or the impure is predominant. What is the ruling?
2
State the Hanafi position of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa holds that tayammum is permissible without pouring out the water. The passage says: 'ولو لم يهرقها جاز له التيمم' (if he does not pour it out, tayammum is permissible for him). The reason is to avoid wasting water (احترازاً عن إضاعة الماء).
This is the mufta bihi position as per the text: 'وهو الصحيح'.
3
Contrast with the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) require pouring out the water before tayammum. The passage states: 'وقالا : لا يجوز تيممه إلا بعد الإراقة'.
Ibn Ziyad proposes a third view: mix the waters to make them all impure, then perform tayammum.
4
Analyze the qiyas analogy
The passage draws an analogy: if a man says to his two wives 'one of you is divorced', then has intercourse with one, his taharri specifies the other for divorce. Similarly, wudu from the first vessel is valid because taharri indicated it was pure.
This qiyas is used to validate the sequence of wudu from the first vessel.
5
Apply the ruling to a multi-person scenario
If three people each have a vessel (one impure unknown) and each performs taharri individually, their prayers are valid. This shows taharri is personal and each person's estimation is independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من ترك ما أمر به وهو الصلاة في ثوب طاهر وعلى طهارة وهو قد أتى بما أمر به وهو التحري، وفي الكافي ما يدل على جواز التحري في الأواني والثياب وفيه تفصيل مذكور في الظهيرية قال : ويجوز التحري في الثوب الواحد حالة الضرورة والثوبين والثياب وإن كان النجس غالباً، وفي الأنائين لا يجوز إلا رواية عن أبي يوسف لكنه إذا توضأ بهما واحداً بعد واحد وصلى ينظر، إن توضأ بالأول وصلى جاز لأن وضوءه من الأول تحر منه أنه طاهر كما لو قال لامرأتيه إحداكما طالق ثم وطىء إحداهما تعينت الأخرى للطلاق فلو توضأ بالثاني ثم صلى ينبغي أن لا تجوز صلاته لأنه توضأ بماء نجس، وإن لم يحدث ولم يصل بعدما توضأ الأول حتى توضأ بالثاني قال عامتهم : لا يجوز لأن أعضاءه صارت نجسة. وقال بعضهم : يجوز وهو الصحيح لأنه لما لم يجز التحري عندنا لغلبة النجاسة أو لاستواء الطاهر بالنجس يهريق المياه كلها ويتيمم ويصلي أو يخلط المياه كلها حتى تصير المياه كلها نجسة ثم يتيمم احترازاً عن إضاعة الماء، ولو لم يهرقها جاز له التيمم. قالوا هذا قول أبي حنيفة. وقالا : لا يجوز تيممه إلا بعد الإراقة. وقال ابن زياد يخلطها ثم يتيمم. وإن كان عند ثلاثة ثلاث أوان أحدها نجس ووقع تحري كل واحد منهم على إناء جازت صلاتهم فرادى، ولو كان أحدهما سؤر حمار والآخر طاهراً يتوضأ بهما ولا .. يتيمم
Whoever leaves what he was commanded, namely prayer in pure clothing and in a state of purity, while he has done what he was commanded, namely taharri (diligent estimation). And in al-Kafi there is evidence for the permissibility of taharri in vessels and clothes, and there is a detail mentioned in al-Zahiriyyah. He said: Taharri is permissible in a single cloth in a state of necessity, and in two cloths and multiple cloths even if the impure is predominant. In two vessels, it is not permissible except in a narration from Abu Yusuf, but if he performs wudu from both one after another and prays, then consideration: if he performs wudu from the first and prays, it is valid because his wudu from the first was by taharri that it is pure, just as if he said to his two wives 'One of you is divorced' then he had intercourse with one, the other is specified for divorce. If he performs wudu from the second then prays, it should be that his prayer is not valid because he performed wudu with impure water. And if he did not break wudu and did not pray after performing wudu from the first until he performed wudu from the second, the majority of them said: it is not valid because his limbs become impure. And some said: it is valid, and that is the correct view, because when taharri is not permissible according to us due to predominance of impurity or equality of pure and impure, he pours out all the water and performs tayammum and prays, or mixes all the water until all the water becomes impure then performs tayammum, to avoid wasting water. And if he does not pour it out, tayammum is permissible for him. They said this is the view of Abu Hanifa. And the two companions said: his tayammum is not permissible except after pouring out. And Ibn Ziyad said: he mixes them then performs tayammum. And if there are three people with three vessels, one of them impure, and each of them makes taharri on a vessel, their prayers individually are valid. And if one of them is the remains of a donkey and the other is pure, he performs wudu from both, and not... tayammum.
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling of taharri (diligent estimation) when there is uncertainty about the purity of water vessels or clothes. The core issue is whether one must pour out the water before performing tayammum. Abu Hanifa holds that if taharri is not possible due to equal probability or predominance of impurity, one may perform tayammum without pouring out the water, to avoid waste. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) require pouring out first. Ibn Ziyad proposes mixing the waters to make them all impure, then tayammum. The passage also discusses scenarios of multiple vessels and the effect of sequential wudu. The preferred view among later Hanafis is that of Abu Hanifa, as indicated by 'وهو الصحيح'.

Key Terms
تحري (taharri): Diligent estimation to determine the pure vessel or cloth when uncertainty exists about impurity.
نجس (najis): Legally impure substance that prevents validity of prayer if present on body, clothes, or place.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on tayammum when there are two vessels, one pure and one impure, and taharri is not possible?
A) Tayammum is not allowed until water is poured out, according to Abu Hanifa.
B) Tayammum is allowed without pouring water, according to Abu Hanifa.
C) One must mix the waters and then perform wudu, according to Ibn Ziyad.
D) One must pray without wudu, according to the Sahibayn.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when uncertainty prevents taharri between two waters, the relied-upon view permits tayammum without pouring out the water, prioritizing avoidance of waste.

The Sunan of Standing in Prayer and the Imam's Starting Time: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Lists sunan and resolves intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on imam's start

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunan acts at the start of prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding when the imam begins the prayer.

Core Idea
The imam starts at 'qad qamat al-salah' per Abu Hanifa; Abu Yusuf says after iqamah ends; both valid.

This lesson examines the recommended acts (sunan) at the beginning of prayer as enumerated in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, including suppressing yawns, removing hands from sleeves, and standing at 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. It then focuses on an intra-Hanafi dispute: when should the imam commence the prayer relative to the iqamah? Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the flexibility within the school.

Guided Path
1
List the sunan acts
Read the source passage and identify the five sunan acts: placing forehead, suppressing yawn, taking hands out of sleeves, suppressing cough, standing at 'hayya 'ala al-falah'.
Each act has its own evidence and wisdom.
2
Understand the evidence for each sunnah
For example, suppressing yawn is based on the hadith: 'Yawning in prayer is from the devil; when one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible.' Note that the command is interpreted as recommendation (sunnah) in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is ahad and zanni, thus yields sunnah not wajib.
3
Analyze the dispute on imam's start time
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: imam starts when mu'adhdhin says 'qad qamat al-salah'. Abu Yusuf: imam starts after iqamah finishes. Compare their proofs: trustworthiness of mu'adhdhin vs. preserving virtue of following the mu'adhdhin.
The source also mentions that responding to iqamah is recommended, so delaying is acceptable.
4
Evaluate the practical difference
If imam starts early, congregation may miss some sunnah of responding; if late, they may delay the prayer start. The thamarah al-khilaf is minor.
The text concludes 'no harm' in either view.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The text implies the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is stronger, but flexibility is allowed. The mufta bihi is the earlier opinion, but delaying is also acceptable.
Both positions are considered valid within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موضع سجوده وكظم فمه عند التثائب وإخراج كفيه من كميه عند التكبير ودفع السعال ما استطاع والقيام حين قيل حي على الفلاح وشروع الإمام مذ قيل قد قامت الصلاة . وهو فصل وإذا أراد الدخول في الصلاة كبر ورفع يديه حذاء أذنيه ولو شرع بالتسبيح أو (Y), أي إمساك فمه والمراد به سده لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام التثاؤب في الصلاة من الشيطان فإذا تثاءب أحدكم فليكظم ما استطاع (۲) وفي الظهيرية : فإن لم يقدر غطاه بيده أو كمه للحديث. قوله : (وإخراج كفيه من كميه عند التكبير لأنه أقرب إلى التواضع وأبعد من التشبه بالجبابرة وأمكن من نشر الأصابع إلا لضرورة برد ونحوه قوله: (ودفع السعال ما استطاع لأنه ليس من أفعال الصلاة ولهذا لو كان بغير عذر لا تفسد صلاته فيجتنبه ما أمكن. قوله : ( والقيام حين قيل حي على الفلاح لأنه أمر به فيستحب المسارعة إليه. أطلقه فشمل الإمام والمأموم إن كان الإمام بقرب المحراب وإلا فيقوم كل صف ينتهي إليه الإمام الأظهر، وإن دخل من قدام وقفوا حين يقع بصرهم عليه. وهذا كله إذا كان المؤذن غير الإمام، فإن كان واحداً وأقام في المسجد فالقوم لا يقومون حتى يفرغ من إقامته. كذا في الظهيرية. قوله : (وشروع الإمام مذ قيل قد قامت الصلاة عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف : يشرع إذا فرغ من الإقامة محافظة على فضيلة متابعة المؤذن وإعانة للمؤذن على الشروع معه. ولهما أن المؤذن أمين وقد أخبر بقيام الصلاة فيشرع عنده صوناً لكلامه عن الكذب، وفيه مسارعة إلى المناجاة وقد تابع المؤذن في الأكثر فيقوم مقام الكل على أنهم قالوا المتابعة في الأذان دون الإقامة. كذا ذكره الشارح وفيه نظر لما نقلناه في باب الأذان أن إجابة الإقامة مستحبة . وفي الظهيرية : ولو أخر حتى يفرغ المؤذن من الإقامة لا بأس به في قولهم جميعاً والله أعلم . فصل
He should place his forehead on the place of prostration, suppress his yawn by holding his mouth, bring out his hands from his sleeves during takbir, suppress coughing as much as possible, stand when 'hayya 'ala al-falah' is said, and the imam starts from when 'qad qamat al-salah' is said. And it is a section. When he intends to enter the prayer, he says takbir and raises his hands to the level of his ears, even if he starts with tasbih or (Y). That is, holding his mouth, meaning closing it, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Yawning in prayer is from the devil; when one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible.' In al-Zahiriyya: If he cannot, he covers it with his hand or sleeve due to the hadith. His statement: 'Bringing out his hands from his sleeves during takbir' because it is closer to humility and farther from resembling the arrogant, and more conducive to spreading the fingers except for necessity of cold etc. His statement: 'Suppressing coughing as much as possible' because it is not from the actions of prayer; for this reason, if it were without excuse, it would not invalidate his prayer, so he avoids it as much as possible. His statement: 'Standing when 'hayya 'ala al-falah' is said' because it is commanded, so it is recommended to hasten to it. He made it general, including the imam and the follower. If the imam is near the mihrab, otherwise each row stands when the imam reaches the apparent limit, and if he enters from the front, they stand when their sight falls on him. This is all if the mu'adhdhin is not the imam. If he is one and performs the iqamah in the mosque, the people do not stand until he finishes his iqamah. Thus in al-Zahiriyya. His statement: 'The start of the imam from when 'qad qamat al-salah' is said' according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He starts when he finishes the iqamah, to preserve the virtue of following the mu'adhdhin and to assist the mu'adhdhin in starting with him. Their proof is that the mu'adhdhin is trustworthy and has informed of the establishment of prayer, so he starts at that point to protect his words from falsehood, and it contains hastening to private conversation with Allah, and he has followed the mu'adhdhin in most, so it stands in place of all, and they said: Following is in the adhan, not the iqamah. Thus mentioned the commentator, but there is a consideration due to what we transmitted in the chapter of adhan that responding to the iqamah is recommended. In al-Zahiriyya: If he delays until the mu'adhdhin finishes the iqamah, there is no harm in it according to all of them. And Allah knows best. A section.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sunan acts at the beginning of prayer and specifically the timing of the imam starting the prayer. The text first lists several recommended acts: placing the forehead on the prostration spot, suppressing yawns, bringing hands out of sleeves during takbir, suppressing coughs, standing when the mu'adhdhin says 'hayya 'ala al-falah', and the imam starting when 'qad qamat al-salah' is said. The commentary then expands each point. The yawn suppression is based on a hadith; covering with hand or sleeve is an alternative. Bringing hands out of sleeves is for humility and avoiding arrogance. Suppressing cough is because it is not part of prayer, but it does not invalidate. Standing at 'hayya 'ala al-falah' is recommended, and the timing of standing for the congregation is detailed: if the imam is near the mihrab, they stand at 'qad qamat al-salah'; otherwise, each row stands when the imam reaches them. If the mu'adhdhin is also the imam, the people wait until he finishes the iqamah. The main dispute is on the imam's start: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say he starts when 'qad qamat al-salah' is said, because the mu'adhdhin is trustworthy and starting immediately protects his statement from falsehood. Abu Yusuf says he starts after the iqamah is finished, to maintain the virtue of following the mu'adhdhin. The commentator notes that responding to iqamah is recommended, so delaying is also acceptable. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated, but the text inclines toward the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad by stating their proof first. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah as it appears in al-Zahiriyya.

Key Terms
كظم (kazm): Suppressing or holding back yawn by closing the mouth.
التثائب (al-tathā'ub): Yawning.
قد قامت الصلاة (qad qāmat al-ṣalāh): The phrase in iqamah announcing the prayer is established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is forbidden.
B) It is better but not required.
C) There is no harm in it according to all (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Abu Yusuf).
D) It is only allowed if the mu'adhdhin is also the imam.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides flexibility: the imam may start at 'qad qamat al-salah' or after the full iqamah, both being valid practices supported by evidence.

Ruling for Unintentional Hadath and Its Proof from Hadith
Commentary defining hadath and establishing the ruling with prophetic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for unintentional hadath during prayer and explain how the hadith overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
Unintentional hadath does not invalidate prayer; the Prophet's hadith permits building after wudu.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains that while logical analogy would deem any hadath invalidating, the Hanafi school follows a specific prophetic hadith that allows continuation for unintentional occurrences. The key is distinguishing between deliberate and involuntary events.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of hadath
Recognize that hadath is a legal preventer (mani') that resides in the limbs until removed. It is a state of impurity that breaks wudu.
The passage notes hadath is a 'man'iyyah shar'iyyah'.
2
Identify the ruling for unintentional hadath
The matn states: 'Whoever is overtaken by an event during prayer, let him perform wudu and build.' This is the ruling: perform wudu and continue the prayer from where you left off.
The term 'sabaqa' indicates the hadath is unintentional.
3
Recognize that qiyas would require invalidity
By analogy to intentional hadath and actions like walking/turning, unintentional hadath would also invalidate prayer because it contradicts the state of purity required for prayer.
Qiyas with intentional hadath is rejected due to textual proof.
4
Examine the prophetic hadith as the proof
The passage cites the hadith: 'Whoever vomits, or has a nosebleed, or experiences madhi, should leave, perform wudu, and build upon his prayer as long as he has not spoken.' The imperative verbs indicate obligation (wujub).
The hadith is mursal but accepted by Hanafis and most scholars.
5
See how the hadith overrides qiyas
Because the hadith is explicit and authentic, it takes precedence over qiyas. The Hanafi school abandons qiyas on the basis of this nass.
The concession applies only to unintentional events, not deliberate ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقدمه على ما يفسدها، وقدمنا أن الحدث مانعية شرعية قائمة بالأعضاء إلى غاية استعمال المزيل. قوله : (ومن سبقه حدث توضأ وبنى والقياس فسادها لأن الحدث ينافيها والمشي والانحراف يفسدانها فأشبه الحدث العمد ولنا قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «من قاء أو رعف أو أمذى فلينصرف وليتوضأ وليبن على صلاته ما لم يتكلم» ولا نزاع في صحته مرسلاً وهو حجة عندنا وعند أكثر أهل العلم ومذهبنا ثابت عن جماعة من الصحابة وكفى بهم قدوة فوجب ترك القياس به والبلوى فيما يسبق دون ما يتعمده فلا يلحق به.
Then he gave precedence to [explaining] what nullifies it, and we have already stated that hadath is a legally established preventer residing in the limbs until the use of the remover. His statement: (Whoever is overtaken by an event during prayer, let him perform wudu and build upon his prayer. Qiyas would necessitate its invalidity because hadath contradicts it, and walking and turning away nullify it, so unintentional hadath resembles intentional hadath. But we have the statement of the Prophet ﷺ: 'Whoever vomits, or has a nosebleed, or experiences madhi, should leave, perform wudu, and build upon his prayer as long as he has not spoken.' There is no dispute regarding its authenticity as a mursal hadith, and it is a proof for us and for most scholars. Our madhhab is established from a group of Companions, and they suffice as role models. Therefore, qiyas must be abandoned on account of it. The [case of] affliction concerns what overtakes [unintentionally], not what one does deliberately, so the latter is not analogous.
Source pages p. 643

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq comments on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq. It first defines hadath as a legal preventer (man'iyyah shar'iyyah) that resides in the limbs until removed by water (or tayammum). The matn ruling states that one who experiences an unintentional hadath (e.g., nosebleed, vomiting, madhi) must perform wudu and continue (build upon) the prayer. The commentator notes that qiyas would suggest invalidity since hadath contradicts prayer, just like intentional hadath or actions like walking. However, the Hanafi school relies on the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ, which explicitly permits building for such unintentional events. The hadith is mursal, but accepted by the Hanafis and most scholars. Moreover, the practice of several Companions supports it. Therefore, qiyas is set aside (tark al-qiyas). The key distinction is that this concession applies only to involuntary (sabaqa) events, not deliberate ones.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): A legally established preventer (man'iyyah) that resides in the limbs and removes the state of purity until removed by water or tayammum.
سبقه (sabaqahu): To overtake unintentionally, without the person's choice or control.
بنى (banaa): To resume and continue the prayer from the point of interruption without starting anew.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a person who experiences an unintentional nosebleed during prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be restarted from the beginning.
B) The person must perform wudu and continue from where he left off, provided he has not spoken.
C) The prayer is valid but requires sajdah al-sahw.
D) The person must perform ghusl and start over.

Key Takeaway
Unintentional hadath during prayer does not invalidate it; the Hanafi school permits building upon the prayer after wudu, based on a prophetic hadith that overrides the general qiyas.
